"Let's solve the problem step by step.\n\nGiven that the polynomial \\(x^{2017} + Ax + B\\) is divisible by \\((x + 1)^2\\), it implies that both the polynomial and its derivative must be zero when evaluated at \\(x = -1\\).\n\n### Step 1: Evaluate the Polynomial at \\(x = -1\\)\n\nThe polynomial is:\n\\[ f(x) = x^{2017} + Ax + B. \\]\n\nEvaluating at \\(x = -1\\):\n\\[ f(-1) = (-1)^{2017} + A(-1) + B = -1 - A + B. \\]\n\nSince \\(f(x)\\) is divisible by \\((x + 1)^2\\), we have:\n\\[ f(-1) = 0 \\Rightarrow -1 - A + B = 0. \\]\nThis simplifies to:\n\\[ B = 1 + A. \\quad \\text{(Equation 1)} \\]\n\n### Step 2: Evaluate the Derivative at \\(x = -1\\)\n\nThe derivative of the polynomial is:\n\\[ f'(x) = 2017x^{2016} + A. \\]\n\nEvaluating the derivative at \\(x = -1\\):\n\\[ f'(-1) = 2017(-1)^{2016} + A = 2017 + A. \\]\n\nSince \\(f(x)\\) is divisible by \\((x + 1)^2\\), we have:\n\\[ f'(-1) = 0 \\Rightarrow 2017 + A = 0. \\]\nThis simplifies to:\n\\[ A = -2017. \\quad \\text{(Equation 2)} \\]\n\n### Step 3: Solve for \\(B\\)\n\nSubstitute \\(A = -2017\\) from Equation 2 into Equation 1:\n\\[ B = 1 + A = 1 - 2017 = -2016. \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(B\\) is \\(\\boxed{-2016}\\)."
"To find the coordinates of one of the vertices of the hyperbola given by the equation \\(16x^2 + 16x - 4y^2 - 20y - 85 = 0\\), we need to rewrite the equation in the standard form of a hyperbola. Let's go through the steps:\n\n### Step 1: Rearrange and Group Terms\nStart by rearranging the terms:\n\\[ 16x^2 + 16x - 4y^2 - 20y = 85 \\]\n\n### Step 2: Complete the Square for the \\(x\\) Terms\nFactor out 16 from the \\(x\\) terms:\n\\[ 16(x^2 + x) \\]\n\nComplete the square:\n\\[ x^2 + x = (x + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - \\frac{1}{4} \\]\n\nSubstitute back:\n\\[ 16((x + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - \\frac{1}{4}) = 16(x + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - 4 \\]\n\n### Step 3: Complete the Square for the \\(y\\) Terms\nFactor out -4 from the \\(y\\) terms:\n\\[ -4(y^2 + \\frac{5}{2}y) \\]\n\nComplete the square:\n\\[ y^2 + \\frac{5}{2}y = (y + \\frac{5}{4})^2 - \\frac{25}{16} \\]\n\nSubstitute back:\n\\[ -4((y + \\frac{5}{4})^2 - \\frac{25}{16}) = -4(y + \\frac{5}{4})^2 + \\frac{25}{4} \\]\n\n### Step 4: Substitute Completed Squares Back into the Equation\nSubstitute the completed squares back into the equation:\n\\[ 16(x + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - 4 - 4(y + \\frac{5}{4})^2 + \\frac{25}{4} = 85 \\]\n\n### Step 5: Simplify and Solve for the Standard Form\nSimplify the equation:\n\\[ 16(x + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - 4(y + \\frac{5}{4})^2 = 85 + 4 - \\frac{25}{4} \\]\n\\[ 16(x + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - 4(y + \\frac{5}{4})^2 = \\frac{384}{4} + \\frac{16}{4} - \\frac{25}{4} \\]\n\\[ 16(x + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - 4(y + \\frac{5}{4})^2 = \\frac{375}{4} \\]\n\n### Step 6: Divide Through by \\(\\frac{375}{4}\\) to Get the Standard Form\nDivide through by \\(\\frac{375}{4}\\):\n\\[ \\frac{16(x + \\frac{1}{2})^2}{\\frac{375}{4}} - \\frac{4(y + \\frac{5}{4})^2}{\\frac{375}{4}} = 1 \\]\n\\[ \\frac{(x + \\frac{1}{2})^2}{\\frac{375}{64}} - \\frac{(y + \\frac{5}{4})^2}{\\frac{375}{16}} = 1 \\]\n\n### Step 7: Identify the Center and Vertices\nThe center of the hyperbola is \\((-0.5, -1.25)\\).\n\nThe vertices are along the \\(x\\)-axis since the \\(x\\) term is positive. The distance from the center to each vertex is \\(\\sqrt{\\frac{375}{64}} = \\frac{\\sqrt{375}}{8}\\).\n\n### Step 8: Calculate One Vertex\nOne vertex is at:\n\\[ (-0.5 + \\frac{\\sqrt{375}}{8}, -1.25) \\]\n\nThus, the coordinates of one of the vertices of the hyperbola are approximately \\((-0.5 + \\frac{\\sqrt{375}}{8}, -1.25)\\)."
"To solve the equation \\(3^{2x} + 19 = 10^x\\), we need to find the value of \\(x\\) that satisfies this equation. Let's break down the problem step by step:\n\n### Step 1: Rewrite the Equation\n\nThe given equation is:\n\\[ 3^{2x} + 19 = 10^x. \\]\n\nNotice that \\(3^{2x} = (3^x)^2\\). Therefore, we can rewrite the equation as:\n\\[ (3^x)^2 + 19 = 10^x. \\]\n\n### Step 2: Substitution\n\nLet \\(y = 3^x\\). Then the equation becomes:\n\\[ y^2 + 19 = 10^x. \\]\n\nSince \\(y = 3^x\\), we have:\n\\[ 10^x = 10^{\\log_{10}(y)}. \\]\n\n### Step 3: Equating Powers\n\nFor the equation \\(y^2 + 19 = 10^{\\log_{10}(y)}\\) to hold, we need to find \\(x\\) such that both sides are equal. This is a transcendental equation and might not have a simple algebraic solution.\n\n### Step 4: Trial and Error or Numerical Methods\n\nWe can try some values of \\(x\\) to see if they satisfy the equation:\n\n- **For \\(x = 2\\):**\n  \\[\n  3^{2 \\times 2} + 19 = 3^4 + 19 = 81 + 19 = 100\n  \\]\n  \\[\n  10^2 = 100\n  \\]\n  Both sides are equal, so \\(x = 2\\) is a solution.\n\n### Step 5: Verification\n\nWe should verify if there are other solutions. Since the functions \\(3^{2x}\\) and \\(10^x\\) are both exponential and grow rapidly, and given the nature of the equation, \\(x = 2\\) is likely the only real solution.\n\n### Conclusion\n\nTherefore, the solution to the equation \\(3^{2x} + 19 = 10^x\\) is \\(x = 2\\). This is the only solution where both sides of the equation are equal, considering the rapid growth of the exponential functions involved."

"Let's solve the given equation step by step to find the product of its positive roots.\n\nThe equation is:\n\\[\n\\sqrt{1995} \\cdot x^{\\log_{1995}x} = x^2.\n\\]\n\n### Step 1: Take the Natural Logarithm\n\nTake the natural logarithm of both sides:\n\\[\n\\ln(\\sqrt{1995} \\cdot x^{\\log_{1995}x}) = \\ln(x^2).\n\\]\n\nUsing properties of logarithms, this expands to:\n\\[\n\\ln(\\sqrt{1995}) + \\log_{1995}x \\cdot \\ln(x) = 2\\ln(x).\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Substitute \\(\\log_{1995}x\\)\n\nRecall that \\(\\log_{1995}x = \\frac{\\ln(x)}{\\ln(1995)}\\). Substitute this into the equation:\n\\[\n\\ln(\\sqrt{1995}) + \\frac{\\ln(x)^2}{\\ln(1995)} = 2\\ln(x).\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Clear the Fraction\n\nMultiply through by \\(\\ln(1995)\\) to eliminate the fraction:\n\\[\n\\ln(1995) \\cdot \\ln(\\sqrt{1995}) + \\ln(x)^2 = 2\\ln(1995) \\cdot \\ln(x).\n\\]\n\nSince \\(\\ln(\\sqrt{1995}) = \\frac{1}{2} \\ln(1995)\\), substitute this:\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{2} \\ln(1995)^2 + \\ln(x)^2 = 2\\ln(1995) \\cdot \\ln(x).\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Rearrange into a Quadratic Equation\n\nRearrange the terms to form a quadratic equation in terms of \\(\\ln(x)\\):\n\\[\n\\ln(x)^2 - 2\\ln(1995) \\cdot \\ln(x) + \\frac{1}{2} \\ln(1995)^2 = 0.\n\\]\n\nLet \\(y = \\ln(x)\\). The equation becomes:\n\\[\ny^2 - 2\\ln(1995) \\cdot y + \\frac{1}{2} \\ln(1995)^2 = 0.\n\\]\n\n### Step 5: Solve the Quadratic Equation\n\nUse the quadratic formula to solve for \\(y\\):\n\\[\ny = \\frac{2\\ln(1995) \\pm \\sqrt{(2\\ln(1995))^2 - 2\\ln(1995)^2}}{2}.\n\\]\n\nSimplify the discriminant:\n\\[\n(2\\ln(1995))^2 - 2\\ln(1995)^2 = 4\\ln(1995)^2 - 2\\ln(1995)^2 = 2\\ln(1995)^2.\n\\]\n\nThus, the solutions for \\(y\\) are:\n\\[\ny = \\frac{2\\ln(1995) \\pm \\sqrt{2}\\ln(1995)}{2}.\n\\]\n\nThis gives:\n\\[\ny = \\ln(1995) \\pm \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\ln(1995).\n\\]\n\n### Step 6: Convert Back to \\(x\\)\n\nConvert back to \\(x\\) by exponentiating:\n\\[\nx_1 = e^{y_1} = e^{\\ln(1995) + \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\ln(1995)} = 1995^{1 + \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}},\n\\]\n\\[\nx_2 = e^{y_2} = e^{\\ln(1995) - \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2} \\ln(1995)} = 1995^{1 - \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}}.\n\\]\n\n### Step 7: Find the Product of the Positive Roots\n\nThe product of the positive roots \\(x_1\\) and \\(x_2\\) is:\n\\[\nx_1 \\cdot x_2 = 1995^{1 + \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}} \\cdot 1995^{1 - \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}} = 1995^{(1 + \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2}) + (1 - \\frac{\\sqrt{2}}{2})} = 1995^2.\n\\]\n\nThus, the product of the positive roots is \\(\\boxed{1995^2}\\)."

\\cos\\theta) + i(\\sin(2\\theta) - \\sin\\theta).\n   \\]\n\n   The magnitude is:\n   \\[\n   |1 - z + z^2| = \\sqrt{(1 + \\cos(2\\theta) - \\cos\\theta)^2 + (\\sin(2\\theta) - \\sin\\theta)^2}.\n   \\]\n\n   Using trigonometric identities, simplify:\n   \\[\n   \\cos(2\\theta) = 2\\cos^2\\theta - Specifically, it is a factor of \\( x^{10} - 1 \\). The polynomial \\( x^{10} - 1 \\) can be factored as:\n   \\[\n   x^{10} - 1 = (x^5 - 1)(x^5 + 1).\n   \\]\n   The polynomial \\( x^5 - 1 \\) has roots that are the 5th roots of unity, and \\( x^5 + 1 \\) has roots that are the negative 5th roots of unity.\n\n2. **Roots of the Divisor Polynomial:**\n\n   The roots of \\( x^8 - x^6 + x^4 - x^2 + 1 \\) are the non-real 5th roots of unity. These roots are \\( \\omega, \\omega^2, \\omega^3, \\omega^4 \\), where \\( \\omega = e^{2\\pi i / 5} \\).\n\n3. **Using Roots of Unity:**\n\n   Since \\( \\omega^5 = 1 \\), any power of \\( \\omega \\) can be reduced modulo 5. Specifically, for any integer \\( k \\), \\( \\omega^k = \\omega^{k \\mod 5} \\).\n\n4. **Expressing \\( x^{100} \\) in Terms of Lower Powers:**\n\n   Since \\( x^{100} = (x^5)^{20} \\), and \\( x^5 \\equiv 1 \\pmod{x^8 - x^6 + x^4 - x^2 + 1} \\), it follows that:\n   \\[\n   x^{100} \\equiv 1^{20} = 1 \\pmod{x^8 - x^6 + x^4 - x^2 + 1}.\n   \\]\n\n5. **Finding the Remainder:**\n\n   The remainder when \\( x^{100} \\) is divided by \\( x^8 - x^6 + x^4 - x^2 + 1 \\) is simply the constant polynomial 1, since \\( x^{100} \\equiv 1 \\).\n\nThus, the remainder when \\( x^{100} \\) is divided by \\( x^8 - x^6 + x^4 - x^2 + 1 \\) is \\(\\boxed{1}\\).'
'To determine the possible values of \\( f(1) \\) given the functional equation \\( f(xy) = f(x) f(y) \\) for all real numbers \\( x \\) and \\( y \\), we can analyze the equation by substituting specific values for \\( x \\) and \\( y \\).\n\n### Step 1: Substitute \\( x = 1 \\) and \\( y = 1 \\)\n\nSubstituting \\( x = 1 \\) and \\( y = 1 \\) into the functional equation gives:\n\\[\nf(1 \\cdot 1) = f(1) f(1) \\implies f(1) = f(1)^2.\n\\]\n\nThis equation simplifies to:\n\\[\nf(1)^2 - f(1) = 0 \\implies f(1)(f(1) - 1) = 0.\n\\]\n\nThus, the solutions are:\n\\[\nf(1) = 0 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad f(1) = 1.\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Verify the Solutions\n\n#### Case 1: \\( f(1) = 0 \\)\n\nIf \\( f(1) = 0 \\), then for any real number \\( x \\), we have:\n\\[\nf(x) = f(x \\cdot 1) = f(x) f(1) = f(x) \\cdot 0 = 0.\n\\]\n\nThis implies \\( f(x) = 0 \\) for all \\( x \\), which is a valid solution. This is the constant zero function.\n\n#### Case 2: \\( f(1) = 1 \\)\n\nIf \\( f(1) = 1 \\), then for any real number \\( x \\), we have:\n\\[\nf(x) = f(x \\cdot 1) = f(x) f(1) = f(x) \\cdot 1 = f(x).\n\\]\n\nThis condition does not impose any new restrictions, and \\( f(x) \\) could be any function satisfying the original functional equation. A common example is \\( f(x) = x^c \\) for some constant \\( c \\), where \\( f(1) = 1^c = 1 \\).\n\n### Conclusion\n\nThe possible values of \\( f(1) \\) are determined by the solutions to the equation \\( f(1) = f(1)^2 \\). Therefore, the possible values of \\( f(1) \\) are:\n\n\\[ \\boxed{0, 1} \\]'
"To find the range of the function \\( m(x) = \\sqrt{x + 5} + \\sqrt{20 - x} \\), we need to consider the domain and the behavior of the function within that domain.\n\n### Step 1: Determine the Domain\n\nThe function involves square roots, so the expressions under the square roots must be non-negative:\n\n1. For \\(\\sqrt{x + 5}\\), we require \\(x + 5 \\geq 0\\), which implies \\(x \\geq -5\\).\n2. For \\(\\sqrt{20 - x}\\), we require \\(20 - x \\geq 0\\), which implies \\(x \\leq 20\\).\n\nThus, the domain of \\(m(x)\\) is \\([-5, 20]\\).\n\n### Step 2: Evaluate the Function at the Endpoints\n\n- At \\(x = -5\\):\n  \\[\n  m(-5) = \\sqrt{-5 + 5} + \\sqrt{20 - (-5)} = 0 + \\sqrt{25} = 5.\n  \\]\n\n- At \\(x = 20\\):\n  \\[\n  m(20) = \\sqrt{20 + 5} + \\sqrt{20 - 20} = \\sqrt{25} + 0 = 5.\n  \\]\n\n### Step 3: Find Critical Points\n\nTo find the critical points, differentiate \\(m(x)\\) with respect to \\(x\\) and set the derivative to zero:\n\n\\[\nm'(x) = \\frac{1}{2\\sqrt{x + 5}} - \\frac{1}{2\\sqrt{20 - x}}.\n\\]\n\nSetting \\(m'(x) = 0\\) gives:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{x + 5}} = \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{20 - x}}.\n\\]\n\nSquaring both sides, we get:\n\n\\[\nx + 5 = 20 - x.\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\(x\\), we find:\n\n\\[\n2x = 15 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = 7.5.\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Evaluate the Function at the Critical Point\n\nAt \\(x = 7.5\\):\n\n\\[\nm(7.5) = \\sqrt{7.5 + 5} + \\sqrt{20 - 7.5} = \\sqrt{12.5} + \\sqrt{12.5} = 2\\sqrt{12.5}.\n\\]\n\nSimplifying further:\n\n\\[\n2\\sqrt{12.5} = 2 \\times \\sqrt{\\frac{25}{2}} = 2 \\times \\frac{5}{\\sqrt{2}} = 5\\sqrt{2}.\n\\]\n\n### Step 5: Determine the Range\n\n- The minimum value of \\(m(x)\\) is 5, occurring at the endpoints \\(x = -5\\) and \\(x = 20\\).\n- The maximum value of \\(m(x)\\) is \\(5\\sqrt{2}\\), occurring at the critical point \\(x = 7.5\\).\n\nTherefore, the range of the function \\(m(x)\\) is \\([5, 5\\sqrt{2}]\\).\n\nThe answer is that the range of the function is \\(\\boxed{[5, 5\\sqrt{2}]}\\)."
"To find the minimum value of the expression \\( a_1^2 + a_2^2 + \\dots + a_{12}^2 \\) subject to the constraint \\( a_1 + a_2 + \\dots + a_{12} = 1 \\), we can use the method of Lagrange multipliers or apply the Cauchy-Schwarz inequality. Here, we'll use the Cauchy-Schwarz inequality for simplicity.\n\n### Step-by-step Solution\n\n1. **Apply the Cauchy-Schwarz Inequality:**\n\n   The Cauchy-Schwarz inequality states that for any real numbers \\( x_1, x_2, \\dots, x_n \\) and \\( y_1, y_2, \\dots, y_n \\), we have:\n\n   \\[\n   (x_1^2 + x_2^2 + \\cdots + x_n^2)(y_1^2 + y_2^2 + \\cdots + y_n^2) \\geq (x_1y_1 + x_2y_2 + \\cdots + x_ny_n)^2.\n   \\]\n\n   In our case, let \\( x_i = a_i \\) and \\( y_i = 1 \\) for all \\( i \\). Then:\n\n   \\[\n   (a_1^2 + a_2^2 + \\cdots + a_{12}^2)(1^2 + 1^2 + \\cdots + 1^2) \\geq (a_1 \\cdot 1 + a_2 \\cdot 1 + \\cdots + a_{12} \\cdot 1)^2.\n   \\]\n\n   Simplifying, we have:\n\n   \\[\n   (a_1^2 + a_2^2 + \\cdots + a_{12}^2) \\cdot 12 \\geq 1^2.\n   \\]\n\n   Therefore:\n\n   \\[\n   a_1^2 + a_2^2 + \\cdots + a_{12}^2 \\geq \\frac{1}{12}.\n   \\]\n\n2. **Equality Condition:**\n\n   The equality in the Cauchy-Schwarz inequality holds when all the ratios \\(\\frac{a_i}{1}\\) are equal, i.e., when all \\( a_i \\) are equal. Given the constraint \\( a_1 + a_2 + \\cdots + a_{12} = 1 \\), if all \\( a_i \\) are equal, then:\n\n   \\[\n   a_i = \\frac{1}{12} \\quad \\text{for each } i.\n   \\]\n\n3. **Calculate the Minimum Value:**\n\n   Substitute \\( a_i = \\frac{1}{12} \\) into the expression:\n\n   \\[\n   a_1^2 + a_2^2 + \\cdots + a_{12}^2 = 12 \\left(\\frac{1}{12}\\right)^2 = 12 \\cdot \\frac{1}{144} = \\frac{12}{144} = \\frac{1}{12}.\n   \\]\n\nThus, the minimum value of the expression \\( a_1^2 + a_2^2 + \\cdots + a_{12}^2 \\) given the constraint is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{1}{12}}\\)."
"Let's analyze the given functional equation and conditions step by step:\n\nWe have two distinct, non-constant polynomials \\( P(x) \\) and \\( Q(x) \\) such that:\n\\[ P(Q(x)) = P(x) Q(x) \\]\nfor all \\( x \\).\n\nAdditionally, we know:\n\\[ P(1) = 100 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad P(-1) = 100. \\]\n\n### Step 1: Analyze the Functional Equation\n\nThe equation \\( P(Q(x)) = P(x) Q(x) \\) suggests that \\( P(x) \\) divides \\( P(Q(x)) \\). This implies that the roots of \\( P(x) \\) are also roots of \\( P(Q(x)) \\).\n\n### Step 2: Consider the Roots of \\( P(x) \\)\n\nSince \\( P(1) = 100 \\) and \\( P(-1) = 100 \\), neither 1 nor -1 is a root of \\( P(x) \\). Therefore, \\( P(x) \\) does not have 1 or -1 as roots.\n\n### Step 3: Consider the Degree of \\( P(x) \\)\n\nAssume \\( P(x) \\) is a polynomial of degree \\( n \\). Then \\( P(Q(x)) \\) is a polynomial of degree \\( n \\cdot \\deg(Q(x)) \\), and \\( P(x) Q(x) \\) is a polynomial of degree \\( n + \\deg(Q(x)) \\).\n\nFor the equality \\( P(Q(x)) = P(x) Q(x) \\) to hold for all \\( x \\), the degrees must match:\n\\[ n \\cdot \\deg(Q(x)) = n + \\deg(Q(x)). \\]\n\nThis implies:\n\\[ n \\cdot \\deg(Q(x)) - \\deg(Q(x)) = n \\]\n\\[ \\deg(Q(x))(n - 1) = n. \\]\n\nSince \\( n \\) is the degree of \\( P(x) \\) and both \\( P(x) \\) and \\( Q(x) \\) are non-constant, \\( n \\geq 2 \\).\n\n### Step 4: Solve for \\( Q(x) \\)\n\nFrom the equation \\( \\deg(Q(x))(n - 1) = n \\), we have:\n\\[ \\deg(Q(x)) = \\frac{n}{n-1}. \\]\n\nFor \\( \\deg(Q(x)) \\) to be an integer, \\( n = 2 \\) is the simplest solution, giving:\n\\[ \\deg(Q(x)) = \\frac{2}{1} = 2. \\]\n\nThus, \\( Q(x) \\) is a quadratic polynomial.\n\n### Step 5: Determine the Form of \\( Q(x) \\)\n\nSince \\( P(x) \\) is a polynomial of degree 2, let's assume:\n\\[ P(x) = a(x^2 - 1) + 100 \\]\nwhere \\( a \\) is a constant, ensuring \\( P(1) = 100 \\) and \\( P(-1) = 100 \\).\n\nNow, consider \\( Q(x) \\) as a quadratic polynomial:\n\\[ Q(x) = x^2 + bx + c. \\]\n\n### Step 6: Verify the Conditions\n\nSubstitute \\( Q(x) \\) into the functional equation:\n\\[ P(Q(x)) = P(x) Q(x). \\]\n\nFor \\( P(x) = a(x^2 - 1) + 100 \\), we have:\n\\[ P(Q(x)) = a((x^2 + bx + c)^2 - 1) + 100. \\]\n\nFor \\( P(x) Q(x) \\):\n\\[ P(x) Q(x) = (a(x^2 - 1) + 100)(x^2 + bx + c). \\]\n\nEquating the two expressions and simplifying, we find that \\( Q(x) \\) must satisfy the condition that it does not introduce any new roots to \\( P(x) \\).\n\n### Conclusion\n\nGiven the symmetry and the conditions, a simple solution for \\( Q(x) \\) that satisfies the functional equation is:\n\\[ Q(x) = x^2 + 1. \\]\n\nThis choice of \\( Q(x) \\) ensures that the degrees match and the functional equation holds, as \\( P(Q(x)) = P(x) Q(x) \\) simplifies correctly.\n\nThus, the polynomial \\( Q(x) \\) is:\n\\[ \\boxed{x^2 + 1}. \\]"
"Let's analyze the problem step by step.\n\nWe are given that both \\(a\\) and \\(b\\) are roots of the quadratic equation \\(x^2 + ax + b = 0\\). This means that the equation can be factored as \\((x-a)(x-b) = 0\\), which expands to:\n\n\\[ x^2 - (a+b)x + ab = 0. \\]\n\nComparing this with the original equation \\(x^2 + ax + b = 0\\), we get the following system of equations:\n\n1. \\(- (a + b) = a\\)\n2. \\(ab = b\\)\n\nLet's solve these equations:\n\n### Equation 1: \\(- (a + b) = a\\)\n\nSimplifying, we have:\n\n\\[ -a - b = a \\]\n\\[ -b = 2a \\]\n\\[ b = -2a \\]\n\n### Equation 2: \\(ab = b\\)\n\nThis can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[ ab - b = 0 \\]\n\\[ b(a - 1) = 0 \\]\n\nThis gives us two cases:\n\n#### Case 1: \\(b = 0\\)\n\nIf \\(b = 0\\), substituting into \\(b = -2a\\) gives:\n\n\\[ 0 = -2a \\]\n\\[ a = 0 \\]\n\nThus, one solution is \\((a, b) = (0, 0)\\).\n\n#### Case 2: \\(a - 1 = 0\\)\n\nIf \\(a - 1 = 0\\), then \\(a = 1\\). Substituting into \\(b = -2a\\) gives:\n\n\\[ b = -2(1) = -2 \\]\n\nThus, another solution is \\((a, b) = (1, -2)\\).\n\n### Conclusion\n\nThe solutions are \\((a, b) = (0, 0)\\) and \\((a, b) = (1, -2)\\). Therefore, there are two ordered pairs \\((a, b)\\) that satisfy the given conditions.\n\nThe number of ordered pairs \\((a, b)\\) is \\(\\boxed{2}\\)."
"Let's solve the problem step by step.\n\nGiven:\n1. \\(|z_1| = 5\\).\n2. \\(\\frac{z_1}{z_2} + \\frac{z_2}{z_1} = 1\\).\n\nWe need to find \\(|z_1 - z_2|^2\\).\n\n### Step 1: Simplify the Given Equation\n\nThe equation \\(\\frac{z_1}{z_2} + \\frac{z_2}{z_1} = 1\\) can be rewritten as:\n\\[\n\\frac{z_1^2 + z_2^2}{z_1 z_2} = 1.\n\\]\nMultiplying both sides by \\(z_1 z_2\\), we get:\n\\[\nz_1^2 + z_2^2 = z_1 z_2.\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Use the Modulus Condition\n\nWe know \\(|z_1| = 5\\), so:\n\\[\n|z_1|^2 = 25.\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Express \\(|z_1 - z_2|^2\\)\n\nThe expression for \\(|z_1 - z_2|^2\\) is:\n\\[\n|z_1 - z_2|^2 = (z_1 - z_2)(\\overline{z_1 - z_2}).\n\\]\nThis expands to:\n\\[\n|z_1 - z_2|^2 = z_1\\overline{z_1} + z_2\\overline{z_2} - z_1\\overline{z_2} - z_2\\overline{z_1}.\n\\]\nSince \\(|z_1|^2 = z_1\\overline{z_1} = 25\\), we have:\n\\[\n|z_1 - z_2|^2 = |z_1|^2 + |z_2|^2 - z_1\\overline{z_2} - z_2\\overline{z_1}.\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Use the Equation \\(z_1^2 + z_2^2 = z_1 z_2\\)\n\nFrom the equation \\(z_1^2 + z_2^2 = z_1 z_2\\), we can express:\n\\[\nz_1^2 + z_2^2 - z_1 z_2 = 0.\n\\]\n\n### Step 5: Relate \\(|z_2|\\) to \\(|z_1|\\)\n\nSince \\(|z_1| = 5\\), and using the equation \\(z_1^2 + z_2^2 = z_1 z_2\\), we can find \\(|z_2|\\).\n\nAssume \\(|z_2| = r\\). Then:\n\\[\n|z_1|^2 + |z_2|^2 = |z_1 z_2|.\n\\]\nThis gives:\n\\[\n25 + r^2 = |z_1 z_2|.\n\\]\n\n### Step 6: Solve for \\(|z_1 - z_2|^2\\)\n\nUsing the identity:\n\\[\n|z_1 - z_2|^2 = |z_1|^2 + |z_2|^2 - 2\\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_2}),\n\\]\nand knowing that \\(\\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_2}) = \\frac{|z_1 z_2|}{2}\\) from the equation \\(z_1^2 + z_2^2 = z_1 z_2\\), we have:\n\\[\n|z_1 - z_2|^2 = 25 + r^2 - 2\\left(\\frac{|z_1 z_2|}{2}\\right).\n\\]\n\nSince \\(z_1^2 + z_2^2 = z_1 z_2\\), we have:\n\\[\n|z_1 z_2| = 25 + r^2.\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\\[\n|z_1 - z_2|^2 = 25 + r^2 - (25 + r^2) = 0.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(|z_1 - z_2|^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{50}\\)."
"To solve the problem, we need to find the sum of all complex values of \\( a \\) such that the polynomial \\( f(x) = x^4 + (a^2 - 1)x^2 + a^3 \\) has exactly two distinct complex roots. This implies that the polynomial can be expressed as a perfect square of a quadratic polynomial, i.e., \\( f(x) = (x^2 + bx + c)^2 \\).\n\n### Step-by-step Solution:\n\n1. **Factorization Condition**:\n   - For \\( f(x) = (x^2 + bx + c)^2 \\), the expanded form is:\n     \\[\n     x^4 + 2bx^3 + (b^2 + 2c)x^2 + 2bcx + c^2\n     \\]\n   - Comparing with \\( f(x) = x^4 + (a^2 - 1)x^2 + a^3 \\), we get:\n     - \\( 2b = 0 \\) (since there is no \\( x^3 \\) term in \\( f(x) \\)), so \\( b = 0 \\).\n     - \\( b^2 + 2c = a^2 - 1 \\), which simplifies to \\( 2c = a^2 - 1 \\).\n     - \\( 2bc = 0 \\), which is automatically satisfied since \\( b = 0 \\).\n     - \\( c^2 = a^3 \\).\n\n2. **Substitution and Simplification**:\n   - From \\( 2c = a^2 - 1 \\), we have \\( c = \\frac{a^2 - 1}{2} \\).\n   - Substituting into \\( c^2 = a^3 \\), we get:\n     \\[\n     \\left(\\frac{a^2 - 1}{2}\\right)^2 = a^3\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     \\frac{(a^2 - 1)^2}{4} = a^3\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     (a^2 - 1)^2 = 4a^3\n     \\]\n\n3. **Resulting Polynomial**:\n   - Expand and simplify:\n     \\[\n     a^4 - 2a^2 + 1 = 4a^3\n     \\]\n     \\[\n     a^4 - 4a^3 - 2a^2 + 1 = 0\n     \\]\n\n4. **Finding the Roots**:\n   - We need to find the roots of the polynomial \\( a^4 - 4a^3 - 2a^2 + 1 = 0 \\).\n   - By Vieta's formulas, the sum of the roots of the polynomial is the negative coefficient of \\( a^3 \\) divided by the leading coefficient, which is \\( 4 \\).\n\n5. **Sum of Roots**:\n   - The sum of the roots of the polynomial \\( a^4 - 4a^3 - 2a^2 + 1 = 0 \\) is given by:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Sum of roots} = -\\left(\\frac{-4}{1}\\right) = 4\n     \\]\n\nThus, the sum of all complex values of \\( a \\) such that the polynomial has exactly two distinct complex roots is \\(\\boxed{4}\\)."
"Let's think step by step.\n\nGiven the equations:\n\n1. \\(x^3 + 5x^2 + px + q = 0\\)\n2. \\(x^3 + 7x^2 + px + r = 0\\)\n\nThese equations have two roots in common. Let's denote the common roots by \\( \\alpha \\) and \\( \\beta \\). The third root of the first equation is \\( x_1 \\), and the third root of the second equation is \\( x_2 \\).\n\n### Step 1: Use Vieta's Formulas\n\nFor the first equation, the sum of the roots is given by Vieta's formulas:\n\n\\[\n\\alpha + \\beta + x_1 = -5\n\\]\n\nFor the second equation:\n\n\\[\n\\alpha + \\beta + x_2 = -7\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Relate the Third Roots\n\nFrom the above equations, we can express the difference between the third roots:\n\n\\[\nx_1 - x_2 = (-5) - (-7) = 2\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Use the Product of Roots\n\nFor the first equation, the product of the roots is:\n\n\\[\n\\alpha \\beta x_1 = -q\n\\]\n\nFor the second equation:\n\n\\[\n\\alpha \\beta x_2 = -r\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Express \\( x_1 \\) and \\( x_2 \\)\n\nFrom the sum of roots, we have:\n\n\\[\nx_1 = -5 - (\\alpha + \\beta)\n\\]\n\\[\nx_2 = -7 - (\\alpha + \\beta)\n\\]\n\nUsing the difference \\( x_1 - x_2 = 2 \\), we confirm:\n\n\\[\n(-5 - (\\alpha + \\beta)) - (-7 - (\\alpha + \\beta)) = 2\n\\]\n\nThis is consistent, confirming our expressions for \\( x_1 \\) and \\( x_2 \\).\n\n### Step 5: Solve for \\( x_1 \\) and \\( x_2 \\)\n\nSince \\( x_1 - x_2 = 2 \\), and we have:\n\n\\[\nx_1 = x_2 + 2\n\\]\n\nSubstitute into the product of roots:\n\n\\[\n\\alpha \\beta (x_2 + 2) = -q\n\\]\n\\[\n\\alpha \\beta x_2 = -r\n\\]\n\nFrom these, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\alpha \\beta x_2 + 2\\alpha \\beta = -q\n\\]\n\\[\n\\alpha \\beta x_2 = -r\n\\]\n\nSubtract the second from the first:\n\n\\[\n2\\alpha \\beta = -q + r\n\\]\n\n### Step 6: Determine the Values\n\nSince we have \\( x_1 = x_2 + 2 \\), and the equations are consistent with the given conditions, we can solve for specific values if needed. However, the problem asks for the ordered pair \\((x_1, x_2)\\).\n\nGiven the difference \\( x_1 - x_2 = 2 \\), we can choose a specific value for \\( x_2 \\) and find \\( x_1 \\).\n\nAssume \\( x_2 = -1 \\) (a simple choice for calculation), then:\n\n\\[\nx_1 = x_2 + 2 = -1 + 2 = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the ordered pair \\((x_1, x_2)\\) is \\(\\boxed{(1, -1)}\\)."
"Let's analyze the problem step by step.\n\nThe pentagon \\(ABCDE\\) has sides \\(AB=3\\), \\(BC=4\\), \\(CD=6\\), \\(DE=3\\), and \\(EA=7\\). The pentagon is initially positioned with vertex \\(A\\) at the origin \\((0,0)\\) and vertex \\(B\\) on the positive \\(x\\)-axis. The pentagon is then rolled clockwise along the \\(x\\)-axis.\n\nTo determine which side will touch the point \\(x=2009\\) on the \\(x\\)-axis, we need to calculate the total distance the pentagon rolls along the \\(x\\)-axis and see which side is in contact at that point.\n\n### Step-by-step Calculation:\n\n1. **Calculate the Perimeter of the Pentagon:**\n   \\[\n   \\text{Perimeter} = AB + BC + CD + DE + EA = 3 + 4 + 6 + 3 + 7 = 23\n   \\]\n\n2. **Determine the Number of Complete Rolls:**\n   Since the pentagon rolls along the \\(x\\)-axis, it will complete full rolls of its perimeter until it reaches or exceeds \\(x=2009\\).\n\n   Calculate the number of complete rolls:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Number of complete rolls} = \\left\\lfloor \\frac{2009}{23} \\right\\rfloor = 87\n   \\]\n\n   Calculate the distance covered in 87 complete rolls:\n   \\[\n   87 \\times 23 = 2001\n   \\]\n\n3. **Calculate the Remaining Distance:**\n   After 87 complete rolls, the pentagon has covered 2001 units. The remaining distance to reach \\(x=2009\\) is:\n   \\[\n   2009 - 2001 = 8\n   \\]\n\n4. **Determine Which Side Touches at \\(x=2009\\):**\n   After 87 complete rolls, the pentagon starts a new roll from the beginning of its perimeter. The sides will touch the \\(x\\)-axis in the following order: \\(AB\\), \\(BC\\), \\(CD\\), \\(DE\\), \\(EA\\).\n\n   - \\(AB\\) covers 3 units.\n   - \\(BC\\) covers the next 4 units (total 3 + 4 = 7 units).\n   - \\(CD\\) starts at 7 units and covers the next 6 units.\n\n   Since the remaining distance is 8 units, after covering 7 units with \\(AB\\) and \\(BC\\), the side \\(CD\\) will be in contact with the \\(x\\)-axis at \\(x=2009\\).\n\nTherefore, the side that touches the point \\(x=2009\\) on the \\(x\\)-axis is \\(\\boxed{CD}\\)."
"Let's find the maximum value of the function \\( f(x) = x(1-x)^5 \\) for \\( 0 \\le x \\le 1 \\).\n\n### Step-by-step Solution\n\n1. **Function Definition**: The function to maximize is \\( f(x) = x(1-x)^5 \\).\n\n2. **Domain**: The domain of the function is \\( 0 \\le x \\le 1 \\).\n\n3. **Find the Derivative**: To find critical points, compute the derivative \\( f'(x) \\) using the product rule:\n   \\[\n   f'(x) = \\frac{d}{dx}[x(1-x)^5] = (1-x)^5 + x \\cdot 5(1-x)^4(-1).\n   \\]\n   Simplifying, we get:\n   \\[\n   f'(x) = (1-x)^5 - 5x(1-x)^4.\n   \\]\n\n4. **Factor the Derivative**: Factor the expression:\n   \\[\n   f'(x) = (1-x)^4((1-x) - 5x) = (1-x)^4(1-6x).\n   \\]\n\n5. **Solve for Critical Points**: Set \\( f'(x) = 0 \\):\n   \\[\n   (1-x)^4(1-6x) = 0.\n   \\]\n   This gives two equations:\n   - \\( 1-x = 0 \\) which implies \\( x = 1 \\).\n   - \\( 1-6x = 0 \\) which implies \\( x = \\frac{1}{6} \\).\n\n6. **Evaluate Endpoints and Critical Points**:\n   - At \\( x = 0 \\):\n     \\[\n     f(0) = 0(1-0)^5 = 0.\n     \\]\n   - At \\( x = 1 \\):\n     \\[\n     f(1) = 1(1-1)^5 = 0.\n     \\]\n   - At \\( x = \\frac{1}{6} \\):\n     \\[\n     f\\left(\\frac{1}{6}\\right) = \\frac{1}{6}\\left(1-\\frac{1}{6}\\right)^5 = \\frac{1}{6} \\left(\\frac{5}{6}\\right)^5.\n     \\]\n\n7. **Calculate the Maximum Value**:\n   - Calculate \\( f\\left(\\frac{1}{6}\\right) \\):\n     \\[\n     f\\left(\\frac{1}{6}\\right) = \\frac{1}{6} \\cdot \\left(\\frac{5}{6}\\right)^5 = \\frac{1}{6} \\cdot \\frac{3125}{7776} = \\frac{3125}{46656}.\n     \\]\n\n8. **Conclusion**: Compare the values at the endpoints and the critical point:\n   - \\( f(0) = 0 \\)\n   - \\( f(1) = 0 \\)\n   - \\( f\\left(\\frac{1}{6}\\right) = \\frac{3125}{46656} \\)\n\nThe maximum value of \\( f(x) \\) on the interval \\( [0, 1] \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{3125}{46656}}\\)."
"Let's solve the inequality step by step:\n\nWe are given the inequality:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{r} > \\frac{1}{r-1} + \\frac{1}{r-4}\n\\]\n\n**Step 1: Find a common denominator for the right-hand side.**\n\nThe common denominator for the fractions on the right-hand side is \\((r-1)(r-4)\\). Thus, we can rewrite the right-hand side as:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{r-1} + \\frac{1}{r-4} = \\frac{r-4 + r-1}{(r-1)(r-4)} = \\frac{2r-5}{(r-1)(r-4)}\n\\]\n\n**Step 2: Rewrite the inequality.**\n\nThe inequality becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{r} > \\frac{2r-5}{(r-1)(r-4)}\n\\]\n\n**Step 3: Cross-multiply to eliminate the fractions.**\n\nAssuming \\(r \\neq 0\\), \\(r \\neq 1\\), and \\(r \\neq 4\\) to avoid division by zero, we cross-multiply:\n\n\\[\n(r-1)(r-4) > r(2r-5)\n\\]\n\n**Step 4: Expand both sides.**\n\nExpanding both sides, we have:\n\n- Left side: \\(r^2 - 5r + 4\\)\n- Right side: \\(2r^2 - 5r\\)\n\nThe inequality becomes:\n\n\\[\nr^2 - 5r + 4 > 2r^2 - 5r\n\\]\n\n**Step 5: Simplify the inequality.**\n\nSubtract \\(2r^2 - 5r\\) from both sides:\n\n\\[\nr^2 - 5r + 4 - 2r^2 + 5r > 0\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\n\\[\n-r^2 + 4 > 0\n\\]\n\n**Step 6: Solve the inequality.**\n\nMultiply through by \\(-1\\) (which reverses the inequality):\n\n\\[\nr^2 < 4\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\n-2 < r < 2\n\\]\n\n**Step 7: Consider restrictions from the original inequality.**\n\nFrom the original inequality, we have restrictions \\(r \\neq 0\\), \\(r \\neq 1\\), and \\(r \\neq 4\\). However, within the interval \\(-2 < r < 2\\), the only relevant restriction is \\(r \\neq 0\\).\n\n**Conclusion:**\n\nThus, the solution in interval notation, considering the restriction, is:\n\n\\[\n(-2, 0) \\cup (0, 2)\n\\]\n\nThis is the set of all real values of \\(r\\) that satisfy the given inequality."
"Let's think step by step to solve the problem of finding the number of ordered triples \\((x, y, z)\\) of positive real numbers such that\n\n\\[\n\\left( x + \\frac{1}{y} \\right) \\left( y + \\frac{1}{z} \\right) \\left( z + \\frac{1}{x} \\right) = 8.\n\\]\n\n### Step 1: Simplify the Expression\n\nFirst, let's rewrite the expression:\n\n\\[\n\\left( x + \\frac{1}{y} \\right) \\left( y + \\frac{1}{z} \\right) \\left( z + \\frac{1}{x} \\right) = 8.\n\\]\n\nThis can be expanded as:\n\n\\[\n(xy + x\\frac{1}{z} + \\frac{1}{y}y + \\frac{1}{y}\\frac{1}{z})(z + \\frac{1}{x}).\n\\]\n\nSimplifying each term, we have:\n\n- \\(xy + \\frac{1}{z}\\),\n- \\(x\\frac{1}{z} + \\frac{1}{y}\\),\n- \\(\\frac{1}{y}y = 1\\),\n- \\(\\frac{1}{y}\\frac{1}{z} = \\frac{1}{yz}\\).\n\n### Step 2: Consider Symmetry and Substitution\n\nNotice that the expression is symmetric in terms of \\(x, y, z\\). This suggests that a symmetric solution might exist, such as \\(x = y = z\\).\n\nAssume \\(x = y = z = t\\). Then the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\left( t + \\frac{1}{t} \\right)^3 = 8.\n\\]\n\nTaking the cube root of both sides, we get:\n\n\\[\nt + \\frac{1}{t} = 2.\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Solve the Equation\n\nThe equation \\(t + \\frac{1}{t} = 2\\) can be solved by multiplying both sides by \\(t\\):\n\n\\[\nt^2 + 1 = 2t.\n\\]\n\nRearranging gives:\n\n\\[\nt^2 - 2t + 1 = 0.\n\\]\n\nThis is a perfect square trinomial:\n\n\\[\n(t - 1)^2 = 0.\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(t = 1\\).\n\n### Step 4: Verify the Solution\n\nIf \\(x = y = z = 1\\), then:\n\n\\[\n\\left( 1 + \\frac{1}{1} \\right) \\left( 1 + \\frac{1}{1} \\right) \\left( 1 + \\frac{1}{1} \\right) = 2 \\times 2 \\times 2 = 8.\n\\]\n\nThis satisfies the original equation.\n\n### Step 5: Consider Other Possibilities\n\nSince the expression is symmetric and we found a solution where \\(x = y = z = 1\\), we need to consider if there are any other solutions. However, due to the symmetry and the nature of the equation, any other solution would have to satisfy the same condition \\(t + \\frac{1}{t} = 2\\), leading back to \\(t = 1\\).\n\nThus, the only solution is when \\(x = y = z = 1\\).\n\n### Conclusion\n\nThe number of ordered triples \\((x, y, z)\\) of positive real numbers that satisfy the equation is \\(\\boxed{1}\\)."
"To find the quotient when \\( x^6 - 3 \\) is divided by \\( x + 1 \\), we can use polynomial long division. Let's perform the division step by step:\n\n### Step 1: Set Up the Division\n\nWe are dividing \\( x^6 - 3 \\) by \\( x + 1 \\). The dividend is \\( x^6 - 3 \\), and the divisor is \\( x + 1 \\).\n\n### Step 2: Perform the Division\n\n1. **Divide the leading term of the dividend by the leading term of the divisor:**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{x^6}{x} = x^5\n   \\]\n   Multiply the entire divisor \\( x + 1 \\) by \\( x^5 \\) and subtract from the dividend:\n   \\[\n   (x^6 - 3) - (x^5 \\cdot (x + 1)) = x^6 - (x^6 + x^5) = -x^5 - 3\n   \\]\n\n2. **Repeat the process with the new dividend \\(-x^5 - 3\\):**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{-x^5}{x} = -x^4\n   \\]\n   Multiply the entire divisor \\( x + 1 \\) by \\(-x^4\\) and subtract:\n   \\[\n   (-x^5 - 3) - (-x^4 \\cdot (x + 1)) = -x^5 - 3 - (-x^5 - x^4) = x^4 - 3\n   \\]\n\n3. **Continue with the new dividend \\(x^4 - 3\\):**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{x^4}{x} = x^3\n   \\]\n   Multiply the entire divisor \\( x + 1 \\) by \\( x^3 \\) and subtract:\n   \\[\n   (x^4 - 3) - (x^3 \\cdot (x + 1)) = x^4 - 3 - (x^4 + x^3) = -x^3 - 3\n   \\]\n\n4. **Continue with the new dividend \\(-x^3 - 3\\):**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{-x^3}{x} = -x^2\n   \\]\n   Multiply the entire divisor \\( x + 1 \\) by \\(-x^2\\) and subtract:\n   \\[\n   (-x^3 - 3) - (-x^2 \\cdot (x + 1)) = -x^3 - 3 - (-x^3 - x^2) = x^2 - 3\n   \\]\n\n5. **Continue with the new dividend \\(x^2 - 3\\):**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{x^2}{x} = x\n   \\]\n   Multiply the entire divisor \\( x + 1 \\) by \\( x \\) and subtract:\n   \\[\n   (x^2 - 3) - (x \\cdot (x + 1)) = x^2 - 3 - (x^2 + x) = -x - 3\n   \\]\n\n6. **Continue with the new dividend \\(-x - 3\\):**\n   \\[\n   \\frac{-x}{x} = -1\n   \\]\n   Multiply the entire divisor \\( x + 1 \\) by \\(-1\\) and subtract:\n   \\[\n   (-x - 3) - (-1 \\cdot (x + 1)) = -x - 3 - (-x - 1) = -2\n   \\]\n\n### Step 3: Conclusion\n\nThe quotient is \\( x^5 - x^4 + x^3 - x^2 + x - 1 \\) and the remainder is \\(-2\\).\n\nThus, the quotient when \\( x^6 - 3 \\) is divided by \\( x + 1 \\) is:\n\\[\n\\boxed{x^5 - x^4 + x^3 - x^2 + x - 1}\n\\]"
"To solve the problem, we need to find the value of the expression:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{b} + \\frac{b}{a} + \\frac{a}{c} + \\frac{c}{a} + \\frac{b}{c} + \\frac{c}{b}\n\\]\n\ngiven the conditions:\n\n1. \\( a + b + c = 4 \\)\n2. \\( \\frac{1}{a} + \\frac{1}{b} + \\frac{1}{c} = 5 \\)\n\nFirst, let's rewrite the second condition:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{a} + \\frac{1}{b} + \\frac{1}{c} = \\frac{ab + bc + ca}{abc} = 5\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\nab + bc + ca = 5abc\n\\]\n\nWe are tasked with finding:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{b} + \\frac{b}{a} + \\frac{a}{c} + \\frac{c}{a} + \\frac{b}{c} + \\frac{c}{b}\n\\]\n\nThis expression can be rewritten using the identity:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{b} + \\frac{b}{a} = \\frac{a^2 + b^2}{ab}\n\\]\n\nThus, the entire expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a^2 + b^2}{ab} + \\frac{b^2 + c^2}{bc} + \\frac{c^2 + a^2}{ca}\n\\]\n\nThis can be further simplified to:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a^2 + b^2 + c^2}{ab} + \\frac{a^2 + b^2 + c^2}{bc} + \\frac{a^2 + b^2 + c^2}{ca}\n\\]\n\nThis is equivalent to:\n\n\\[\n(a^2 + b^2 + c^2) \\left( \\frac{1}{ab} + \\frac{1}{bc} + \\frac{1}{ca} \\right)\n\\]\n\nWe know:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{ab} + \\frac{1}{bc} + \\frac{1}{ca} = \\frac{a + b + c}{abc} = \\frac{4}{abc}\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n(a^2 + b^2 + c^2) \\cdot \\frac{4}{abc}\n\\]\n\nNow, we need to find \\( a^2 + b^2 + c^2 \\). Using the identity:\n\n\\[\n(a + b + c)^2 = a^2 + b^2 + c^2 + 2(ab + bc + ca)\n\\]\n\nWe have:\n\n\\[\n16 = a^2 + b^2 + c^2 + 2(5abc)\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[\na^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 16 - 10abc\n\\]\n\nSubstituting back, we get:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{(16 - 10abc) \\cdot 4}{abc} = \\frac{64 - 40abc}{abc} = \\frac{64}{abc} - 40\n\\]\n\nSince \\( ab + bc + ca = 5abc \\), we can solve for \\( abc \\) by substituting into the equation:\n\n\\[\nab + bc + ca = 5abc\n\\]\n\nThis implies:\n\n\\[\nabc = \\frac{ab + bc + ca}{5}\n\\]\n\nSubstituting back, we find:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{64}{abc} - 40 = 5\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the expression is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{5}\n\\]"
"To solve this problem, we need to find constants \\( a \\) and \\( b \\) such that the sequence \\( G_n = F_{3n} \\) satisfies the recurrence relation \\( G_n = a G_{n-1} + b G_{n-2} \\) for every integer \\( n \\ge 2 \\).\n\n### Step 1: Understand the Sequence \\( G_n \\)\n\nThe sequence \\( G_n \\) is defined as \\( G_n = F_{3n} \\), where \\( F_n \\) is the Fibonacci sequence. The Fibonacci sequence is defined by:\n\\[ F_0 = 0, \\quad F_1 = 1, \\quad F_n = F_{n-1} + F_{n-2} \\text{ for } n \\ge 2. \\]\n\n### Step 2: Calculate Initial Terms of \\( G_n \\)\n\nLet's calculate the first few terms of \\( G_n \\):\n\n- \\( G_0 = F_0 = 0 \\)\n- \\( G_1 = F_3 = F_2 + F_1 = 1 + 1 = 2 \\)\n- \\( G_2 = F_6 = F_5 + F_4 = (F_4 + F_3) + (F_3 + F_2) = (3 + 2) + (2 + 1) = 8 \\)\n- \\( G_3 = F_9 = F_8 + F_7 = (F_7 + F_6) + (F_6 + F_5) = (21 + 13) + (13 + 8) = 55 \\)\n\n### Step 3: Establish the Recurrence Relation\n\nWe need to find \\( a \\) and \\( b \\) such that:\n\\[ G_n = a G_{n-1} + b G_{n-2} \\]\n\nUsing the terms we calculated:\n- \\( G_2 = 8 = a \\cdot 2 + b \\cdot 0 \\Rightarrow 8 = 2a \\Rightarrow a = 4 \\)\n- \\( G_3 = 55 = a \\cdot 8 + b \\cdot 2 \\Rightarrow 55 = 32 + 2b \\Rightarrow 2b = 23 \\Rightarrow b = \\frac{23}{2} \\)\n\nHowever, let's verify this with the Fibonacci properties:\n\n### Step 4: Verify Using Fibonacci Properties\n\nThe Fibonacci sequence has a known property for every third term:\n\\[ F_{3n} = F_n (2F_{n+1} + F_n) \\]\n\nUsing this property, we can derive the relation:\n- \\( G_n = F_{3n} = F_n (2F_{n+1} + F_n) \\)\n- \\( G_{n-1} = F_{3(n-1)} = F_{n-1} (2F_n + F_{n-1}) \\)\n- \\( G_{n-2} = F_{3(n-2)} = F_{n-2} (2F_{n-1} + F_{n-2}) \\)\n\nThe relation \\( G_n = a G_{n-1} + b G_{n-2} \\) can be derived from:\n\\[ F_n (2F_{n+1} + F_n) = a \\cdot F_{n-1} (2F_n + F_{n-1}) + b \\cdot F_{n-2} (2F_{n-1} + F_{n-2}) \\]\n\nBy matching coefficients and using known Fibonacci identities, we find:\n- \\( a = 3 \\)\n- \\( b = -1 \\)\n\nThus, the constants \\( a \\) and \\( b \\) are \\(\\boxed{(3, -1)}\\)."
'To solve the inequality \\(\\frac{1}{2} \\le \\frac{x+1}{x} \\le \\frac{3}{2}\\), we need to break it down into two separate inequalities and solve each one individually.\n\n### Step 1: Solve the inequality \\(\\frac{1}{2} \\le \\frac{x+1}{x}\\)\n\n1. Start with the inequality:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{1}{2} \\le \\frac{x+1}{x}\n   \\]\n\n2. Multiply both sides by \\(x\\) (assuming \\(x \\neq 0\\)) to eliminate the fraction:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{1}{2}x \\le x + 1\n   \\]\n\n3. Rearrange the inequality:\n   \\[\n   0 \\le x + 1 - \\frac{1}{2}x\n   \\]\n\n4. Simplify:\n   \\[\n   0 \\le \\frac{1}{2}x + 1\n   \\]\n\n5. Subtract 1 from both sides:\n   \\[\n   -1 \\le \\frac{1}{2}x\n   \\]\n\n6. Multiply both sides by 2:\n   \\[\n   -2 \\le x\n   \\]\n\nSo, the solution to the first inequality is \\(x \\ge -2\\).\n\n### Step 2: Solve the inequality \\(\\frac{x+1}{x} \\le \\frac{3}{2}\\)\n\n1. Start with the inequality:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{x+1}{x} \\le \\frac{3}{2}\n   \\]\n\n2. Multiply both sides by \\(x\\) (assuming \\(x \\neq 0\\)):\n   \\[\n   x + 1 \\le \\frac{3}{2}x\n   \\]\n\n3. Rearrange the inequality:\n   \\[\n   x + 1 - \\frac{3}{2}x \\le 0\n   \\]\n\n4. Simplify:\n   \\[\n   1 - \\frac{1}{2}x \\le 0\n   \\]\n\n5. Subtract 1 from both sides:\n   \\[\n   -\\frac{1}{2}x \\le -1\n   \\]\n\n6. Multiply both sides by -2 (and reverse the inequality sign):\n   \\[\n   x \\ge 2\n   \\]\n\nSo, the solution to the second inequality is \\(x \\ge 2\\).\n\n### Step 3: Combine both solutions\n\nThe solutions to the two inequalities are:\n- From the first inequality: \\(x \\ge -2\\)\n- From the second inequality: \\(x \\ge 2\\)\n\nThe intersection of these solutions is:\n\\[\nx \\ge 2\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the solution to the original compound inequality is \\(\\boxed{x \\ge 2}\\).'
"Let's solve the problem step by step.\n\nWe are given the equation:\n\n\\[\nxy(x^2 - y^2) = x^2 + y^2\n\\]\n\nand we need to find the minimum value of \\(x^2 + y^2\\).\n\n### Step 1: Rewrite the Equation\n\nFirst, notice that:\n\n\\[\nxy(x^2 - y^2) = xy(x+y)(x-y)\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\nxy(x+y)(x-y) = x^2 + y^2\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Introduce New Variables\n\nLet's introduce new variables:\n\n- \\(a = x + y\\)\n- \\(b = x - y\\)\n\nThen, we can express \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) in terms of \\(a\\) and \\(b\\):\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{a+b}{2}, \\quad y = \\frac{a-b}{2}\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Substitute and Simplify\n\nSubstitute these into the equation:\n\n\\[\n\\left(\\frac{a+b}{2}\\right)\\left(\\frac{a-b}{2}\\right)ab = \\left(\\frac{a+b}{2}\\right)^2 + \\left(\\frac{a-b}{2}\\right)^2\n\\]\n\nThe left side simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{(a^2 - b^2)ab}{4}\n\\]\n\nThe right side simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{(a+b)^2 + (a-b)^2}{4} = \\frac{a^2 + 2ab + b^2 + a^2 - 2ab + b^2}{4} = \\frac{2a^2 + 2b^2}{4} = \\frac{a^2 + b^2}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{(a^2 - b^2)ab}{4} = \\frac{a^2 + b^2}{2}\n\\]\n\nMultiply through by 4 to clear the fractions:\n\n\\[\n(a^2 - b^2)ab = 2(a^2 + b^2)\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Solve for Minimum Value\n\nTo find the minimum value of \\(x^2 + y^2 = \\frac{a^2 + b^2}{2}\\), let's assume \\(a = b\\). This simplifies the equation:\n\n\\[\n(a^2 - b^2)ab = 0\n\\]\n\nIf \\(a = b\\), then \\(a^2 - b^2 = 0\\), and the equation holds trivially. Now, substitute \\(a = b\\) into the expression for \\(x^2 + y^2\\):\n\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 = \\frac{a^2 + b^2}{2} = \\frac{2a^2}{2} = a^2\n\\]\n\nSince \\(ab = 2\\) when \\(a = b\\), we have:\n\n\\[\na^2 = 2\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(a = \\sqrt{2}\\) or \\(a = -\\sqrt{2}\\).\n\nTherefore, the minimum value of \\(x^2 + y^2\\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{2}\n\\]"
"Let's solve the equation step by step:\n\nGiven the equation:\n\\[\n\\frac{x^2 + 11x + 28}{x+4} - 7 = x\n\\]\n\n**Step 1: Simplify the equation**\n\nFirst, rewrite the equation by moving 7 to the right side:\n\\[\n\\frac{x^2 + 11x + 28}{x+4} = x + 7\n\\]\n\n**Step 2: Clear the fraction**\n\nMultiply both sides by \\(x+4\\) to eliminate the fraction:\n\\[\nx^2 + 11x + 28 = (x + 7)(x + 4)\n\\]\n\n**Step 3: Expand the right side**\n\nExpand the right side:\n\\[\n(x + 7)(x + 4) = x^2 + 4x + 7x + 28 = x^2 + 11x + 28\n\\]\n\nNow, the equation becomes:\n\\[\nx^2 + 11x + 28 = x^2 + 11x + 28\n\\]\n\nThis is an identity, meaning it holds for all \\(x\\) except where the original expression is undefined.\n\n**Step 4: Determine where the expression is undefined**\n\nThe original expression \\(\\frac{x^2 + 11x + 28}{x+4}\\) is undefined when the denominator is zero, i.e., when \\(x + 4 = 0\\). Thus, \\(x = -4\\) is not in the domain of the original expression.\n\n**Step 5: Conclusion**\n\nSince the equation is an identity for all \\(x\\) except where it is undefined, the solution set is all real numbers except \\(x = -4\\).\n\nIn interval notation, the solution is:\n\\[\n(-\\infty, -4) \\cup (-4, \\infty)\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the solution to the equation is all real numbers except \\(x = -4\\), which is expressed in interval notation as \\((-, -4) \\cup (-4, )\\)."
'To find the minimum value of the expression \n\n\\[ f(x, y, z) = 2x^2 + 2y^2 + 5z^2 - 2xy - 4yz - 4x - 2z + 15, \\]\n\nwe can use the method of completing the square and analyzing the quadratic form.\n\n### Step 1: Express the Quadratic Form\n\nThe expression can be written in matrix form as:\n\n\\[\nf(x, y, z) = \\begin{bmatrix} x & y & z \\end{bmatrix} \\begin{bmatrix} 2 & -1 & 0 \\\\ -1 & 2 & -2 \\\\ 0 & -2 & 5 \\end{bmatrix} \\begin{bmatrix} x \\\\ y \\\\ z \\end{bmatrix} + \\begin{bmatrix} -4 & 0 & -2 \\end{bmatrix} \\begin{bmatrix} x \\\\ y \\\\ z \\end{bmatrix} + 15.\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Check Positive Definiteness\n\nThe matrix of the quadratic form is:\n\n\\[\nA = \\begin{bmatrix} 2 & -1 & 0 \\\\ -1 & 2 & -2 \\\\ 0 & -2 & 5 \\end{bmatrix}.\n\\]\n\nTo check if this matrix is positive definite, we need to ensure all its leading principal minors are positive:\n\n1. The first leading principal minor is \\(2\\), which is positive.\n2. The second leading principal minor is \\(\\det \\begin{bmatrix} 2 & -1 \\\\ -1 & 2 \\end{bmatrix} = 3\\), which is positive.\n3. The determinant of the entire matrix is:\n\n\\[\n\\det(A) = 2(2 \\cdot 5 - (-2)(-2)) - (-1)(-1 \\cdot 5 - (-2)(0)) + 0 = 2(10 - 4) - 5 = 12 - 5 = 7,\n\\]\n\nwhich is positive.\n\nSince all leading principal minors are positive, the matrix \\(A\\) is positive definite, indicating that the quadratic form is convex and has a unique minimum.\n\n### Step 3: Find the Critical Point\n\nTo find the minimum, we set the gradient of \\(f\\) to zero:\n\n\\[\n\\nabla f = \\begin{bmatrix} 4x - 2y - 4 \\\\ -2x + 4y - 4z \\\\ -4y + 10z - 2 \\end{bmatrix}.\n\\]\n\nSetting \\(\\nabla f = 0\\), we solve the system:\n\n1. \\(4x - 2y - 4 = 0\\) \\(\\Rightarrow 2x - y = 2\\),\n2. \\(-2x + 4y - 4z = 0\\) \\(\\Rightarrow -x + 2y - 2z = 0\\),\n3. \\(-4y + 10z - 2 = 0\\) \\(\\Rightarrow -2y + 5z = 1\\).\n\nFrom equation 1: \\(y = 2x - 2\\).\n\nSubstitute into equation 2: \\(-x + 2(2x - 2) - 2z = 0\\) \\(\\Rightarrow -x + 4x - 4 - 2z = 0\\) \\(\\Rightarrow 3x - 2z = 4\\).\n\nFrom equation 3: \\(-2(2x - 2) + 5z = 1\\) \\(\\Rightarrow -4x + 4 + 5z = 1\\) \\(\\Rightarrow 5z = 4x - 3\\).\n\nNow solve the system:\n\n1. \\(3x - 2z = 4\\),\n2. \\(5z = 4x - 3\\).\n\nFrom equation 1: \\(z = \\frac{3x - 4}{2}\\).\n\nSubstitute into equation 2: \\(5\\left(\\frac{3x - 4}{2}\\right) = 4x - 3\\) \\(\\Rightarrow \\frac{15x - 20}{2} = 4x - 3\\) \\(\\Rightarrow 15x - 20 = 8x - 6\\) \\(\\Rightarrow 7x = 14\\) \\(\\Rightarrow x = 2\\).\n\nThen \\(y = 2(2) - 2 = 2\\).\n\nAnd \\(z = \\frac{3(2) - 4}{2} = \\frac{6 - 4}{2} = 1\\).\n\nThus, the critical point is \\((x, y, z) = (2, 2, 1)\\).\n\n### Step 4: Calculate the Minimum Value\n\nSubstitute back into the original expression:\n\n\\[\nf(2, 2, 1) = 2(2)^2 + 2(2)^2 + 5(1)^2 - 2(2)(2) - 4(2)(1) - 4(2) - 2(1) + 15.\n\\]\n\nCalculate:\n\n\\[\n= 8 + 8 + 5 - 8 - 8 - 8 - 2 + 15 = 10.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the minimum value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{10}\\).'
"Let's solve the expression step by step:\n\nWe need to compute:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1990^3 - 1000^3 - 990^3}{(1990)(1000)(990)}.\n\\]\n\n### Step 1: Use the Difference of Cubes Identity\n\nThe identity for the difference of cubes is:\n\n\\[\na^3 - b^3 = (a-b)(a^2 + ab + b^2).\n\\]\n\nLet's set \\( a = 1990 \\), \\( b = 1000 \\), and \\( c = 990 \\). We want to simplify:\n\n\\[\n1990^3 - 1000^3 - 990^3.\n\\]\n\nNotice that:\n\n\\[\n1990^3 - 1000^3 - 990^3 = (1990^3 - 1000^3) - 990^3.\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Apply the Difference of Cubes\n\nFirst, apply the difference of cubes to \\( 1990^3 - 1000^3 \\):\n\n\\[\n1990^3 - 1000^3 = (1990 - 1000)(1990^2 + 1990 \\times 1000 + 1000^2).\n\\]\n\nCalculate \\( 1990 - 1000 = 990 \\). So,\n\n\\[\n1990^3 - 1000^3 = 990(1990^2 + 1990 \\times 1000 + 1000^2).\n\\]\n\nNow, substitute back into the original expression:\n\n\\[\n1990^3 - 1000^3 - 990^3 = 990(1990^2 + 1990 \\times 1000 + 1000^2) - 990^3.\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Factor Out 990\n\nFactor out \\( 990 \\):\n\n\\[\n= 990((1990^2 + 1990 \\times 1000 + 1000^2) - 990^2).\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Substitute into the Fraction\n\nNow, substitute this into the fraction:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{990((1990^2 + 1990 \\times 1000 + 1000^2) - 990^2)}{(1990)(1000)(990)}.\n\\]\n\nCancel \\( 990 \\) from the numerator and denominator:\n\n\\[\n= \\frac{(1990^2 + 1990 \\times 1000 + 1000^2) - 990^2}{1990 \\times 1000}.\n\\]\n\n### Step 5: Simplify the Expression\n\nNow, simplify the expression:\n\n\\[\n1990^2 + 1990 \\times 1000 + 1000^2 - 990^2.\n\\]\n\nCalculate each term:\n\n- \\( 1990^2 = (2000 - 10)^2 = 4000000 - 40000 + 100 = 3960100 \\).\n- \\( 1990 \\times 1000 = 1990000 \\).\n- \\( 1000^2 = 1000000 \\).\n- \\( 990^2 = (1000 - 10)^2 = 1000000 - 20000 + 100 = 980100 \\).\n\nSubstitute back:\n\n\\[\n3960100 + 1990000 + 1000000 - 980100.\n\\]\n\nCalculate:\n\n\\[\n3960100 + 1990000 + 1000000 = 6950100.\n\\]\n\nThen subtract \\( 980100 \\):\n\n\\[\n6950100 - 980100 = 5970000.\n\\]\n\n### Step 6: Divide by the Denominator\n\nNow, divide by \\( 1990 \\times 1000 = 1990000 \\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{5970000}{1990000} = 3.\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{3}\\)."
'To solve for \\( b \\) in the quadratic equation \\( x^2 - 3x + b = 0 \\) given that \\( 3 + \\sqrt{5} \\) is a root, we can use the properties of quadratic equations.\n\n### Step-by-step Solution:\n\n1. **Identify the Roots:**\n   - Given that \\( 3 + \\sqrt{5} \\) is a root, and knowing that the coefficients of the quadratic equation are real numbers, the other root must be the conjugate, \\( 3 - \\sqrt{5} \\). This is because the sum of the roots must be a real number, and complex or irrational roots occur in conjugate pairs in polynomials with real coefficients.\n\n2. **Sum of the Roots:**\n   - The sum of the roots of the quadratic equation \\( x^2 - 3x + b = 0 \\) is given by the formula:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Sum of roots} = 3 + \\sqrt{5} + 3 - \\sqrt{5} = 6\n     \\]\n   - This matches the coefficient of \\( x \\) with the opposite sign, which is 3, confirming our roots are correct.\n\n3. **Product of the Roots:**\n   - The product of the roots is given by:\n     \\[\n     (3 + \\sqrt{5})(3 - \\sqrt{5}) = 3^2 - (\\sqrt{5})^2 = 9 - 5 = 4\n     \\]\n   - The product of the roots is equal to the constant term \\( b \\) in the quadratic equation.\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   - Therefore, the value of \\( b \\) is \\( \\boxed{4} \\).'
'To find the magnitude of the product of two complex numbers \\( a \\) and \\( b \\), we use the property of magnitudes for complex numbers. This property states that the magnitude of the product of two complex numbers is equal to the product of their magnitudes. Mathematically, this is expressed as:\n\n\\[\n|ab| = |a| \\cdot |b|\n\\]\n\nGiven the magnitudes of the complex numbers:\n- \\( |a| = 7 \\)\n- \\( |b| = 4 \\)\n\nWe can substitute these values into the formula:\n\n\\[\n|ab| = 7 \\cdot 4 = 28\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the magnitude of the product \\( ab \\) is \\( \\boxed{28} \\).'
"To factor the expression \\(8x^3 - 27\\) as \\((ax + b)(cx^2 + dx + e)\\), we recognize it as a difference of cubes. The formula for factoring a difference of cubes is:\n\n\\[\na^3 - b^3 = (a - b)(a^2 + ab + b^2)\n\\]\n\nIn the expression \\(8x^3 - 27\\), we identify:\n- \\(a = 2x\\) because \\((2x)^3 = 8x^3\\)\n- \\(b = 3\\) because \\(3^3 = 27\\)\n\nApplying the difference of cubes formula, we have:\n\n\\[\n8x^3 - 27 = (2x - 3)((2x)^2 + (2x)(3) + 3^2)\n\\]\n\nNow, let's simplify the second factor:\n\n1. \\((2x)^2 = 4x^2\\)\n2. \\((2x)(3) = 6x\\)\n3. \\(3^2 = 9\\)\n\nThus, the factorization becomes:\n\n\\[\n(2x - 3)(4x^2 + 6x + 9)\n\\]\n\nComparing this with the form \\((ax + b)(cx^2 + dx + e)\\), we identify the coefficients:\n\n- \\(a = 2\\)\n- \\(b = -3\\)\n- \\(c = 4\\)\n- \\(d = 6\\)\n- \\(e = 9\\)\n\nNow, we calculate the sum of these coefficients:\n\n\\[\na + b + c + d + e = 2 - 3 + 4 + 6 + 9\n\\]\n\nCalculating the sum:\n\n\\[\n2 - 3 + 4 + 6 + 9 = 18\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the sum of the coefficients is \\(\\boxed{18}\\)."
"Let's solve the equation \\(\\frac{3x+2}{x-1}=4\\) for \\(x\\) step by step.\n\n### Step 1: Eliminate the Fraction\nTo eliminate the fraction, multiply both sides of the equation by \\(x-1\\). This will remove the denominator:\n\n\\[\n(x-1) \\cdot \\frac{3x+2}{x-1} = 4 \\cdot (x-1)\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n3x + 2 = 4(x - 1)\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Distribute on the Right Side\nExpand the right side of the equation by distributing the 4:\n\n\\[\n3x + 2 = 4x - 4\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Rearrange the Equation\nMove all terms involving \\(x\\) to one side and constant terms to the other side. Subtract \\(3x\\) from both sides to isolate the terms with \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\n2 = 4x - 3x - 4\n\\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\n\\[\n2 = x - 4\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Solve for \\(x\\)\nAdd 4 to both sides to solve for \\(x\\):\n\n\\[\n2 + 4 = x\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = 6\n\\]\n\nThus, the solution to the equation is \\(x = 6\\).\n\n### Verification\nTo verify, substitute \\(x = 6\\) back into the original equation:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3(6) + 2}{6 - 1} = \\frac{18 + 2}{5} = \\frac{20}{5} = 4\n\\]\n\nThe left side equals the right side, confirming that \\(x = 6\\) is indeed the correct solution."
"Let's solve the problem step by step.\n\n### Step 1: Find the Intersection Points \\( P \\) and \\( Q \\)\n\nThe parabola is given by the equation \\( y^2 = 4ax \\), and its focus is at the point \\( (a, 0) \\).\n\nThe line passing through the focus has the equation \\( y = m(x - a) \\), which simplifies to \\( y = mx - ma \\).\n\nTo find the intersection points \\( P \\) and \\( Q \\), substitute \\( y = mx - ma \\) into the parabola equation:\n\n\\[\n(mx - ma)^2 = 4ax.\n\\]\n\nExpanding and simplifying:\n\n\\[\nm^2x^2 - 2m^2ax + m^2a^2 = 4ax.\n\\]\n\nRearrange the terms:\n\n\\[\nm^2x^2 - (2m^2a + 4a)x + m^2a^2 = 0.\n\\]\n\nThis is a quadratic equation in \\( x \\). The solutions for \\( x \\) are given by the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{(2m^2a + 4a) \\pm \\sqrt{(2m^2a + 4a)^2 - 4m^2a^2}}{2m^2}.\n\\]\n\nSimplify the discriminant:\n\n\\[\n(2m^2a + 4a)^2 - 4m^2a^2 = 4a^2(m^2 + 2)^2 - 4m^2a^2 = 4a^2(m^4 + 4m^2 + 4 - m^2) = 16a^2.\n\\]\n\nThus, the solutions for \\( x \\) are:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{2a(m^2 + 2) \\pm 4a}{2m^2} = \\frac{2a(m^2 + 2 \\pm 2)}{2m^2}.\n\\]\n\nThis gives us:\n\n\\[\nx_1 = \\frac{2a(m^2 + 4)}{2m^2} = \\frac{a(m^2 + 4)}{m^2},\n\\]\n\\[\nx_2 = \\frac{2a(m^2)}{2m^2} = a.\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Determine the Coordinates of \\( P \\) and \\( Q \\)\n\nThe \\( x \\)-coordinates of \\( P \\) and \\( Q \\) are \\( x_1 = \\frac{a(m^2 + 4)}{m^2} \\) and \\( x_2 = a \\).\n\nFor \\( P \\), substitute \\( x_1 \\) back into the line equation to find \\( y_1 \\):\n\n\\[\ny_1 = m\\left(\\frac{a(m^2 + 4)}{m^2} - a\\right) = m\\left(\\frac{4a}{m^2}\\right) = \\frac{4a}{m}.\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( P = \\left(\\frac{a(m^2 + 4)}{m^2}, \\frac{4a}{m}\\right) \\).\n\nFor \\( Q \\), since \\( x_2 = a \\), substitute into the line equation:\n\n\\[\ny_2 = m(a - a) = 0.\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( Q = (a, 0) \\).\n\n### Step 3: Find the Reflection \\( R \\) of \\( P \\)\n\nThe reflection of \\( P \\) in the \\( x \\)-axis is \\( R = \\left(\\frac{a(m^2 + 4)}{m^2}, -\\frac{4a}{m}\\right) \\).\n\n### Step 4: Find the Intersection of Line \\( QR \\) with the \\( x \\)-axis\n\nThe line \\( QR \\) passes through \\( Q = (a, 0) \\) and \\( R = \\left(\\frac{a(m^2 + 4)}{m^2}, -\\frac{4a}{m}\\right) \\).\n\nThe slope of line \\( QR \\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\text{slope} = \\frac{-\\frac{4a}{m} - 0}{\\frac{a(m^2 + 4)}{m^2} - a} = \\frac{-\\frac{4a}{m}}{\\frac{4a}{m^2}} = -m.\n\\]\n\nThe equation of line \\( QR \\) is:\n\n\\[\ny - 0 = -m(x - a) \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad y = -mx + ma.\n\\]\n\nTo find the intersection with the \\( x \\)-axis, set \\( y = 0 \\):\n\n\\[\n0 = -mx + ma \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad mx = ma \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad x = a.\n\\]\n\nThus, the intersection of line \\( QR \\) with the \\( x \\)-axis is at \\( x = a \\).\n\nThe answer is \\(\\boxed{a}\\)."
'To solve this problem, we need to perform polynomial long division of the numerator by the denominator and express the result in the form given on the right-hand side of the equation.\n\nThe given equation is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{5x^4 - 8x^3 + 2x^2 + 4x + 7}{(x + 2)^4} = a + \\frac{b}{x + 2} + \\frac{c}{(x + 2)^2} + \\frac{d}{(x + 2)^3} + \\frac{e}{(x + 2)^4}\n\\]\n\n### Step 1: Polynomial Long Division\n\nWe divide the polynomial \\(5x^4 - 8x^3 + 2x^2 + 4x + 7\\) by \\((x + 2)^4\\).\n\n1. **Divide the leading term of the numerator by the leading term of the denominator:**\n\n   \\[\n   \\frac{5x^4}{x^4} = 5\n   \\]\n\n   So, the first term of the quotient is \\(5\\).\n\n2. **Multiply the entire divisor by this term and subtract from the original polynomial:**\n\n   \\[\n   (5x^4 - 8x^3 + 2x^2 + 4x + 7) - 5(x + 2)^4\n   \\]\n\n   Since \\((x + 2)^4\\) is exactly \\(x^4\\) plus lower degree terms, the subtraction will cancel out the \\(x^4\\) term and leave a remainder of lower degree.\n\n3. **The remainder will be a polynomial of degree less than 4, which can be expressed as:**\n\n   \\[\n   R(x) = b(x + 2)^3 + c(x + 2)^2 + d(x + 2) + e\n   \\]\n\n   where \\(R(x)\\) is the remainder after dividing \\(5x^4 - 8x^3 + 2x^2 + 4x + 7\\) by \\((x + 2)^4\\).\n\n### Step 2: Determine the Coefficients\n\nSince the division results in a constant term \\(a = 5\\) and a remainder that is expressed in terms of \\((x + 2)\\), the coefficients \\(b\\), \\(c\\), \\(d\\), and \\(e\\) are determined by matching the remainder to the polynomial \\(R(x)\\).\n\n### Step 3: Sum of Coefficients\n\nThe sum \\(a + b + c + d + e\\) is the sum of the constant term from the division and the coefficients of the remainder. Since the polynomial division results in a constant term \\(a = 5\\) and the remainder is zero (as the division is exact), the sum of the coefficients is simply:\n\n\\[\na + b + c + d + e = 5 + 0 + 0 + 0 + 0 = 5\n\\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(a + b + c + d + e\\) is \\(\\boxed{5}\\).'
"Let's think step by step.\n\nWe are given the function:\n\\[ f(r) = \\sum_{j=2}^{2008} \\frac{1}{j^r} = \\frac{1}{2^r} + \\frac{1}{3^r} + \\cdots + \\frac{1}{2008^r}. \\]\n\nWe need to find:\n\\[ \\sum_{k=2}^{\\infty} f(k) = \\sum_{k=2}^{\\infty} \\sum_{j=2}^{2008} \\frac{1}{j^k}. \\]\n\n### Step 1: Interchange the Order of Summation\n\nWe can interchange the order of summation:\n\\[ \\sum_{k=2}^{\\infty} \\sum_{j=2}^{2008} \\frac{1}{j^k} = \\sum_{j=2}^{2008} \\sum_{k=2}^{\\infty} \\frac{1}{j^k}. \\]\n\n### Step 2: Evaluate the Inner Sum\n\nThe inner sum:\n\\[ \\sum_{k=2}^{\\infty} \\frac{1}{j^k} \\]\nis a geometric series with the first term \\(\\frac{1}{j^2}\\) and common ratio \\(\\frac{1}{j}\\).\n\nThe sum of an infinite geometric series is given by:\n\\[ \\sum_{k=2}^{\\infty} \\frac{1}{j^k} = \\frac{\\frac{1}{j^2}}{1 - \\frac{1}{j}} = \\frac{1}{j^2} \\cdot \\frac{j}{j-1} = \\frac{1}{j(j-1)}. \\]\n\n### Step 3: Evaluate the Outer Sum\n\nNow, we need to evaluate:\n\\[ \\sum_{j=2}^{2008} \\frac{1}{j(j-1)}. \\]\n\n### Step 4: Use Partial Fraction Decomposition\n\nThe expression \\(\\frac{1}{j(j-1)}\\) can be decomposed into partial fractions:\n\\[ \\frac{1}{j(j-1)} = \\frac{1}{j-1} - \\frac{1}{j}. \\]\n\n### Step 5: Evaluate the Telescoping Series\n\nThe sum becomes:\n\\[ \\sum_{j=2}^{2008} \\left( \\frac{1}{j-1} - \\frac{1}{j} \\right). \\]\n\nThis is a telescoping series, where most terms cancel out:\n- The first few terms are: \\((1 - \\frac{1}{2}) + (\\frac{1}{2} - \\frac{1}{3}) + \\cdots + (\\frac{1}{2007} - \\frac{1}{2008})\\).\n\nAfter cancellation, we are left with:\n\\[ 1 - \\frac{1}{2008}. \\]\n\n### Conclusion\n\nThe final result of the sum is:\n\\[ \\frac{2007}{2008}. \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\sum_{k=2}^{\\infty} \\sum_{j=2}^{2008} \\frac{1}{j^k}\\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{2007}{2008}}\\)."
"To compute the area of the ellipse given by the equation \\(9x^2 + y^2 = 36\\), we need to rewrite the equation in the standard form of an ellipse. The standard form of an ellipse is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x^2}{a^2} + \\frac{y^2}{b^2} = 1\n\\]\n\nLet's start with the given equation:\n\n\\[\n9x^2 + y^2 = 36\n\\]\n\nTo convert this into the standard form, we divide every term by 36:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{9x^2}{36} + \\frac{y^2}{36} = 1\n\\]\n\nSimplifying the fractions, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{x^2}{4} + \\frac{y^2}{36} = 1\n\\]\n\nThis is now in the standard form of an ellipse, where \\(a^2 = 4\\) and \\(b^2 = 36\\). Therefore, we find:\n\n- \\(a = \\sqrt{4} = 2\\)\n- \\(b = \\sqrt{36} = 6\\)\n\nThe formula for the area \\(A\\) of an ellipse is given by:\n\n\\[\nA = \\pi \\cdot a \\cdot b\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the values of \\(a\\) and \\(b\\) into the formula, we get:\n\n\\[\nA = \\pi \\cdot 2 \\cdot 6 = 12\\pi\n\\]\n\nThus, the area of the ellipse is \\(\\boxed{12\\pi}\\)."
'To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of nonzero coefficients in the polynomial \\( P(x) \\) when expressed in standard form, given that:\n\n\\[\nx^{512} + x^{256} + 1 = (x^2 + x + 1) P(x).\n\\]\n\n### Step-by-step Solution\n\n1. **Understanding the Factorization:**\n\n   The polynomial \\( x^2 + x + 1 \\) is a factor of \\( x^3 - 1 \\) and has roots \\(\\omega\\) and \\(\\omega^2\\), where \\(\\omega = e^{2\\pi i / 3}\\) is a primitive cube root of unity. This means that \\( x^2 + x + 1 \\) divides any polynomial that is zero at these roots.\n\n2. **Expressing \\( x^{512} + x^{256} + 1 \\) in Terms of Roots of Unity:**\n\n   Since \\( x^3 \\equiv 1 \\pmod{x^2 + x + 1} \\), we can express powers of \\( x \\) modulo \\( x^2 + x + 1 \\) in terms of \\( x^3 \\equiv 1 \\). Specifically, any power of \\( x \\) that is a multiple of 3 will reduce to 1, and other powers will cycle through the values of the roots of unity.\n\n3. **Degree Consideration:**\n\n   The degree of \\( x^{512} + x^{256} + 1 \\) is 512. The degree of \\( x^2 + x + 1 \\) is 2. Therefore, the degree of \\( P(x) \\) is \\( 512 - 2 = 510 \\).\n\n4. **Finding the Polynomial \\( P(x) \\):**\n\n   To find \\( P(x) \\), we need to divide \\( x^{512} + x^{256} + 1 \\) by \\( x^2 + x + 1 \\). This division will result in a polynomial of degree 510.\n\n5. **Counting Nonzero Coefficients:**\n\n   The polynomial \\( x^{512} + x^{256} + 1 \\) can be expressed in terms of powers of \\( x^3 \\) because \\( x^3 \\equiv 1 \\pmod{x^2 + x + 1} \\). This means that the polynomial can be reduced to a form that is a multiple of \\( x^2 + x + 1 \\) plus a remainder that is a linear combination of \\( x^2, x, \\) and 1.\n\n   The polynomial \\( P(x) \\) will have nonzero coefficients corresponding to the terms that remain after division by \\( x^2 + x + 1 \\). Since the degree of \\( P(x) \\) is 510, and it is derived from a polynomial of degree 512, it will have a significant number of nonzero coefficients.\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n\n   The polynomial \\( P(x) \\) will have nonzero coefficients for each term that is not canceled out by the division process. Given the symmetry and the nature of the roots of unity, \\( P(x) \\) will have nonzero coefficients for most of its terms up to degree 510.\n\n   Therefore, the number of nonzero coefficients in \\( P(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{510}\\).'
'To determine the horizontal asymptote of the function \\( y = \\frac{4x^3 + 2x - 4}{3x^3 - 2x^2 + 5x - 1} \\), we need to consider the degrees of the numerator and the denominator.\n\n1. **Degrees of the Polynomials:**\n   - The degree of the numerator \\( 4x^3 + 2x - 4 \\) is 3.\n   - The degree of the denominator \\( 3x^3 - 2x^2 + 5x - 1 \\) is also 3.\n\n2. **Horizontal Asymptote for Rational Functions:**\n   - When the degrees of the numerator and the denominator are equal, the horizontal asymptote is determined by the ratio of the leading coefficients of the numerator and the denominator.\n\n3. **Leading Coefficients:**\n   - The leading coefficient of the numerator is 4.\n   - The leading coefficient of the denominator is 3.\n\n4. **Horizontal Asymptote:**\n   - The horizontal asymptote is at \\( y = \\frac{\\text{leading coefficient of the numerator}}{\\text{leading coefficient of the denominator}} = \\frac{4}{3} \\).\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( y \\) at which there is a horizontal asymptote for the graph of the equation is \\( \\boxed{\\frac{4}{3}} \\).'
'To find the radical conjugate of the expression \\(\\sqrt{11} - 1\\), we follow the standard procedure for finding the conjugate of a binomial involving a square root.\n\n### Step-by-step Explanation:\n\n1. **Identify the Expression:**\n   The given expression is \\(\\sqrt{11} - 1\\).\n\n2. **Understand the Concept of Radical Conjugate:**\n   The radical conjugate of an expression of the form \\(\\sqrt{a} - b\\) is \\(\\sqrt{a} + b\\). This is because the conjugate is formed by changing the sign between the two terms.\n\n3. **Apply the Concept:**\n   For the expression \\(\\sqrt{11} - 1\\), the radical conjugate is obtained by changing the minus sign to a plus sign:\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{11} + 1\n   \\]\n\n4. **Verify the Result:**\n   The product of an expression and its radical conjugate is a rational number. Specifically, for \\((\\sqrt{11} - 1)(\\sqrt{11} + 1)\\), we use the difference of squares formula:\n   \\[\n   (\\sqrt{11} - 1)(\\sqrt{11} + 1) = (\\sqrt{11})^2 - (1)^2 = 11 - 1 = 10\n   \\]\n   This confirms that \\(\\sqrt{11} + 1\\) is indeed the correct radical conjugate.\n\nThus, the radical conjugate of \\(\\sqrt{11} - 1\\) is \\(\\boxed{\\sqrt{11} + 1}\\).'
"Let's analyze the sequence defined by the recurrence relation \\( F_{n} = (F_{n-1} + F_{n-2}) \\mod 3 \\) with initial conditions \\( F_{0} = 0 \\) and \\( F_{1} = 1 \\).\n\n### Step 1: Generate the Sequence\n\nWe start by calculating the first few terms of the sequence:\n\n- \\( F_0 = 0 \\)\n- \\( F_1 = 1 \\)\n- \\( F_2 = (F_1 + F_0) \\mod 3 = (1 + 0) \\mod 3 = 1 \\)\n- \\( F_3 = (F_2 + F_1) \\mod 3 = (1 + 1) \\mod 3 = 2 \\)\n- \\( F_4 = (F_3 + F_2) \\mod 3 = (2 + 1) \\mod 3 = 0 \\)\n- \\( F_5 = (F_4 + F_3) \\mod 3 = (0 + 2) \\mod 3 = 2 \\)\n- \\( F_6 = (F_5 + F_4) \\mod 3 = (2 + 0) \\mod 3 = 2 \\)\n- \\( F_7 = (F_6 + F_5) \\mod 3 = (2 + 2) \\mod 3 = 1 \\)\n- \\( F_8 = (F_7 + F_6) \\mod 3 = (1 + 2) \\mod 3 = 0 \\)\n- \\( F_9 = (F_8 + F_7) \\mod 3 = (0 + 1) \\mod 3 = 1 \\)\n- \\( F_{10} = (F_9 + F_8) \\mod 3 = (1 + 0) \\mod 3 = 1 \\)\n\nContinuing this process, we notice that the sequence starts repeating. Let's identify the cycle:\n\n### Step 2: Identify the Cycle\n\nBy continuing the calculations, we find that the sequence repeats every 8 terms:\n\n- \\( F_0 = 0 \\)\n- \\( F_1 = 1 \\)\n- \\( F_2 = 1 \\)\n- \\( F_3 = 2 \\)\n- \\( F_4 = 0 \\)\n- \\( F_5 = 2 \\)\n- \\( F_6 = 2 \\)\n- \\( F_7 = 1 \\)\n- \\( F_8 = 0 \\) (same as \\( F_0 \\))\n- \\( F_9 = 1 \\) (same as \\( F_1 \\))\n- \\( F_{10} = 1 \\) (same as \\( F_2 \\))\n- \\( F_{11} = 2 \\) (same as \\( F_3 \\))\n- \\( F_{12} = 0 \\) (same as \\( F_4 \\))\n- \\( F_{13} = 2 \\) (same as \\( F_5 \\))\n- \\( F_{14} = 2 \\) (same as \\( F_6 \\))\n- \\( F_{15} = 1 \\) (same as \\( F_7 \\))\n\nThus, the sequence has a period of 8.\n\n### Step 3: Calculate the Required Sum\n\nSince the sequence repeats every 8 terms, we need to find the position of \\( F_{2017} \\) to \\( F_{2024} \\) within the cycle:\n\n- \\( 2017 \\mod 8 = 1 \\) (corresponds to \\( F_1 \\))\n- \\( 2018 \\mod 8 = 2 \\) (corresponds to \\( F_2 \\))\n- \\( 2019 \\mod 8 = 3 \\) (corresponds to \\( F_3 \\))\n- \\( 2020 \\mod 8 = 4 \\) (corresponds to \\( F_4 \\))\n- \\( 2021 \\mod 8 = 5 \\) (corresponds to \\( F_5 \\))\n- \\( 2022 \\mod 8 = 6 \\) (corresponds to \\( F_6 \\))\n- \\( 2023 \\mod 8 = 7 \\) (corresponds to \\( F_7 \\))\n- \\( 2024 \\mod 8 = 0 \\) (corresponds to \\( F_0 \\))\n\nNow, sum these terms from the cycle:\n\\[ F_1 + F_2 + F_3 + F_4 + F_5 + F_6 + F_7 + F_0 = 1 + 1 + 2 + 0 + 2 + 2 + 1 + 0 = 9. \\]\n\nThus, the sum \\( F_{2017} + F_{2018} + F_{2019} + F_{2020} + F_{2021} + F_{2022} + F_{2023} + F_{2024} \\) is \\(\\boxed{9}\\)."
"Let's simplify the given expression step by step:\n\nThe expression is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{(2^4 + \\frac{1}{4})(4^4 + \\frac{1}{4}) \\dotsm [(2n)^4 + \\frac{1}{4}]}{(1^4 + \\frac{1}{4})(3^4 + \\frac{1}{4}) \\dotsm [(2n - 1)^4 + \\frac{1}{4}]}.\n\\]\n\n### Step 1: Express Each Term\n\nEach term in the numerator and denominator can be expressed in the form \\(x^4 + \\frac{1}{4}\\).\n\nFor the numerator, the terms are \\((2k)^4 + \\frac{1}{4}\\) for \\(k = 1, 2, \\ldots, n\\).\n\nFor the denominator, the terms are \\((2k-1)^4 + \\frac{1}{4}\\) for \\(k = 1, 2, \\ldots, n\\).\n\n### Step 2: Simplify Each Term\n\nNotice that:\n\n\\[\nx^4 + \\frac{1}{4} = \\left(x^2 + \\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2 - x^2.\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten using the identity:\n\n\\[\nx^4 + \\frac{1}{4} = \\left(x^2 + \\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2 - \\left(x^2 - \\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2.\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Apply the Identity\n\nFor the numerator:\n\n\\[\n(2k)^4 + \\frac{1}{4} = \\left((2k)^2 + \\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2 - \\left((2k)^2 - \\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2.\n\\]\n\nFor the denominator:\n\n\\[\n(2k-1)^4 + \\frac{1}{4} = \\left((2k-1)^2 + \\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2 - \\left((2k-1)^2 - \\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2.\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Recognize the Pattern\n\nThe terms in the numerator and denominator can be paired such that:\n\n- The numerator term \\((2k)^4 + \\frac{1}{4}\\) corresponds to the denominator term \\((2k-1)^4 + \\frac{1}{4}\\).\n\n### Step 5: Simplify the Expression\n\nNotice that:\n\n\\[\n(2k)^4 + \\frac{1}{4} = (4k^2 + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - (4k^2 - \\frac{1}{2})^2\n\\]\n\nand\n\n\\[\n(2k-1)^4 + \\frac{1}{4} = ((2k-1)^2 + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - ((2k-1)^2 - \\frac{1}{2})^2.\n\\]\n\nThe expression simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{(2k)^4 + \\frac{1}{4}}{(2k-1)^4 + \\frac{1}{4}} = \\frac{(4k^2 + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - (4k^2 - \\frac{1}{2})^2}{((2k-1)^2 + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - ((2k-1)^2 - \\frac{1}{2})^2}.\n\\]\n\n### Step 6: Final Simplification\n\nThe expression simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n\\prod_{k=1}^{n} \\frac{(2k)^4 + \\frac{1}{4}}{(2k-1)^4 + \\frac{1}{4}} = \\prod_{k=1}^{n} \\frac{(4k^2 + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - (4k^2 - \\frac{1}{2})^2}{((2k-1)^2 + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - ((2k-1)^2 - \\frac{1}{2})^2}.\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n\\prod_{k=1}^{n} \\frac{(4k^2 + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - (4k^2 - \\frac{1}{2})^2}{((2k-1)^2 + \\frac{1}{2})^2 - ((2k-1)^2 - \\frac{1}{2})^2} = \\prod_{k=1}^{n} \\frac{16k^2}{1} = \\prod_{k=1}^{n} 16k^2.\n\\]\n\nThus, the simplified expression is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{2^n}.\n\\]"
'To solve the problem, we need to find the number of distinct four-tuples \\((a, b, c, d)\\) of rational numbers that satisfy the equation:\n\n\\[\na\\log_{10} 2 + b\\log_{10} 3 + c\\log_{10} 5 + d\\log_{10} 7 = 2005.\n\\]\n\n### Step-by-step Solution\n\n1. **Understanding the Equation:**\n\n   The equation is a linear combination of logarithms of prime numbers, set equal to a constant. The coefficients \\(a\\), \\(b\\), \\(c\\), and \\(d\\) are rational numbers.\n\n2. **Rational Solutions:**\n\n   Since \\(a\\), \\(b\\), \\(c\\), and \\(d\\) are rational, we can express them as fractions:\n   \\[\n   a = \\frac{p}{q}, \\quad b = \\frac{r}{s}, \\quad c = \\frac{t}{u}, \\quad d = \\frac{v}{w}\n   \\]\n   where \\(p, q, r, s, t, u, v, w\\) are integers and \\(q, s, u, w \\neq 0\\).\n\n3. **Rewriting the Equation:**\n\n   Multiply the entire equation by the least common multiple of the denominators \\(q, s, u, w\\) to clear the fractions. This gives:\n   \\[\n   p \\cdot \\log_{10} 2 + r \\cdot \\log_{10} 3 + t \\cdot \\log_{10} 5 + v \\cdot \\log_{10} 7 = 2005 \\cdot \\text{lcm}(q, s, u, w).\n   \\]\n\n4. **Linear Independence of Logarithms:**\n\n   The logarithms \\(\\log_{10} 2\\), \\(\\log_{10} 3\\), \\(\\log_{10} 5\\), and \\(\\log_{10} 7\\) are linearly independent over the rationals. This is because if there were a nontrivial rational linear combination of these logarithms equaling zero, it would imply a nontrivial integer relation among the primes 2, 3, 5, and 7, which is impossible.\n\n5. **Implication of Linear Independence:**\n\n   Since the logarithms are linearly independent, the only way the equation can hold is if each coefficient of the logarithms is zero. However, this would imply that the right-hand side, 2005, must also be zero, which is not the case.\n\n6. **Conclusion:**\n\n   The linear independence of the logarithms over the rationals implies that there are no nontrivial rational solutions to the equation. Therefore, there are no distinct four-tuples \\((a, b, c, d)\\) of rational numbers that satisfy the given equation.\n\nThus, the number of distinct four-tuples \\((a, b, c, d)\\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\).'
"Let's solve the problem step by step.\n\nWe are given:\n1. \\( a + b + c = 0 \\)\n2. \\( a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 4 \\)\n\nWe need to find \\( a^4 + b^4 + c^4 \\).\n\n### Step 1: Use the identity for the square of sums\n\nFrom the identity for the square of sums, we have:\n\\[\n(a + b + c)^2 = a^2 + b^2 + c^2 + 2(ab + bc + ca)\n\\]\n\nSubstituting the given values:\n\\[\n0 = 4 + 2(ab + bc + ca)\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( ab + bc + ca \\):\n\\[\n2(ab + bc + ca) = -4 \\implies ab + bc + ca = -2\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Use the identity for the sum of fourth powers\n\nWe use the identity:\n\\[\na^4 + b^4 + c^4 = (a^2 + b^2 + c^2)^2 - 2(a^2b^2 + b^2c^2 + c^2a^2)\n\\]\n\nWe already know \\( a^2 + b^2 + c^2 = 4 \\), so:\n\\[\n(a^2 + b^2 + c^2)^2 = 4^2 = 16\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Find \\( a^2b^2 + b^2c^2 + c^2a^2 \\)\n\nWe use the identity:\n\\[\n(a^2 + b^2 + c^2)^2 = a^4 + b^4 + c^4 + 2(a^2b^2 + b^2c^2 + c^2a^2)\n\\]\n\nWe have:\n\\[\n16 = a^4 + b^4 + c^4 + 2(a^2b^2 + b^2c^2 + c^2a^2)\n\\]\n\nWe also know:\n\\[\n(ab + bc + ca)^2 = a^2b^2 + b^2c^2 + c^2a^2 + 2abc(a + b + c)\n\\]\n\nSince \\( a + b + c = 0 \\), the term \\( 2abc(a + b + c) = 0 \\). Thus:\n\\[\n(ab + bc + ca)^2 = a^2b^2 + b^2c^2 + c^2a^2\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\( ab + bc + ca = -2 \\):\n\\[\n(-2)^2 = a^2b^2 + b^2c^2 + c^2a^2 \\implies 4 = a^2b^2 + b^2c^2 + c^2a^2\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Calculate \\( a^4 + b^4 + c^4 \\)\n\nSubstitute back into the equation:\n\\[\n16 = a^4 + b^4 + c^4 + 2 \\times 4\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\\[\n16 = a^4 + b^4 + c^4 + 8\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\\[\na^4 + b^4 + c^4 = 16 - 8 = 8\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( a^4 + b^4 + c^4 \\) is \\(\\boxed{8}\\)."
'To find the remainder when \\(x^4 - 3x^3 + 4x^2 + 11x - 9\\) is divided by \\(x^2 - 3x + 2\\) using synthetic division, we follow these steps:\n\n### Step 1: Factor the Divisor\nThe divisor is \\(x^2 - 3x + 2\\). We can factor it as \\((x - 1)(x - 2)\\). This means we will perform synthetic division twice, first with \\(x = 1\\) and then with \\(x = 2\\).\n\n### Step 2: First Synthetic Division with \\(x = 1\\)\n1. Write down the coefficients of the dividend: \\(1, -3, 4, 11, -9\\).\n2. Use synthetic division with \\(x = 1\\):\n\n   \\[\n   \\begin{array}{r|rrrrr}\n   1 & 1 & -3 & 4 & 11 & -9 \\\\\n     &   & 1 & -2 & 2 & 13 \\\\\n   \\hline\n     & 1 & -2 & 2 & 13 & 4 \\\\\n   \\end{array}\n   \\]\n\n   The quotient is \\(x^3 - 2x^2 + 2x + 13\\) and the remainder is 4.\n\n### Step 3: Second Synthetic Division with \\(x = 2\\)\n1. Use the quotient from the first division: \\(1, -2, 2, 13\\).\n2. Use synthetic division with \\(x = 2\\):\n\n   \\[\n   \\begin{array}{r|rrrr}\n   2 & 1 & -2 & 2 & 13 \\\\\n     &   & 2 & 0 & 4 \\\\\n   \\hline\n     & 1 & 0 & 2 & 17 \\\\\n   \\end{array}\n   \\]\n\n   The quotient is \\(x^2 + 0x + 2\\) and the remainder is 17.\n\n### Conclusion\nThe final remainder when \\(x^4 - 3x^3 + 4x^2 + 11x - 9\\) is divided by \\(x^2 - 3x + 2\\) is 17. Therefore, the answer is \\(\\boxed{17}\\).'
"Let's solve the problem step by step.\n\nGiven that \\( f(x) \\) is a cubic polynomial, we can express it as:\n\\[ f(x) = ax^3 + bx^2 + cx + d. \\]\n\n### Step 1: Use the condition \\( f(0) = 0 \\)\n\nThe condition \\( f(0) = 0 \\) implies:\n\\[ d = 0. \\]\n\nSo, the polynomial simplifies to:\n\\[ f(x) = ax^3 + bx^2 + cx. \\]\n\n### Step 2: Use the condition \\( f(1) = 1 \\)\n\nSubstitute \\( x = 1 \\) into the polynomial:\n\\[ a(1)^3 + b(1)^2 + c(1) = 1 \\]\n\\[ a + b + c = 1. \\]\n\n### Step 3: Use the condition \\( f(2) = 2 \\)\n\nSubstitute \\( x = 2 \\) into the polynomial:\n\\[ a(2)^3 + b(2)^2 + c(2) = 2 \\]\n\\[ 8a + 4b + 2c = 2. \\]\n\n### Step 4: Use the condition \\( f(3) = 4 \\)\n\nSubstitute \\( x = 3 \\) into the polynomial:\n\\[ a(3)^3 + b(3)^2 + c(3) = 4 \\]\n\\[ 27a + 9b + 3c = 4. \\]\n\n### Step 5: Solve the system of equations\n\nWe have the following system of equations:\n1. \\( a + b + c = 1 \\)\n2. \\( 8a + 4b + 2c = 2 \\)\n3. \\( 27a + 9b + 3c = 4 \\)\n\nLet's solve these equations.\n\nFrom equation 2, divide everything by 2:\n\\[ 4a + 2b + c = 1. \\]\n\nSubtract equation 1 from this:\n\\[ (4a + 2b + c) - (a + b + c) = 1 - 1 \\]\n\\[ 3a + b = 0 \\]\n\\[ b = -3a. \\]\n\nSubstitute \\( b = -3a \\) into equation 1:\n\\[ a - 3a + c = 1 \\]\n\\[ -2a + c = 1 \\]\n\\[ c = 2a + 1. \\]\n\nSubstitute \\( b = -3a \\) and \\( c = 2a + 1 \\) into equation 3:\n\\[ 27a + 9(-3a) + 3(2a + 1) = 4 \\]\n\\[ 27a - 27a + 6a + 3 = 4 \\]\n\\[ 6a + 3 = 4 \\]\n\\[ 6a = 1 \\]\n\\[ a = \\frac{1}{6}. \\]\n\nNow, find \\( b \\) and \\( c \\):\n\\[ b = -3a = -3 \\times \\frac{1}{6} = -\\frac{1}{2}. \\]\n\\[ c = 2a + 1 = 2 \\times \\frac{1}{6} + 1 = \\frac{1}{3} + 1 = \\frac{4}{3}. \\]\n\n### Step 6: Find \\( f(5) \\)\n\nNow that we have \\( a = \\frac{1}{6} \\), \\( b = -\\frac{1}{2} \\), and \\( c = \\frac{4}{3} \\), the polynomial is:\n\\[ f(x) = \\frac{1}{6}x^3 - \\frac{1}{2}x^2 + \\frac{4}{3}x. \\]\n\nSubstitute \\( x = 5 \\) into the polynomial:\n\\[ f(5) = \\frac{1}{6}(5)^3 - \\frac{1}{2}(5)^2 + \\frac{4}{3}(5). \\]\n\\[ f(5) = \\frac{1}{6}(125) - \\frac{1}{2}(25) + \\frac{4}{3}(5). \\]\n\\[ f(5) = \\frac{125}{6} - \\frac{25}{2} + \\frac{20}{3}. \\]\n\nConvert all terms to have a common denominator of 6:\n\\[ f(5) = \\frac{125}{6} - \\frac{75}{6} + \\frac{40}{6}. \\]\n\\[ f(5) = \\frac{125 - 75 + 40}{6}. \\]\n\\[ f(5) = \\frac{90}{6}. \\]\n\\[ f(5) = 15. \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( f(5) \\) is \\(\\boxed{15}\\)."
"Let's analyze the given equation step by step to determine the type of conic section it represents:\n\nThe equation is:\n\\[ y^2 - x + 5y - 25 = 0. \\]\n\n### Step 1: Rearrange the Equation\n\nRearrange the equation to isolate \\( x \\):\n\\[ x = y^2 + 5y - 25. \\]\n\nThis equation is now in the form of a quadratic equation in terms of \\( y \\) with respect to \\( x \\).\n\n### Step 2: Identify the Type of Conic Section\n\nThe equation \\( x = y^2 + 5y - 25 \\) is a quadratic function in \\( y \\). It can be rewritten as:\n\\[ x = (y^2 + 5y) - 25. \\]\n\nThis is a standard form of a parabola that opens horizontally. The presence of the \\( y^2 \\) term and the absence of an \\( x^2 \\) term indicates that the graph is a parabola.\n\n### Step 3: Confirm the Characteristics\n\n- **Parabola**: A parabola is characterized by having one squared term. In this case, \\( y^2 \\) is the squared term, confirming that the graph is a parabola.\n- **Not a Circle, Ellipse, or Hyperbola**: These conic sections require both \\( x^2 \\) and \\( y^2 \\) terms, which are not present simultaneously in this equation.\n- **Not a Point, Line, Two Lines, or Empty**: The equation is a quadratic in \\( y \\), which means it represents a curve (specifically a parabola) rather than a degenerate conic section like a point, line, or two lines.\n\n### Conclusion\n\nThe equation \\( y^2 - x + 5y - 25 = 0 \\) represents a parabola. Therefore, the graph of the equation is a \\(\\boxed{\\text{parabola}}\\)."
