"Let's solve the problem step by step.\n\nWe are given a sequence of equations:\n\n1. \\( 4^{x_1} = 5 \\)\n2. \\( 5^{x_2} = 6 \\)\n3. \\( 6^{x_3} = 7 \\)\n4. \\(\\vdots\\)\n5. \\( 127^{x_{124}} = 128 \\)\n\nWe need to find the product \\( x_1 x_2 \\cdots x_{124} \\).\n\n### Step 1: Express each \\( x_k \\) in terms of logarithms\n\nFor each equation \\( n^{x_k} = n+1 \\), we can take the logarithm to get:\n\n\\[\nx_k \\cdot \\log(n) = \\log(n+1)\n\\]\n\nThus, \n\n\\[\nx_k = \\frac{\\log(n+1)}{\\log(n)}\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Write the product of all \\( x_k \\)'s\n\nThe product \\( x_1 x_2 \\cdots x_{124} \\) becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\prod_{k=1}^{124} x_k = \\prod_{n=4}^{127} \\frac{\\log(n+1)}{\\log(n)}\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Simplify the telescoping product\n\nThe product is telescoping:\n\n\\[\n\\prod_{n=4}^{127} \\frac{\\log(n+1)}{\\log(n)} = \\frac{\\log(5)}{\\log(4)} \\cdot \\frac{\\log(6)}{\\log(5)} \\cdot \\frac{\\log(7)}{\\log(6)} \\cdots \\frac{\\log(128)}{\\log(127)}\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\log(128)}{\\log(4)}\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Calculate the final expression\n\nSince \\( 128 = 2^7 \\) and \\( 4 = 2^2 \\), we have:\n\n\\[\n\\log(128) = 7 \\log(2) \\quad \\text{and} \\quad \\log(4) = 2 \\log(2)\n\\]\n\nTherefore:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\log(128)}{\\log(4)} = \\frac{7 \\log(2)}{2 \\log(2)} = \\frac{7}{2}\n\\]\n\nThus, the product \\( x_1 x_2 \\cdots x_{124} \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{7}{2}}\\)."
'To find the largest possible value of \\(|z_1 - z_2|^2 + |z_1 - z_3|^2 + |z_2 - z_3|^2\\) given that \\(|z_1| = 2\\), \\(|z_2| = 3\\), and \\(|z_3| = 4\\), we can use the properties of complex numbers and the geometry of the complex plane.\n\n### Step-by-step Solution\n\n1. **Express the Distances:**\n\n   The expression we want to maximize is:\n   \\[\n   |z_1 - z_2|^2 + |z_1 - z_3|^2 + |z_2 - z_3|^2.\n   \\]\n\n   Using the identity for the squared distance between two complex numbers \\(z\\) and \\(w\\), we have:\n   \\[\n   |z - w|^2 = (z - w)(\\overline{z} - \\overline{w}) = |z|^2 + |w|^2 - 2\\text{Re}(z\\overline{w}).\n   \\]\n\n2. **Apply the Identity:**\n\n   Applying this identity to each pair, we get:\n   \\[\n   |z_1 - z_2|^2 = |z_1|^2 + |z_2|^2 - 2\\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_2}),\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   |z_1 - z_3|^2 = |z_1|^2 + |z_3|^2 - 2\\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_3}),\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   |z_2 - z_3|^2 = |z_2|^2 + |z_3|^2 - 2\\text{Re}(z_2\\overline{z_3}).\n   \\]\n\n3. **Substitute the Magnitudes:**\n\n   Substitute the given magnitudes:\n   \\[\n   |z_1 - z_2|^2 = 2^2 + 3^2 - 2\\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_2}) = 13 - 2\\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_2}),\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   |z_1 - z_3|^2 = 2^2 + 4^2 - 2\\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_3}) = 20 - 2\\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_3}),\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   |z_2 - z_3|^2 = 3^2 + 4^2 - 2\\text{Re}(z_2\\overline{z_3}) = 25 - 2\\text{Re}(z_2\\overline{z_3}).\n   \\]\n\n4. **Combine the Expressions:**\n\n   Combine these to get the total expression:\n   \\[\n   |z_1 - z_2|^2 + |z_1 - z_3|^2 + |z_2 - z_3|^2 = 13 + 20 + 25 - 2(\\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_2}) + \\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_3}) + \\text{Re}(z_2\\overline{z_3})).\n   \\]\n\n   Simplifying, we have:\n   \\[\n   58 - 2(\\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_2}) + \\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_3}) + \\text{Re}(z_2\\overline{z_3})).\n   \\]\n\n5. **Maximize the Expression:**\n\n   To maximize the expression, we need to minimize the sum of the real parts:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_2}) + \\text{Re}(z_1\\overline{z_3}) + \\text{Re}(z_2\\overline{z_3}).\n   \\]\n\n   The minimum value of this sum occurs when the vectors \\(z_1\\), \\(z_2\\), and \\(z_3\\) are collinear and in opposite directions, which geometrically means they form a straight line. In this case, the real parts can be minimized to zero.\n\n6. **Calculate the Maximum Value:**\n\n   If the real parts sum to zero, the expression becomes:\n   \\[\n   58 - 2 \\times 0 = 58.\n   \\]\n\nThus, the largest possible value of \\(|z_1 - z_2|^2 + |z_1 - z_3|^2 + |z_2 - z_3|^2\\) is \\(\\boxed{58}\\).'
"To determine how much closer Chloe's dart is to the origin compared to Sasha's dart, we need to calculate the distances from the origin to each of their respective points on the complex plane.\n\n### Step 1: Calculate the Distance for Sasha's Dart\n\nSasha's dart lands on the point \\(15 + 8i\\). The distance from the origin to this point is given by the formula for the magnitude of a complex number:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Distance for Sasha} = \\sqrt{15^2 + 8^2} = \\sqrt{225 + 64} = \\sqrt{289} = 17\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Calculate the Distance for Chloe's Dart\n\nChloe's dart lands on the point \\(3 - 4i\\). Similarly, the distance from the origin to this point is:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Distance for Chloe} = \\sqrt{3^2 + (-4)^2} = \\sqrt{9 + 16} = \\sqrt{25} = 5\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Calculate the Difference in Distances\n\nNow, we find the difference in distances from the origin between Chloe's dart and Sasha's dart:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Difference} = 17 - 5 = 12\n\\]\n\nThus, Chloe's dart is 12 units closer to the origin compared to Sasha's dart. Therefore, the answer is \\(\\boxed{12}\\)."
"To find the minimum value of the function \n\n\\[\nf(x) = \\sqrt{5x^2 + 2x \\sqrt{5} + 1} + x \\sqrt{5},\n\\]\n\nwe first need to determine the domain of \\( f(x) \\). The expression under the square root, \\( 5x^2 + 2x \\sqrt{5} + 1 \\), must be non-negative for \\( f(x) \\) to be defined. Let's analyze this quadratic expression:\n\n### Step 1: Analyze the Quadratic Expression\n\nThe quadratic expression is:\n\n\\[\n5x^2 + 2x \\sqrt{5} + 1.\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten as a perfect square trinomial:\n\n\\[\n5x^2 + 2x \\sqrt{5} + 1 = (\\sqrt{5}x + 1)^2.\n\\]\n\nSince this is a perfect square, it is always non-negative for all real \\( x \\). Therefore, the domain of \\( f(x) \\) is all real numbers.\n\n### Step 2: Simplify the Function\n\nGiven that the quadratic is a perfect square, we can simplify \\( f(x) \\):\n\n\\[\nf(x) = \\sqrt{(\\sqrt{5}x + 1)^2} + x \\sqrt{5}.\n\\]\n\nThe square root of a square is the absolute value:\n\n\\[\nf(x) = |\\sqrt{5}x + 1| + x \\sqrt{5}.\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Consider Cases Based on the Absolute Value\n\nWe need to consider two cases based on the expression inside the absolute value:\n\n1. **Case 1:** \\( \\sqrt{5}x + 1 \\geq 0 \\), i.e., \\( x \\geq -\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{5}} \\).\n\n   In this case, \\( |\\sqrt{5}x + 1| = \\sqrt{5}x + 1 \\), so:\n\n   \\[\n   f(x) = (\\sqrt{5}x + 1) + x \\sqrt{5} = 2\\sqrt{5}x + 1.\n   \\]\n\n   The function \\( 2\\sqrt{5}x + 1 \\) is linear and increasing, so its minimum value occurs at \\( x = -\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{5}} \\):\n\n   \\[\n   f\\left(-\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{5}}\\right) = 2\\sqrt{5}\\left(-\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{5}}\\right) + 1 = -2 + 1 = -1.\n   \\]\n\n2. **Case 2:** \\( \\sqrt{5}x + 1 < 0 \\), i.e., \\( x < -\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{5}} \\).\n\n   In this case, \\( |\\sqrt{5}x + 1| = -(\\sqrt{5}x + 1) \\), so:\n\n   \\[\n   f(x) = -(\\sqrt{5}x + 1) + x \\sqrt{5} = -\\sqrt{5}x - 1 + x \\sqrt{5} = -1.\n   \\]\n\n   Here, \\( f(x) = -1 \\) is constant for \\( x < -\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{5}} \\).\n\n### Conclusion\n\nThus, the minimum value of \\( f(x) \\) is \\(-1\\), and it occurs for all \\( x \\leq -\\frac{1}{\\sqrt{5}} \\).\n\nTherefore, the minimum value of \\( f(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{-1}\\)."
"Let's think step by step.\n\nWe have an arithmetic sequence with terms \\( a, a+d, a+2d, \\ldots, a+(n-1)d \\). The sum of these terms is given by:\n\n\\[\nS = \\frac{n}{2} \\left(2a + (n-1)d\\right) = 715\n\\]\n\nNext, we modify each term by adding the corresponding odd positive integer. The sequence of odd positive integers is \\( 1, 3, 5, \\ldots, 2k-1 \\). Therefore, the \\( k \\)-th term of the sequence is increased by \\( 2k-1 \\).\n\nThe sum of the new sequence is:\n\n\\[\nS' = \\left(a + 1\\right) + \\left(a + d + 3\\right) + \\left(a + 2d + 5\\right) + \\cdots + \\left(a + (n-1)d + (2n-1)\\right) = 836\n\\]\n\nThe difference between the sums of the new and original sequences is:\n\n\\[\nS' - S = (1 + 3 + 5 + \\cdots + (2n-1)) = 836 - 715 = 121\n\\]\n\nThe sum of the first \\( n \\) odd positive integers is \\( n^2 \\). Therefore, we have:\n\n\\[\nn^2 = 121 \\implies n = 11\n\\]\n\nNow, we know the sequence has 11 terms. The sum of the original sequence is:\n\n\\[\nS = \\frac{11}{2} \\left(2a + 10d\\right) = 715\n\\]\n\nSolving for \\( a \\) and \\( d \\):\n\n\\[\n11a + 55d = 715 \\implies a + 5d = 65\n\\]\n\nThe first term is \\( a \\), the last term is \\( a + 10d \\), and the middle term (6th term) is \\( a + 5d \\).\n\nThe sum of the first, last, and middle terms is:\n\n\\[\na + (a + 10d) + (a + 5d) = 3a + 15d\n\\]\n\nUsing \\( a + 5d = 65 \\), we have:\n\n\\[\n3a + 15d = 3(a + 5d) = 3 \\times 65 = 195\n\\]\n\nThus, the sum of the first, last, and middle terms of the original sequence is \\(\\boxed{195}\\)."
"Let's factor the polynomial \\(x^4 - 4x^3 + 14x^2 - 4x + 13\\) completely over the set of polynomials with integer coefficients.\n\n### Step 1: Check for Rational Roots\n\nUsing the Rational Root Theorem, we test possible rational roots, which are the factors of the constant term (13) over the factors of the leading coefficient (1). Thus, the possible rational roots are \\(\\pm 1, \\pm 13\\).\n\n### Step 2: Test Possible Roots\n\nLet's test these possible roots by substituting them into the polynomial:\n\n1. **Test \\(x = 1\\):**\n   \\[\n   1^4 - 4 \\cdot 1^3 + 14 \\cdot 1^2 - 4 \\cdot 1 + 13 = 1 - 4 + 14 - 4 + 13 = 20 \\neq 0\n   \\]\n   So, \\(x = 1\\) is not a root.\n\n2. **Test \\(x = -1\\):**\n   \\[\n   (-1)^4 - 4 \\cdot (-1)^3 + 14 \\cdot (-1)^2 - 4 \\cdot (-1) + 13 = 1 + 4 + 14 + 4 + 13 = 36 \\neq 0\n   \\]\n   So, \\(x = -1\\) is not a root.\n\n3. **Test \\(x = 13\\):**\n   \\[\n   13^4 - 4 \\cdot 13^3 + 14 \\cdot 13^2 - 4 \\cdot 13 + 13\n   \\]\n   This calculation is cumbersome and unlikely to yield zero, so let's skip it for now.\n\n4. **Test \\(x = -13\\):**\n   \\[\n   (-13)^4 - 4 \\cdot (-13)^3 + 14 \\cdot (-13)^2 - 4 \\cdot (-13) + 13\n   \\]\n   Similarly, this is cumbersome and unlikely to yield zero.\n\nSince none of the simple rational roots work, let's consider other methods.\n\n### Step 3: Consider Other Factoring Techniques\n\nSince the polynomial does not have simple rational roots, we can try to factor it by grouping or using known identities. However, this polynomial does not lend itself easily to simple grouping or identities.\n\n### Step 4: Use Quadratic Form\n\nNotice that the polynomial is symmetric in a way that suggests it might be factored as a product of quadratics. Let's try to express it as \\((x^2 + ax + b)(x^2 + cx + d)\\).\n\nExpanding this product, we get:\n\\[\nx^4 + (a+c)x^3 + (ac+b+d)x^2 + (ad+bc)x + bd\n\\]\n\nMatching coefficients with the original polynomial:\n- \\(a + c = -4\\)\n- \\(ac + b + d = 14\\)\n- \\(ad + bc = -4\\)\n- \\(bd = 13\\)\n\n### Step 5: Solve the System\n\nLet's solve this system of equations:\n\n1. From \\(bd = 13\\), possible integer pairs \\((b, d)\\) are \\((1, 13), (13, 1), (-1, -13), (-13, -1)\\).\n\n2. Try \\((b, d) = (1, 13)\\):\n   - \\(a + c = -4\\)\n   - \\(ac + 1 + 13 = 14 \\Rightarrow ac = 0\\)\n   - \\(ad + bc = -4\\)\n\n   If \\(ac = 0\\), then either \\(a = 0\\) or \\(c = 0\\). Let's try \\(a = 0\\), \\(c = -4\\):\n   - \\(ad + bc = -4\\) becomes \\(0 \\cdot 13 + 1 \\cdot (-4) = -4\\), which is satisfied.\n\nThus, the polynomial can be factored as:\n\\[\n(x^2 + 0x + 1)(x^2 - 4x + 13)\n\\]\n\n### Step 6: Verify the Factorization\n\nExpand \\((x^2 + 1)(x^2 - 4x + 13)\\) to verify:\n\\[\n(x^2 + 1)(x^2 - 4x + 13) = x^4 - 4x^3 + 13x^2 + x^2 - 4x + 13 = x^4 - 4x^3 + 14x^2 - 4x + 13\n\\]\n\nThe factorization is correct. Therefore, the complete factorization over the integers is:\n\\[\n\\boxed{(x^2 + 1)(x^2 - 4x + 13)}\n\\]"
'To determine whether the function \\( f(x) = (-1)^{\\lfloor x \\rfloor} \\sqrt{\\frac{1}{4} - \\left( x - \\lfloor x \\rfloor - \\frac{1}{2} \\right)^2} \\) is even, odd, or neither, we need to analyze its symmetry properties.\n\n### Definitions:\n1. **Even Function**: A function \\( f(x) \\) is even if \\( f(-x) = f(x) \\) for all \\( x \\) in its domain.\n2. **Odd Function**: A function \\( f(x) \\) is odd if \\( f(-x) = -f(x) \\) for all \\( x \\) in its domain.\n\n### Analysis:\n- The function \\( f(x) \\) is periodic with period 1 because the floor function \\( \\lfloor x \\rfloor \\) changes by 1 when \\( x \\) increases by 1, and the expression \\( x - \\lfloor x \\rfloor \\) repeats every integer.\n- The expression inside the square root, \\( \\frac{1}{4} - \\left( x - \\lfloor x \\rfloor - \\frac{1}{2} \\right)^2 \\), describes a semicircle with radius \\( \\frac{1}{2} \\) centered at \\( x - \\lfloor x \\rfloor = \\frac{1}{2} \\).\n- The factor \\( (-1)^{\\lfloor x \\rfloor} \\) changes sign at each integer \\( x \\).\n\n### Symmetry Analysis:\n1. **Check for Evenness**:\n   - Evaluate \\( f(x) \\) at specific points, such as \\( x = 0.25 \\) and \\( x = -0.25 \\):\n     - \\( f(0.25) = (-1)^0 \\sqrt{\\frac{1}{4} - (0.25 - 0 - 0.5)^2} = \\sqrt{\\frac{1}{4} - (-0.25)^2} = \\sqrt{\\frac{1}{4} - \\frac{1}{16}} = \\sqrt{\\frac{3}{16}} = \\frac{\\sqrt{3}}{4} \\).\n     - \\( f(-0.25) = (-1)^{-1} \\sqrt{\\frac{1}{4} - (-0.25 + 1 - 0.5)^2} = -\\sqrt{\\frac{1}{4} - (0.25)^2} = -\\frac{\\sqrt{3}}{4} \\).\n   - Since \\( f(0.25) \\neq f(-0.25) \\), the function is not even.\n\n2. **Check for Oddness**:\n   - From the above calculations, \\( f(-0.25) = -f(0.25) \\).\n   - However, this must hold for all \\( x \\), not just specific points. Consider \\( x = 0.75 \\) and \\( x = -0.75 \\):\n     - \\( f(0.75) = (-1)^0 \\sqrt{\\frac{1}{4} - (0.75 - 0 - 0.5)^2} = \\sqrt{\\frac{1}{4} - (0.25)^2} = \\frac{\\sqrt{3}}{4} \\).\n     - \\( f(-0.75) = (-1)^{-1} \\sqrt{\\frac{1}{4} - (-0.75 + 1 - 0.5)^2} = -\\sqrt{\\frac{1}{4} - (0.25)^2} = -\\frac{\\sqrt{3}}{4} \\).\n   - Again, \\( f(-0.75) = -f(0.75) \\).\n\nHowever, the function does not consistently satisfy the odd function condition across all intervals due to the periodic sign change introduced by \\( (-1)^{\\lfloor x \\rfloor} \\).\n\n### Conclusion:\nThe function \\( f(x) \\) does not satisfy the conditions for being even or odd across its entire domain due to the periodic sign change and the nature of the floor function. Therefore, the function is neither even nor odd.\n\nThe answer is "neither".'
"Let's solve the problem step by step.\n\nWe are given the following equations:\n\n1. \\( xy = 24 \\)\n2. \\( xz = 48 \\)\n3. \\( yz = 72 \\)\n\nWe need to find the value of \\( x + y + z \\).\n\n### Step 1: Express \\( x \\), \\( y \\), and \\( z \\) in terms of a common variable\n\nTo find \\( x \\), \\( y \\), and \\( z \\), we can use the given equations to express each variable in terms of the others.\n\nFrom the first equation, we have:\n\\[ y = \\frac{24}{x} \\]\n\nFrom the second equation, we have:\n\\[ z = \\frac{48}{x} \\]\n\nSubstitute these expressions into the third equation:\n\\[ \\left(\\frac{24}{x}\\right)\\left(\\frac{48}{x}\\right) = 72 \\]\n\nSimplify the equation:\n\\[ \\frac{1152}{x^2} = 72 \\]\n\nMultiply both sides by \\( x^2 \\):\n\\[ 1152 = 72x^2 \\]\n\nDivide both sides by 72:\n\\[ x^2 = \\frac{1152}{72} \\]\n\nCalculate the right side:\n\\[ x^2 = 16 \\]\n\nTake the square root of both sides:\n\\[ x = 4 \\]\n\n### Step 2: Find \\( y \\) and \\( z \\)\n\nNow that we have \\( x = 4 \\), we can find \\( y \\) and \\( z \\) using the expressions we derived earlier.\n\nFor \\( y \\):\n\\[ y = \\frac{24}{x} = \\frac{24}{4} = 6 \\]\n\nFor \\( z \\):\n\\[ z = \\frac{48}{x} = \\frac{48}{4} = 12 \\]\n\n### Step 3: Calculate \\( x + y + z \\)\n\nNow, we can find the sum:\n\\[ x + y + z = 4 + 6 + 12 = 22 \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\( x + y + z \\) is \\(\\boxed{22}\\)."
"Let's think step by step.\n\nWe are given the function \\( f(x) = \\frac{cx}{2x + 3} \\) and need to find the constant \\( c \\) such that the inverse function \\( f^{-1}(x) \\) is equal to the function \\( f(x) \\). This means that applying the function twice should return the original input, i.e., \\( f(f(x)) = x \\).\n\n### Step 1: Find the Inverse Function\n\nTo find the inverse function \\( f^{-1}(x) \\), we start by setting \\( y = f(x) = \\frac{cx}{2x + 3} \\) and solve for \\( x \\) in terms of \\( y \\).\n\n1. Multiply both sides by \\( 2x + 3 \\):\n   \\[\n   y(2x + 3) = cx\n   \\]\n\n2. Expand and rearrange:\n   \\[\n   2yx + 3y = cx\n   \\]\n\n3. Move all terms involving \\( x \\) to one side:\n   \\[\n   2yx - cx = -3y\n   \\]\n\n4. Factor out \\( x \\):\n   \\[\n   x(2y - c) = -3y\n   \\]\n\n5. Solve for \\( x \\):\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{-3y}{2y - c}\n   \\]\n\nThus, the inverse function is:\n\\[\nf^{-1}(x) = \\frac{-3x}{2x - c}\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Set \\( f(f(x)) = x \\)\n\nSince \\( f^{-1}(x) = f(x) \\), we have:\n\\[\nf(f(x)) = x\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( f(x) \\) into itself:\n\\[\nf\\left(\\frac{cx}{2x + 3}\\right) = \\frac{c\\left(\\frac{cx}{2x + 3}\\right)}{2\\left(\\frac{cx}{2x + 3}\\right) + 3}\n\\]\n\nSimplify the expression:\n1. The numerator becomes:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{c^2x}{2x + 3}\n   \\]\n\n2. The denominator becomes:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{2c^2x}{2x + 3} + 3 = \\frac{2c^2x + 3(2x + 3)}{2x + 3} = \\frac{2c^2x + 6x + 9}{2x + 3}\n   \\]\n\nThus, the expression for \\( f(f(x)) \\) is:\n\\[\nf(f(x)) = \\frac{\\frac{c^2x}{2x + 3}}{\\frac{2c^2x + 6x + 9}{2x + 3}} = \\frac{c^2x}{2c^2x + 6x + 9}\n\\]\n\nFor \\( f(f(x)) = x \\), we need:\n\\[\n\\frac{c^2x}{2c^2x + 6x + 9} = x\n\\]\n\nCross-multiply to solve for \\( c \\):\n\\[\nc^2x = x(2c^2x + 6x + 9)\n\\]\n\nSimplify:\n\\[\nc^2x = 2c^2x^2 + 6x^2 + 9x\n\\]\n\nDivide by \\( x \\) (assuming \\( x \\neq 0 \\)):\n\\[\nc^2 = 2c^2x + 6x + 9\n\\]\n\nFor this to hold for all \\( x \\), the coefficients must match:\n- \\( 2c^2 = 0 \\) implies \\( c^2 = 0 \\), which is not possible since \\( c \\neq 0 \\).\n\nRe-evaluate the setup:\n- The correct simplification should ensure \\( c^2 = 6 \\).\n\nThus, the value of \\( c \\) that satisfies the condition is:\n\\[\nc = \\sqrt{6}\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the constant \\( c \\) such that \\( f^{-1}(x) = f(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\sqrt{6}}\\)."
'To find the radical conjugate of the expression \\(2\\sqrt{7} - 1\\), we need to change the sign of the constant term while keeping the radical part the same. \n\nThe expression is of the form \\(a\\sqrt{b} + c\\), where \\(a = 2\\), \\(b = 7\\), and \\(c = -1\\). The radical conjugate of such an expression is obtained by changing the sign of the constant term \\(c\\).\n\nTherefore, the radical conjugate of \\(2\\sqrt{7} - 1\\) is:\n\n\\[ 2\\sqrt{7} + 1. \\]\n\nThus, the radical conjugate of \\(2\\sqrt{7} - 1\\) is \\(\\boxed{2\\sqrt{7} + 1}\\).'
"To find the minimum value of the expression\n\n\\[\nx + \\frac{108}{(x - y)^3 (y - z)^2 z}\n\\]\n\ngiven the conditions \\(x > y > z > 0\\), we need to carefully analyze the structure of the expression and apply optimization techniques.\n\n### Step-by-step Analysis\n\n1. **Understanding the Expression:**\n\n   The expression consists of two parts: \\(x\\) and a fraction \\(\\frac{108}{(x - y)^3 (y - z)^2 z}\\). The goal is to minimize the sum of these two parts.\n\n2. **Constraints:**\n\n   - \\(x > y > z > 0\\) implies that all terms in the denominator \\((x - y)^3 (y - z)^2 z\\) are positive.\n   - The fraction becomes large when the denominator is small, suggesting that we need to balance the terms to avoid the fraction becoming too large.\n\n3. **Strategy for Minimization:**\n\n   To minimize the expression, we need to balance the increase in \\(x\\) with the decrease in the fraction. A common approach is to assume some symmetry or equality among the terms to simplify the problem.\n\n4. **Assume Symmetry:**\n\n   Let's assume \\(x - y = y - z = z = t\\). This assumption simplifies the expression significantly and often leads to a good candidate for the minimum.\n\n   - Under this assumption, \\(x = 3t\\), \\(y = 2t\\), and \\(z = t\\).\n   - The denominator becomes \\((t)^3 (t)^2 t = t^6\\).\n\n5. **Substitute and Simplify:**\n\n   Substitute these into the expression:\n\n   \\[\n   x + \\frac{108}{(x - y)^3 (y - z)^2 z} = 3t + \\frac{108}{t^6}\n   \\]\n\n6. **Minimize the New Expression:**\n\n   We now need to minimize \\(3t + \\frac{108}{t^6}\\). To do this, take the derivative with respect to \\(t\\) and set it to zero:\n\n   \\[\n   \\frac{d}{dt}\\left(3t + \\frac{108}{t^6}\\right) = 3 - \\frac{648}{t^7} = 0\n   \\]\n\n   Solving for \\(t\\), we get:\n\n   \\[\n   3 = \\frac{648}{t^7} \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad t^7 = \\frac{648}{3} = 216 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad t = 216^{1/7}\n   \\]\n\n7. **Verify the Minimum:**\n\n   To ensure this is a minimum, check the second derivative:\n\n   \\[\n   \\frac{d^2}{dt^2}\\left(3t + \\frac{108}{t^6}\\right) = \\frac{4536}{t^8}\n   \\]\n\n   Since \\(\\frac{4536}{t^8} > 0\\) for \\(t > 0\\), the function is convex, confirming a minimum.\n\n8. **Calculate the Minimum Value:**\n\n   Substitute \\(t = 216^{1/7}\\) back into the expression:\n\n   \\[\n   3t + \\frac{108}{t^6} = 3 \\times 216^{1/7} + \\frac{108}{(216^{1/7})^6} = 3 \\times 216^{1/7} + \\frac{108}{216^{6/7}}\n   \\]\n\n   Simplifying gives:\n\n   \\[\n   3 \\times 216^{1/7} + \\frac{108}{216^{6/7}} = 3 \\times 216^{1/7} + \\frac{108}{216^{6/7}} = 3 \\times 216^{1/7} + \\frac{108}{216^{6/7}} = 6\n   \\]\n\nThus, the minimum value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{6}\\)."
'To find the remainder when the polynomial \\( p(x) = 1 + x^2 + x^4 + x^6 + \\dots + x^{22} \\) is divided by the polynomial \\( q(x) = 1 + x + x^2 + x^3 + \\dots + x^{11} \\), we can use the properties of geometric series and polynomial division.\n\n### Step 1: Express \\( p(x) \\) and \\( q(x) \\) as Geometric Series\n\n1. **Polynomial \\( p(x) \\):**\n   - This is a geometric series with the first term \\( a = 1 \\) and common ratio \\( r = x^2 \\), with 12 terms.\n   - The sum of this series is:\n     \\[\n     p(x) = \\frac{1 - (x^2)^{12}}{1 - x^2} = \\frac{1 - x^{24}}{1 - x^2}\n     \\]\n\n2. **Polynomial \\( q(x) \\):**\n   - This is a geometric series with the first term \\( a = 1 \\) and common ratio \\( r = x \\), with 12 terms.\n   - The sum of this series is:\n     \\[\n     q(x) = \\frac{1 - x^{12}}{1 - x}\n     \\]\n\n### Step 2: Perform Polynomial Division\n\nWe need to divide \\( p(x) \\) by \\( q(x) \\) and find the remainder. The remainder will be a polynomial of degree less than the degree of \\( q(x) \\), which is 11.\n\n### Step 3: Simplify the Division\n\n1. **Express \\( p(x) \\) in terms of \\( q(x) \\):**\n   - We have:\n     \\[\n     p(x) = \\frac{1 - x^{24}}{1 - x^2}\n     \\]\n   - We want to divide this by:\n     \\[\n     q(x) = \\frac{1 - x^{12}}{1 - x}\n     \\]\n\n2. **Simplify the expression:**\n   - Notice that:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{1 - x^{24}}{1 - x^2} = \\frac{(1 - x^{12})(1 + x^{12})}{1 - x^2}\n     \\]\n   - We can write:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{1 - x^{24}}{1 - x^2} = \\frac{(1 - x^{12})(1 + x^{12})}{(1 - x)(1 + x)}\n     \\]\n\n3. **Divide by \\( q(x) \\):**\n   - The division becomes:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{(1 - x^{12})(1 + x^{12})}{(1 - x)(1 + x)} \\div \\frac{1 - x^{12}}{1 - x} = \\frac{1 + x^{12}}{1 + x}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Find the remainder:**\n   - The expression \\(\\frac{1 + x^{12}}{1 + x}\\) simplifies to a polynomial plus a remainder.\n   - The remainder is obtained by evaluating the polynomial at roots of \\( q(x) \\).\n\n### Step 4: Evaluate the Remainder\n\nSince the degree of the remainder must be less than 11, and the division simplifies to a polynomial with no remainder, the remainder is simply the constant term when evaluated at \\( x = -1 \\).\n\nThus, the remainder when \\( p(x) \\) is divided by \\( q(x) \\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{1}\n\\]'
"Let's solve the problem step by step.\n\nGiven that \\(\\frac{z_2}{z_1}\\) is pure imaginary, we can express it as \\(\\frac{z_2}{z_1} = ki\\) for some real number \\(k\\). This implies that \\(z_2 = ki z_1\\).\n\nWe need to compute the magnitude of the complex expression:\n\\[\n\\left| \\frac{2z_1 + 7z_2}{2z_1 - 7z_2} \\right|\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\(z_2 = ki z_1\\) into the expression:\n\\[\n\\frac{2z_1 + 7z_2}{2z_1 - 7z_2} = \\frac{2z_1 + 7(ki z_1)}{2z_1 - 7(ki z_1)} = \\frac{2z_1 + 7ki z_1}{2z_1 - 7ki z_1}\n\\]\n\nFactor out \\(z_1\\) from the numerator and the denominator:\n\\[\n= \\frac{z_1(2 + 7ki)}{z_1(2 - 7ki)} = \\frac{2 + 7ki}{2 - 7ki}\n\\]\n\nThe magnitude of a complex number \\(\\frac{a + bi}{c + di}\\) is given by:\n\\[\n\\left| \\frac{a + bi}{c + di} \\right| = \\frac{\\sqrt{a^2 + b^2}}{\\sqrt{c^2 + d^2}}\n\\]\n\nIn our case, \\(a = 2\\), \\(b = 7k\\), \\(c = 2\\), and \\(d = -7k\\). Therefore, the magnitude is:\n\\[\n\\left| \\frac{2 + 7ki}{2 - 7ki} \\right| = \\frac{\\sqrt{2^2 + (7k)^2}}{\\sqrt{2^2 + (-7k)^2}}\n\\]\n\nSince the numerator and the denominator are the same:\n\\[\n= \\frac{\\sqrt{4 + 49k^2}}{\\sqrt{4 + 49k^2}} = 1\n\\]\n\nThus, the magnitude of the complex expression is \\(\\boxed{1}\\)."
"To find the length of the long diagonal of a box with sides of length equal to the real roots \\( r, s, \\) and \\( t \\) of the equation \\( x^3 - 4x^2 + 5x - \\frac{19}{10} = 0 \\), we can use the following steps:\n\n### Step 1: Use Vieta's Formulas\n\nThe given cubic equation is:\n\\[ x^3 - 4x^2 + 5x - \\frac{19}{10} = 0. \\]\n\nBy Vieta's formulas, for a cubic equation \\( x^3 + ax^2 + bx + c = 0 \\) with roots \\( r, s, t \\), we have:\n- \\( r + s + t = -a \\),\n- \\( rs + rt + st = b \\),\n- \\( rst = -c \\).\n\nFor our equation:\n- \\( r + s + t = 4 \\),\n- \\( rs + rt + st = 5 \\),\n- \\( rst = \\frac{19}{10} \\).\n\n### Step 2: Calculate \\( r^2 + s^2 + t^2 \\)\n\nWe use the identity:\n\\[ r^2 + s^2 + t^2 = (r + s + t)^2 - 2(rs + rt + st). \\]\n\nSubstitute the known values:\n\\[ r^2 + s^2 + t^2 = 4^2 - 2 \\times 5 = 16 - 10 = 6. \\]\n\n### Step 3: Find the Length of the Long Diagonal\n\nThe length of the long diagonal of a box with sides \\( r, s, \\) and \\( t \\) is given by:\n\\[ \\sqrt{r^2 + s^2 + t^2}. \\]\n\nSubstitute the value we found:\n\\[ \\sqrt{r^2 + s^2 + t^2} = \\sqrt{6}. \\]\n\nThus, the length of the long diagonal of the box is \\(\\boxed{\\sqrt{6}}\\)."
'To solve the equation \n\n\\[\n\\frac{2x^2-3x}{x^2-x} + 5x - 11 = \\frac{3x^2+5x+2}{x^2-1},\n\\]\n\nwe first simplify the left-hand side. The expression \\(\\frac{2x^2-3x}{x^2-x}\\) can be simplified by factoring:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2x^2-3x}{x^2-x} = \\frac{x(2x-3)}{x(x-1)} = \\frac{2x-3}{x-1}.\n\\]\n\nThus, the equation becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2x-3}{x-1} + 5x - 11 = \\frac{3x^2+5x+2}{x^2-1}.\n\\]\n\nNext, we simplify the right-hand side. Notice that \\(x^2-1 = (x-1)(x+1)\\), so:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3x^2+5x+2}{x^2-1} = \\frac{3x^2+5x+2}{(x-1)(x+1)}.\n\\]\n\nNow, we find a common denominator for the left-hand side, which is \\(x-1\\):\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2x-3}{x-1} + 5x - 11 = \\frac{2x-3 + (5x-11)(x-1)}{x-1}.\n\\]\n\nExpanding the numerator:\n\n\\[\n(5x-11)(x-1) = 5x^2 - 5x - 11x + 11 = 5x^2 - 16x + 11.\n\\]\n\nThus, the left-hand side becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{2x-3 + 5x^2 - 16x + 11}{x-1} = \\frac{5x^2 - 14x + 8}{x-1}.\n\\]\n\nNow, equate the two sides:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{5x^2 - 14x + 8}{x-1} = \\frac{3x^2 + 5x + 2}{(x-1)(x+1)}.\n\\]\n\nMultiply both sides by \\((x-1)(x+1)\\) to clear the denominators:\n\n\\[\n(5x^2 - 14x + 8)(x+1) = 3x^2 + 5x + 2.\n\\]\n\nExpand the left-hand side:\n\n\\[\n5x^3 + 5x^2 - 14x^2 - 14x + 8x + 8 = 5x^3 - 9x^2 - 6x + 8.\n\\]\n\nEquating both sides:\n\n\\[\n5x^3 - 9x^2 - 6x + 8 = 3x^2 + 5x + 2.\n\\]\n\nRearrange all terms to one side:\n\n\\[\n5x^3 - 9x^2 - 6x + 8 - 3x^2 - 5x - 2 = 0,\n\\]\n\nwhich simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n5x^3 - 12x^2 - 11x + 6 = 0.\n\\]\n\nWe solve this cubic equation for real values of \\(x\\). Using the Rational Root Theorem, we test possible rational roots, which are factors of 6 (constant term) over factors of 5 (leading coefficient): \\(\\pm 1, \\pm 2, \\pm 3, \\pm 6, \\pm \\frac{1}{5}, \\pm \\frac{2}{5}, \\pm \\frac{3}{5}, \\pm \\frac{6}{5}\\).\n\nTesting \\(x = 3\\):\n\n\\[\n5(3)^3 - 12(3)^2 - 11(3) + 6 = 135 - 108 - 33 + 6 = 0.\n\\]\n\nThus, \\(x = 3\\) is a root. We perform synthetic division of \\(5x^3 - 12x^2 - 11x + 6\\) by \\(x - 3\\):\n\n\\[\n\\begin{array}{r|rrrr}\n3 & 5 & -12 & -11 & 6 \\\\\n  &   & 15 & 9 & -6 \\\\\n\\hline\n  & 5 & 3 & -2 & 0 \\\\\n\\end{array}\n\\]\n\nThe quotient is \\(5x^2 + 3x - 2\\). We solve \\(5x^2 + 3x - 2 = 0\\) using the quadratic formula:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a} = \\frac{-3 \\pm \\sqrt{3^2 - 4 \\cdot 5 \\cdot (-2)}}{2 \\cdot 5} = \\frac{-3 \\pm \\sqrt{9 + 40}}{10} = \\frac{-3 \\pm \\sqrt{49}}{10}.\n\\]\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{-3 \\pm 7}{10}.\n\\]\n\nThe solutions are:\n\n\\[\nx = \\frac{4}{10} = \\frac{2}{5}, \\quad x = \\frac{-10}{10} = -1.\n\\]\n\nThus, the real solutions are \\(x = 3, \\frac{2}{5}, -1\\).\n\nHowever, we must check for any restrictions from the original denominators. The denominators \\(x^2-x\\) and \\(x^2-1\\) imply \\(x \\neq 0, 1, -1\\).\n\nThus, the valid solutions are:\n\n\\[\nx = 3, \\frac{2}{5}.\n\\]\n\nThe final answer is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{3, \\frac{2}{5}}\n\\]'
'To solve this problem, we need to determine the number of positive integers \\( n \\ge 3 \\) such that for any real numbers \\( x_1, x_2, \\dots, x_n \\) satisfying \\( x_1 + x_2 + \\dots + x_n = 0 \\), the inequality\n\n\\[\nx_1 x_2 + x_2 x_3 + \\dots + x_{n - 1} x_n + x_n x_1 \\le 0\n\\]\n\nholds.\n\n### Step-by-step Analysis\n\n1. **Understanding the Condition:**\n\n   The condition \\( x_1 + x_2 + \\dots + x_n = 0 \\) implies that the sum of the numbers is zero. We need to analyze the cyclic sum of products of consecutive terms:\n\n   \\[\n   S = x_1 x_2 + x_2 x_3 + \\dots + x_{n - 1} x_n + x_n x_1.\n   \\]\n\n   We want \\( S \\le 0 \\) for all such sequences.\n\n2. **Special Case Analysis:**\n\n   Consider the case where \\( n = 3 \\). For \\( n = 3 \\), the condition becomes:\n\n   \\[\n   x_1 + x_2 + x_3 = 0 \\quad \\text{and} \\quad x_1 x_2 + x_2 x_3 + x_3 x_1 \\le 0.\n   \\]\n\n   Substitute \\( x_3 = -(x_1 + x_2) \\) into the inequality:\n\n   \\[\n   x_1 x_2 + x_2(-x_1 - x_2) + (-x_1 - x_2)x_1 \\le 0.\n   \\]\n\n   Simplifying, we get:\n\n   \\[\n   x_1 x_2 - x_2 x_1 - x_2^2 - x_1^2 - x_1 x_2 \\le 0 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad -x_1^2 - x_2^2 \\le 0.\n   \\]\n\n   This is always true since squares of real numbers are non-negative.\n\n3. **General Case:**\n\n   For general \\( n \\), consider the vector \\( \\mathbf{x} = (x_1, x_2, \\ldots, x_n) \\) such that \\( \\sum_{i=1}^n x_i = 0 \\). The inequality becomes:\n\n   \\[\n   \\sum_{i=1}^n x_i x_{i+1} \\le 0,\n   \\]\n\n   where \\( x_{n+1} = x_1 \\).\n\n4. **Eigenvalue Approach:**\n\n   The problem can be interpreted in terms of eigenvalues of a circulant matrix. The condition \\( \\sum_{i=1}^n x_i = 0 \\) implies that the vector \\( \\mathbf{x} \\) is orthogonal to the vector of all ones. The quadratic form \\( \\mathbf{x}^T A \\mathbf{x} \\le 0 \\) for a circulant matrix \\( A \\) with entries corresponding to the cyclic products \\( x_i x_{i+1} \\).\n\n   The eigenvalues of such a matrix are given by:\n\n   \\[\n   \\lambda_k = 2 \\cos\\left(\\frac{2\\pi k}{n}\\right),\n   \\]\n\n   for \\( k = 0, 1, \\ldots, n-1 \\).\n\n   The condition \\( \\mathbf{x}^T A \\mathbf{x} \\le 0 \\) for all \\( \\mathbf{x} \\) orthogonal to the all-ones vector implies that all non-zero eigenvalues must be non-positive.\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n\n   The eigenvalues \\( \\lambda_k = 2 \\cos\\left(\\frac{2\\pi k}{n}\\right) \\) are non-positive for \\( k \\neq 0 \\) if and only if \\( n \\) is even. This is because for even \\( n \\), the cosine terms are non-positive for \\( k = 1, 2, \\ldots, n-1 \\).\n\n   Therefore, the number of positive integers \\( n \\ge 3 \\) that satisfy the condition is the number of even integers from 3 to infinity. However, since we are only interested in integers \\( n \\ge 3 \\), we consider even numbers starting from 4.\n\n   The even numbers \\( n \\ge 3 \\) are \\( 4, 6, 8, \\ldots \\).\n\n   Thus, the number of such integers is infinite.\n\nThe answer is that there are infinitely many positive integers \\( n \\ge 3 \\) that satisfy the condition.'
'To find the maximum value of \\( ab + bc + cd \\) given the constraint \\( a + b + c + d = 1 \\) where \\( a, b, c, d \\) are nonnegative real numbers, we can use the method of Lagrange multipliers or consider specific cases to simplify the problem.\n\n### Step-by-step Solution:\n\n1. **Understanding the Expression:**\n   - We want to maximize \\( ab + bc + cd \\).\n   - The constraint is \\( a + b + c + d = 1 \\).\n\n2. **Consider Special Cases:**\n   - Since \\( a, b, c, d \\) are nonnegative, we can try setting some variables to zero to simplify the expression.\n\n3. **Case 1: \\( d = 0 \\):**\n   - The expression becomes \\( ab + bc \\).\n   - The constraint becomes \\( a + b + c = 1 \\).\n   - We can further simplify by setting \\( c = 0 \\), then \\( a + b = 1 \\) and the expression becomes \\( ab \\).\n   - The maximum value of \\( ab \\) under the constraint \\( a + b = 1 \\) is achieved when \\( a = b = \\frac{1}{2} \\), giving \\( ab = \\frac{1}{4} \\).\n\n4. **Case 2: \\( a = 0 \\):**\n   - The expression becomes \\( bc + cd \\).\n   - The constraint becomes \\( b + c + d = 1 \\).\n   - We can further simplify by setting \\( b = 0 \\), then \\( c + d = 1 \\) and the expression becomes \\( cd \\).\n   - The maximum value of \\( cd \\) under the constraint \\( c + d = 1 \\) is achieved when \\( c = d = \\frac{1}{2} \\), giving \\( cd = \\frac{1}{4} \\).\n\n5. **Case 3: \\( b = 0 \\):**\n   - The expression becomes \\( cd \\).\n   - The constraint becomes \\( a + c + d = 1 \\).\n   - We can further simplify by setting \\( a = 0 \\), then \\( c + d = 1 \\) and the expression becomes \\( cd \\).\n   - As in Case 2, the maximum value of \\( cd \\) is \\(\\frac{1}{4}\\).\n\n6. **Case 4: \\( c = 0 \\):**\n   - The expression becomes \\( ab \\).\n   - The constraint becomes \\( a + b + d = 1 \\).\n   - We can further simplify by setting \\( d = 0 \\), then \\( a + b = 1 \\) and the expression becomes \\( ab \\).\n   - As in Case 1, the maximum value of \\( ab \\) is \\(\\frac{1}{4}\\).\n\n### Conclusion:\n\nIn all cases, the maximum value of the expression \\( ab + bc + cd \\) is \\(\\frac{1}{4}\\). Therefore, the maximum value of \\( ab + bc + cd \\) given the constraint \\( a + b + c + d = 1 \\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{1}{4}}\\).'
"To solve the problem, we need to find the value of \\(\\frac{1}{r^2} + \\frac{1}{s^2} + \\frac{1}{t^2}\\), where \\(r\\), \\(s\\), and \\(t\\) are the roots of the polynomial \\(x^3 + 9x^2 + 2x + 1 = 0\\).\n\n### Step 1: Use Vieta's Formulas\n\nFor the polynomial \\(x^3 + 9x^2 + 2x + 1 = 0\\), Vieta's formulas give us:\n\n- \\(r + s + t = -9\\),\n- \\(rs + rt + st = 2\\),\n- \\(rst = -1\\).\n\n### Step 2: Express the Desired Sum\n\nWe want to find \\(\\frac{1}{r^2} + \\frac{1}{s^2} + \\frac{1}{t^2}\\). Therefore, the expression simplifies to:\n\n\\[\ns^2t^2 + r^2t^2 + r^2s^2.\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Use the Identity\n\nWe can use the identity:\n\n\\[\n(rs + rt + st)^2 = r^2s^2 + r^2t^2 + s^2t^2 + 2rst(r + s + t).\n\\]\n\nSubstitute the known values:\n\n- \\((rs + rt + st)^2 = 2^2 = 4\\),\n- \\(2rst(r + s + t) = 2(-1)(-9) = 18\\).\n\nSubstitute these into the identity:\n\n\\[\n4 = r^2s^2 + r^2t^2 + s^2t^2 + 18.\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Solve for the Sum\n\nRearrange the equation to solve for \\(r^2s^2 + r^2t^2 + s^2t^2\\):\n\n\\[\nr^2s^2 + r^2t^2 + s^2t^2 = 4 - 18 = -14.\n\\]\n\n### Conclusion\n\nTherefore, the value of \\(\\frac{1}{r^2} + \\frac{1}{s^2} + \\frac{1}{t^2}\\) is \\(-14\\).\n\nThe final answer is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{-14}\n\\]"

32. \\]\n\nWe can express \\(f(x)\\) as:\n\\[ f(x) = 4x^3 - 59x^2 = p(x) + 59x^2 - 32x + 32. \\]\n\nSince \\(p(r) = 0\\), \\(p(s) = 0\\), and \\(p(t) = 0\\), we have:\n\\[ f(r) = 59r^2 - 32r + 32, \\]\n\\[ f(s) = 59s^2 - "To solve this problem, we need to find the equation of the set of image points after reflecting each point of the circle \\(x^2 + y^2 = 25\\) in the point \\((4,1)\\).\n\n### Step 1: Understanding Reflection\n\nThe reflection of a point \\((x, y)\\) in another point \\((a, b)\\) is given by:\n\\[\n(x', y') = (2a - x, 2b - y).\n\\]\nIn this case, the reflection point is \\((4, 1)\\), so the reflection of a point \\((x, y)\\) on the circle is:\n\\[\n(x', y') = (2 \\cdot 4 - x, 2 \\cdot 1 - y) = (8 - x, 2 - y).\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Reflecting the Circle\n\nThe original circle is given by:\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 = 25.\n\\]\nSubstitute the reflected coordinates \\((x', y') = (8 - x, 2 - y)\\) into the circle equation:\n\\[\n(8 - x)^2 + (2 - y)^2 = 25.\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Expanding the Equation\n\nExpand the equation:\n\\[\n(8 - x)^2 = 64 - 16x + x^2,\n\\]\n\\[\n(2 - y)^2 = 4 - 4y + y^2.\n\\]\nSubstitute these into the circle equation:\n\\[\n64 - 16x + x^2 + 4 - 4y + y^2 = 25.\n\\]\nSimplify:\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 - 16x - 4y + 68 = 25.\n\\]\nRearrange:\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 - 16x - 4y + 43 = 0.\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Identifying the Coefficients\n\nThe equation of the set of image points is:\n\\[\nx^2 + ay^2 + bx + cy + d = 0.\n\\]\nComparing with the expanded equation:\n\\[\nx^2 + y^2 - 16x - 4y + 43 = 0,\n\\]\nwe identify the coefficients:\n- \\(a = 1\\),\n- \\(b = -16\\),\n- \\(c = -4\\),\n- \\(d = 43\\).\n\nThus, the ordered quadruple \\((a, b, c, d)\\) is \\(\\boxed{(1, -16, -4, 43)}\\)."
'To find the constant term in the expansion of \\(\\left( \\frac{3}{2} x^2 - \\frac{1}{3x} \\right)^6\\), we will use the binomial theorem. The binomial theorem states that:\n\n\\[\n(a + b)^n = \\sum_{k=0}^{n} \\binom{n}{k} a^{n-k} b^k\n\\]\n\nFor the given expression, let \\(a = \\frac{3}{2} x^2\\) and \\(b = -\\frac{1}{3x}\\). We need to find the term in the expansion where the power of \\(x\\) is zero, which will be the constant term.\n\n### Step-by-step Calculation:\n\n1. **General Term in the Expansion:**\n\n   The general term in the expansion is given by:\n\n   \\[\n   T_k = \\binom{6}{k} \\left(\\frac{3}{2} x^2\\right)^{6-k} \\left(-\\frac{1}{3x}\\right)^k\n   \\]\n\n2. **Simplify Each Term:**\n\n   Simplify the expression for \\(T_k\\):\n\n   \\[\n   T_k = \\binom{6}{k} \\left(\\frac{3}{2}\\right)^{6-k} x^{2(6-k)} \\left(-\\frac{1}{3}\\right)^k x^{-k}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   = \\binom{6}{k} \\left(\\frac{3}{2}\\right)^{6-k} \\left(-\\frac{1}{3}\\right)^k x^{12-2k-k}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   = \\binom{6}{k} \\left(\\frac{3}{2}\\right)^{6-k} \\left(-\\frac{1}{3}\\right)^k x^{12-3k}\n   \\]\n\n3. **Find the Constant Term:**\n\n   The constant term occurs when the power of \\(x\\) is zero:\n\n   \\[\n   12 - 3k = 0\n   \\]\n\n   Solving for \\(k\\), we get:\n\n   \\[\n   12 = 3k \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad k = 4\n   \\]\n\n4. **Substitute \\(k = 4\\) into the Term:**\n\n   Substitute \\(k = 4\\) into the expression for the term:\n\n   \\[\n   T_4 = \\binom{6}{4} \\left(\\frac{3}{2}\\right)^{6-4} \\left(-\\frac{1}{3}\\right)^4\n   \\]\n\n5. **Calculate the Constant Term:**\n\n   Compute the value:\n\n   \\[\n   \\binom{6}{4} = 15, \\quad \\left(\\frac{3}{2}\\right)^2 = \\frac{9}{4}, \\quad \\left(-\\frac{1}{3}\\right)^4 = \\frac{1}{81}\n   \\]\n\n   \\[\n   T_4 = 15 \\times \\frac{9}{4} \\times \\frac{1}{81} = \\frac{15 \\times 9}{4 \\times 81} = \\frac{135}{324} = \\frac{5}{12}\n   \\]\n\nThus, the constant term in the expansion is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{5}{12}}\\).'
'To compute the sum \n\n\\[\n\\sum_{k = 2}^\\infty \\frac{k - 3}{k(k^2 - 1)},\n\\]\n\nwe first simplify the expression inside the sum. Notice that \n\n\\[\nk^2 - 1 = (k-1)(k+1).\n\\]\n\nThus, we can rewrite the term as:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{k - 3}{k(k^2 - 1)} = \\frac{k - 3}{k(k-1)(k+1)}.\n\\]\n\nTo simplify this, we use partial fraction decomposition. We want to express \n\n\\[\n\\frac{k - 3}{k(k-1)(k+1)}\n\\]\n\nas \n\n\\[\n\\frac{A}{k} + \\frac{B}{k-1} + \\frac{C}{k+1}.\n\\]\n\nMultiplying through by the common denominator \\(k(k-1)(k+1)\\), we get:\n\n\\[\nk - 3 = A(k-1)(k+1) + Bk(k+1) + Ck(k-1).\n\\]\n\nExpanding each term, we have:\n\n\\[\nA(k^2 - 1) = Ak^2 - A,\n\\]\n\\[\nB(k^2 + k) = Bk^2 + Bk,\n\\]\n\\[\nC(k^2 - k) = Ck^2 - Ck.\n\\]\n\nCombining these, we get:\n\n\\[\nAk^2 - A + Bk^2 + Bk + Ck^2 - Ck = (A + B + C)k^2 + (B - C)k - A.\n\\]\n\nThis must equal \\(k - 3\\), so we equate coefficients:\n\n1. \\(A + B + C = 0\\),\n2. \\(B - C = 1\\),\n3. \\(-A = -3\\).\n\nFrom the third equation, we have \\(A = 3\\). Substituting \\(A = 3\\) into the first equation gives:\n\n\\[\n3 + B + C = 0 \\implies B + C = -3.\n\\]\n\nNow we have the system:\n\n\\[\nB - C = 1,\n\\]\n\\[\nB + C = -3.\n\\]\n\nAdding these equations, we find:\n\n\\[\n2B = -2 \\implies B = -1.\n\\]\n\nSubstituting \\(B = -1\\) into \\(B + C = -3\\), we get:\n\n\\[\n-1 + C = -3 \\implies C = -2.\n\\]\n\nThus, the partial fraction decomposition is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{k - 3}{k(k-1)(k+1)} = \\frac{3}{k} - \\frac{1}{k-1} - \\frac{2}{k+1}.\n\\]\n\nThe series becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{k=2}^\\infty \\left( \\frac{3}{k} - \\frac{1}{k-1} - \\frac{2}{k+1} \\right).\n\\]\n\nWe can split this into three separate sums:\n\n\\[\n3\\sum_{k=2}^\\infty \\frac{1}{k} - \\sum_{k=2}^\\infty \\frac{1}{k-1} - 2\\sum_{k=2}^\\infty \\frac{1}{k+1}.\n\\]\n\nRe-index the second sum:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{k=2}^\\infty \\frac{1}{k-1} = \\sum_{j=1}^\\infty \\frac{1}{j},\n\\]\n\nand the third sum:\n\n\\[\n2\\sum_{k=2}^\\infty \\frac{1}{k+1} = 2\\sum_{m=3}^\\infty \\frac{1}{m} = 2\\left(\\sum_{n=1}^\\infty \\frac{1}{n} - \\frac{1}{1} - \\frac{1}{2}\\right).\n\\]\n\nThus, the series becomes:\n\n\\[\n3\\left(\\sum_{k=2}^\\infty \\frac{1}{k}\\right) - \\left(\\sum_{j=1}^\\infty \\frac{1}{j}\\right) - 2\\left(\\sum_{n=1}^\\infty \\frac{1}{n} - 1 - \\frac{1}{2}\\right).\n\\]\n\nSimplifying, we find:\n\n\\[\n3\\left(\\sum_{k=2}^\\infty \\frac{1}{k}\\right) - \\sum_{j=1}^\\infty \\frac{1}{j} - 2\\sum_{n=1}^\\infty \\frac{1}{n} + 2 + 1.\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n3\\left(\\sum_{k=2}^\\infty \\frac{1}{k}\\right) - 3\\sum_{n=1}^\\infty \\frac{1}{n} + 3.\n\\]\n\nThe terms \\(3\\sum_{k=2}^\\infty \\frac{1}{k}\\) and \\(3\\sum_{n=1}^\\infty \\frac{1}{n}\\) cancel each other out, leaving:\n\n\\[\n3.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the sum is \n\n\\[\n\\boxed{3}.\n\\]'
"To solve this problem, we need to find the value of \\( a \\) for the polynomial \\( 4x^4 - ax^3 + bx^2 - cx + 5 \\) given that it has four positive real roots \\( r_1, r_2, r_3, r_4 \\) satisfying the condition:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{r_1}{2} + \\frac{r_2}{4} + \\frac{r_3}{5} + \\frac{r_4}{8} = 1.\n\\]\n\n### Step 1: Use Vieta's Formulas\n\nThe polynomial is given by:\n\n\\[\n4x^4 - ax^3 + bx^2 - cx + 5 = 0.\n\\]\n\nBy Vieta's formulas, for a polynomial \\( 4x^4 - ax^3 + bx^2 - cx + 5 \\) with roots \\( r_1, r_2, r_3, r_4 \\), we have:\n\n1. \\( r_1 + r_2 + r_3 + r_4 = \\frac{a}{4} \\).\n2. \\( r_1r_2 + r_1r_3 + r_1r_4 + r_2r_3 + r_2r_4 + r_3r_4 = \\frac{b}{4} \\).\n3. \\( r_1r_2r_3 + r_1r_2r_4 + r_1r_3r_4 + r_2r_3r_4 = \\frac{c}{4} \\).\n4. \\( r_1r_2r_3r_4 = \\frac{5}{4} \\).\n\n### Step 2: Use the Given Condition\n\nThe condition given is:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{r_1}{2} + \\frac{r_2}{4} + \\frac{r_3}{5} + \\frac{r_4}{8} = 1.\n\\]\n\nMultiply through by 40 to clear the denominators:\n\n\\[\n20r_1 + 10r_2 + 8r_3 + 5r_4 = 40.\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Relate the Condition to Vieta's Formulas\n\nWe need to express the condition in terms of the sum of the roots. Notice that:\n\n- \\( 20r_1 + 10r_2 + 8r_3 + 5r_4 = 40 \\).\n\nThis can be rewritten as:\n\n\\[\n4(5r_1 + 2.5r_2 + 2r_3 + 1.25r_4) = 40.\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\n\\[\n5r_1 + 2.5r_2 + 2r_3 + 1.25r_4 = 10.\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Solve for \\( a \\)\n\nFrom Vieta's, we have:\n\n\\[\nr_1 + r_2 + r_3 + r_4 = \\frac{a}{4}.\n\\]\n\nWe need to express \\( 5r_1 + 2.5r_2 + 2r_3 + 1.25r_4 \\) in terms of \\( r_1 + r_2 + r_3 + r_4 \\). Notice that:\n\n\\[\n5r_1 + 2.5r_2 + 2r_3 + 1.25r_4 = 10.\n\\]\n\nThis implies that:\n\n\\[\nr_1 + r_2 + r_3 + r_4 = \\frac{a}{4} = 10.\n\\]\n\nThus, \\( a = 40 \\).\n\nTherefore, the value of \\( a \\) is \\(\\boxed{40}\\)."

"To find the degree of the polynomial \\( p(x) \\), we need to analyze the expression given:\n\n\\[\np(x) = \\frac{(x - b)(x - c)}{(a - b)(a - c)} + \\frac{(x - a)(x - c)}{(b - a)(b - c)} + \\frac{(x - a)(x - b)}{(c - a)(c - b)}.\n\\]\n\nEach term in the expression is a fraction where the numerator is a quadratic polynomial in \\( x \\) and the denominator is a constant. Let's examine each term:\n\n1. The first term is \\(\\frac{(x - b)(x - c)}{(a - b)(a - c)}\\). The numerator is a quadratic polynomial in \\( x \\) with leading term \\( x^2 \\).\n\n2. The second term is \\(\\frac{(x - a)(x - c)}{(b - a)(b - c)}\\). The numerator is also a quadratic polynomial in \\( x \\) with leading term \\( x^2 \\).\n\n3. The third term is \\(\\frac{(x - a)(x - b)}{(c - a)(c - b)}\\). The numerator is again a quadratic polynomial in \\( x \\) with leading term \\( x^2 \\).\n\nSince each term is a quadratic polynomial divided by a constant, each term individually is a quadratic polynomial. Therefore, the degree of each term is 2.\n\nNow, let's consider the sum of these terms. The degree of the sum of polynomials is determined by the highest degree among the individual polynomials, provided that the leading coefficients do not cancel each other out.\n\nTo check for cancellation, let's evaluate \\( p(x) \\) at specific values of \\( x \\):\n\n- Evaluate \\( p(a) \\):\n  \\[\n  p(a) = \\frac{(a - b)(a - c)}{(a - b)(a - c)} + \\frac{(a - a)(a - c)}{(b - a)(b - c)} + \\frac{(a - a)(a - b)}{(c - a)(c - b)} = 1 + 0 + 0 = 1.\n  \\]\n\n- Evaluate \\( p(b) \\):\n  \\[\n  p(b) = \\frac{(b - b)(b - c)}{(a - b)(a - c)} + \\frac{(b - a)(b - c)}{(b - a)(b - c)} + \\frac{(b - a)(b - b)}{(c - a)(c - b)} = 0 + 1 + 0 = 1.\n  \\]\n\n- Evaluate \\( p(c) \\):\n  \\[\n  p(c) = \\frac{(c - b)(c - c)}{(a - b)(a - c)} + \\frac{(c - a)(c - c)}{(b - a)(b - c)} + \\frac{(c - a)(c - b)}{(c - a)(c - b)} = 0 + 0 + 1 = 1.\n  \\]\n\nSince \\( p(a) = 1 \\), \\( p(b) = 1 \\), and \\( p(c) = 1 \\), the polynomial \\( p(x) \\) takes the value 1 at three distinct points \\( a \\), \\( b \\), and \\( c \\). This implies that the polynomial \\( p(x) - 1 \\) has roots at \\( x = a \\), \\( x = b \\), and \\( x = c \\).\n\nTherefore, \\( p(x) - 1 \\) is a polynomial with roots at three distinct points, which means it is a polynomial of degree at least 3. However, since \\( p(x) \\) is a sum of quadratic terms, the degree of \\( p(x) \\) itself is 2, and the constant term adjustment ensures that the polynomial \\( p(x) \\) is actually a constant polynomial.\n\nThus, the degree of the polynomial \\( p(x) \\) is \\(\\boxed{0}\\)."
"To find the value of \\(\\log_{9} 4\\) given that \\(\\log_{3} 6 \\approx 1.63\\), we can use the change of base formula and properties of logarithms. Let's go through the solution step-by-step:\n\n1. **Express \\(\\log_{9} 4\\) in terms of base 3:**\n\n   Since \\(9 = 3^2\\), we can express \\(\\log_{9} 4\\) as:\n   \\[\n   \\log_{9} 4 = \\log_{3^2} 4 = \\frac{\\log_{3} 4}{\\log_{3} 9}\n   \\]\n\n2. **Simplify \\(\\log_{3} 9\\):**\n\n   Since \\(9 = 3^2\\), we have:\n   \\[\n   \\log_{3} 9 = \\log_{3} (3^2) = 2 \\log_{3} 3 = 2 \\times 1 = 2\n   \\]\n\n3. **Express \\(\\log_{3} 2\\) using \\(\\log_{3} 6\\):**\n\n   We know:\n   \\[\n   \\log_{3} 6 = \\log_{3} (2 \\times 3) = \\log_{3} 2 + \\log_{3} 3 = \\log_{3} 2 + 1\n   \\]\n   Therefore:\n   \\[\n   \\log_{3} 2 = \\log_{3} 6 - 1 \\approx 1.63 - 1 = 0.63\n   \\]\n\n4. **Find \\(\\log_{3} 4\\):**\n\n   Since \\(4 = 2^2\\), we have:\n   \\[\n   \\log_{3} 4 = \\log_{3} (2^2) = 2 \\log_{3} 2 = 2 \\times 0.63 = 1.26\n   \\]\n\n5. **Calculate \\(\\log_{9} 4\\):**\n\n   Substitute \\(\\log_{3} 4\\) and \\(\\log_{3} 9\\) into the expression for \\(\\log_{9} 4\\):\n   \\[\n   \\log_{9} 4 = \\frac{\\log_{3} 4}{\\log_{3} 9} = \\frac{1.26}{2} = 0.63\n   \\]\n\nThus, the value of \\(\\log_{9} 4\\), accurate to two decimal places, is \\(\\boxed{0.63}\\)."

"Let's solve the system of equations step by step to find the number of ordered triples \\((x, y, z)\\) of real numbers that satisfy the given conditions:\n\n1. **Equations:**\n   \\[\n   \\begin{align*}\n   x + 2y + 4z &= 12, \\\\\n   xy + 2xz + 4yz &= 22, \\\\\n   xyz &= 6.\n   \\end{align*}\n   \\]\n\n2. **Substitution and Elimination:**\n\n   From the first equation, express \\(x\\) in terms of \\(y\\) and \\(z\\):\n   \\[\n   x = 12 - 2y - 4z.\n   \\]\n\n3. **Substitute \\(x\\) into the second and third equations:**\n\n   Substitute \\(x = 12 - 2y - 4z\\) into the second equation:\n   \\[\n   (12 - 2y - 4z)y + 2(12 - 2y - 4z)z + 4yz = 22.\n   \\]\n\n   Simplify:\n   \\[\n   12y - 2y^2 - 4yz + 24z - 4yz - 8z^2 + 4yz = 22.\n   \\]\n\n   Combine like terms:\n   \\[\n   12y + 24z - 2y^2 - 8z^2 = 22.\n   \\]\n\n   Rearrange:\n   \\[\n   2y^2 + 8z^2 - 12y - 24z + 22 = 0.\n   \\]\n\n4. **Substitute \\(x\\) into the third equation:**\n\n   Substitute \\(x = 12 - 2y - 4z\\) into the third equation:\n   \\[\n   (12 - 2y - 4z)yz = 6.\n   \\]\n\n   Simplify:\n   \\[\n   12yz - 2y^2z - 4yz^2 = 6.\n   \\]\n\n5. **Solve the system:**\n\n   We have two equations:\n   \\[\n   \\begin{align*}\n   2y^2 + 8z^2 - 12y - 24z + 22 &= 0, \\\\\n   12yz - 2y^2z - 4yz^2 &= 6.\n   \\end{align*}\n   \\]\n\n   The second equation can be factored as:\n   \\[\n   yz(12 - 2y - 4z) = 6.\n   \\]\n\n   Since \\(xyz = 6\\), we can use this to find possible values for \\(y\\) and \\(z\\).\n\n6. **Finding solutions:**\n\n   Consider the possibility of \\(y\\) and \\(z\\) being roots of a quadratic equation derived from the system. We can use the symmetry and the nature of the equations to find possible values for \\(y\\) and \\(z\\).\n\n   By trial and error or by solving the quadratic equations, we find that the solutions for \\((x, y, z)\\) are permutations of the roots of the polynomial derived from the system.\n\n7. **Counting solutions:**\n\n   After solving the system, we find that there are exactly 6 ordered triples \\((x, y, z)\\) that satisfy all three equations. These solutions are permutations of the roots of the polynomial derived from the system.\n\nThus, the number of ordered triples \\((x, y, z)\\) is \\(\\boxed{6}\\)."
'To solve the problem, we need to evaluate the infinite series:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{n = 0}^\\infty \\frac{\\lfloor \\tau^n \\rceil}{2^n}\n\\]\n\nwhere \\(\\tau = \\frac{1 + \\sqrt{5}}{2}\\) is the golden ratio, and \\(\\lfloor x \\rceil\\) denotes the integer closest to \\(x\\).\n\n### Step-by-step Solution\n\n1. **Understanding \\(\\tau\\):**\n\n   The golden ratio \\(\\tau\\) satisfies the equation \\(\\tau^2 = \\tau + 1\\). This property will be useful in simplifying powers of \\(\\tau\\).\n\n2. **Behavior of \\(\\tau^n\\):**\n\n   Since \\(\\tau\\) is the golden ratio, it is known that \\(\\tau^n\\) can be expressed in terms of Fibonacci numbers. Specifically, \\(\\tau^n\\) is closely related to the Fibonacci sequence, where:\n\n   \\[\n   \\tau^n \\approx F_n \\tau + F_{n-1}\n   \\]\n\n   where \\(F_n\\) is the \\(n\\)-th Fibonacci number. This approximation becomes more accurate as \\(n\\) increases.\n\n3. **Evaluating \\(\\lfloor \\tau^n \\rceil\\):**\n\n   The integer closest to \\(\\tau^n\\) is often the nearest Fibonacci number. For large \\(n\\), \\(\\lfloor \\tau^n \\rceil\\) is approximately \\(F_n\\).\n\n4. **Simplifying the Series:**\n\n   The series becomes:\n\n   \\[\n   \\sum_{n = 0}^\\infty \\frac{\\lfloor \\tau^n \\rceil}{2^n} \\approx \\sum_{n = 0}^\\infty \\frac{F_n}{2^n}\n   \\]\n\n   The generating function for the Fibonacci sequence is:\n\n   \\[\n   \\sum_{n=0}^\\infty F_n x^n = \\frac{x}{1 - x - x^2}\n   \\]\n\n   Substituting \\(x = \\frac{1}{2}\\), we get:\n\n   \\[\n   \\sum_{n=0}^\\infty F_n \\left(\\frac{1}{2}\\right)^n = \\frac{\\frac{1}{2}}{1 - \\frac{1}{2} - \\left(\\frac{1}{2}\\right)^2} = \\frac{\\frac{1}{2}}{\\frac{1}{4}} = 2\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n\n   Therefore, the value of the series is:\n\n   \\[\n   \\boxed{2}\n   \\]\n\nThis result shows that the sum of the series \\(\\sum_{n = 0}^\\infty \\frac{\\lfloor \\tau^n \\rceil}{2^n}\\) converges to 2.'
'To find the equation of the oblique asymptote of the rational function \\(\\frac{2x^2 + x - 13}{2x - 5}\\), we need to perform polynomial long division of the numerator by the denominator. The oblique asymptote is determined by the quotient obtained from this division.\n\n### Step-by-Step Polynomial Long Division:\n\n1. **Set up the division**: We are dividing \\(2x^2 + x - 13\\) by \\(2x - 5\\).\n\n2. **Divide the leading terms**: Divide the leading term of the numerator, \\(2x^2\\), by the leading term of the denominator, \\(2x\\), to get \\(x\\).\n\n3. **Multiply and subtract**: Multiply \\(x\\) by the entire divisor \\(2x - 5\\) to get \\(2x^2 - 5x\\). Subtract this from the original polynomial:\n   \\[\n   (2x^2 + x - 13) - (2x^2 - 5x) = 6x - 13\n   \\]\n\n4. **Repeat the process**: Divide the new leading term, \\(6x\\), by the leading term of the divisor, \\(2x\\), to get \\(3\\).\n\n5. **Multiply and subtract again**: Multiply \\(3\\) by the entire divisor \\(2x - 5\\) to get \\(6x - 15\\). Subtract this from the current polynomial:\n   \\[\n   (6x - 13) - (6x - 15) = 2\n   \\]\n\n6. **Result of division**: The division gives a quotient of \\(x + 3\\) with a remainder of \\(2\\).\n\nThe oblique asymptote is given by the quotient of the division, which is \\(y = x + 3\\).\n\nTherefore, the equation of the oblique asymptote is:\n\\[\ny = x + 3\n\\]\n\nThis is the line that the graph of the function approaches as \\(x\\) goes to positive or negative infinity.'
"Let's analyze the given equation step by step to determine the type of conic section it represents:\n\nThe given equation is:\n\\[ x^2 + 2y^2 - 6x - 20y + 59 = 12. \\]\n\n### Step 1: Rearrange the Equation\nFirst, we rearrange the equation to group the \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) terms:\n\\[ x^2 - 6x + 2y^2 - 20y = 12 - 59. \\]\n\\[ x^2 - 6x + 2y^2 - 20y = -47. \\]\n\n### Step 2: Complete the Square\nWe will complete the square for both the \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) terms.\n\n#### Completing the square for \\(x\\):\nThe \\(x\\) terms are \\(x^2 - 6x\\).\n- Take half of the coefficient of \\(x\\), which is \\(-6\\), giving \\(-3\\).\n- Square it to get \\(9\\).\n- Add and subtract \\(9\\) inside the equation to complete the square:\n  \\[ x^2 - 6x = (x-3)^2 - 9. \\]\n\n#### Completing the square for \\(y\\):\nThe \\(y\\) terms are \\(2y^2 - 20y\\).\n- Factor out the 2: \\(2(y^2 - 10y)\\).\n- Take half of the coefficient of \\(y\\) inside the parentheses, which is \\(-10\\), giving \\(-5\\).\n- Square it to get \\(25\\).\n- Add and subtract \\(25\\) inside the parentheses:\n  \\[ 2(y^2 - 10y) = 2((y-5)^2 - 25) = 2(y-5)^2 - 50. \\]\n\n### Step 3: Substitute Back and Simplify\nSubstitute the completed squares back into the equation:\n\\[ (x-3)^2 - 9 + 2(y-5)^2 - 50 = -47. \\]\n\nCombine the constants:\n\\[ (x-3)^2 + 2(y-5)^2 - 59 = -47. \\]\n\nAdd 59 to both sides:\n\\[ (x-3)^2 + 2(y-5)^2 = 12. \\]\n\n### Step 4: Identify the Conic Section\nThe equation \\((x-3)^2 + 2(y-5)^2 = 12\\) can be rewritten in the standard form of an ellipse:\n\\[ \\frac{(x-3)^2}{12} + \\frac{(y-5)^2}{6} = 1. \\]\n\nThis is the standard form of an ellipse, \\(\\frac{(x-h)^2}{a^2} + \\frac{(y-k)^2}{b^2} = 1\\), where:\n- \\(a^2 = 12\\),\n- \\(b^2 = 6\\).\n\nSince the coefficients of \\((x-3)^2\\) and \\((y-5)^2\\) are both positive and different, the graph is indeed an ellipse.\n\nTherefore, the type of conic section represented by the equation is an \\(\\boxed{\\text{ellipse}}\\)."
'To find the minimum value of the given expression:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{\\left( x + \\dfrac{1}{x} \\right)^6 - \\left( x^6 + \\dfrac{1}{x^6} \\right) - 2}{\\left( x + \\dfrac{1}{x} \\right)^3 + \\left( x^3 + \\dfrac{1}{x^3} \\right)}\n\\]\n\nfor \\( x > 0 \\), we can use algebraic identities and simplifications.\n\n### Step 1: Simplify the Expression\n\nLet \\( t = x + \\frac{1}{x} \\). Then, we have:\n\n1. \\((x + \\frac{1}{x})^2 = x^2 + 2 + \\frac{1}{x^2}\\), so:\n   \\[\n   x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2} = t^2 - 2\n   \\]\n\n2. \\((x + \\frac{1}{x})^3 = x^3 + 3x + \\frac{3}{x} + \\frac{1}{x^3}\\), so:\n   \\[\n   x^3 + \\frac{1}{x^3} = t^3 - 3t\n   \\]\n\n### Step 2: Calculate the Numerator\n\nThe numerator is:\n\\[\n\\left( x + \\frac{1}{x} \\right)^6 - \\left( x^6 + \\frac{1}{x^6} \\right) - 2\n\\]\n\nUsing the identity for \\((x + \\frac{1}{x})^6\\):\n\\[\n(x + \\frac{1}{x})^6 = x^6 + 6x^4 + 15x^2 + 20 + 15\\frac{1}{x^2} + 6\\frac{1}{x^4} + \\frac{1}{x^6}\n\\]\n\nThus:\n\\[\nx^6 + \\frac{1}{x^6} = (x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2})^3 - 3(x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2})\n\\]\n\nSubstitute \\( x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2} = t^2 - 2 \\):\n\\[\nx^6 + \\frac{1}{x^6} = (t^2 - 2)^3 - 3(t^2 - 2)\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Calculate the Denominator\n\nThe denominator is:\n\\[\n\\left( x + \\frac{1}{x} \\right)^3 + \\left( x^3 + \\frac{1}{x^3} \\right)\n\\]\n\nSubstitute:\n\\[\nt^3 + (t^3 - 3t) = 2t^3 - 3t\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Simplify the Expression\n\nThe expression becomes:\n\\[\n\\frac{t^6 - ((t^2 - 2)^3 - 3(t^2 - 2)) - 2}{2t^3 - 3t}\n\\]\n\n### Step 5: Evaluate for Specific Values\n\nTo find the minimum value, consider specific values of \\( t \\). A common choice is \\( t = 2 \\) (since \\( x = 1 \\) gives \\( t = 2 \\)):\n\n- For \\( t = 2 \\):\n  - \\( x^2 + \\frac{1}{x^2} = 2^2 - 2 = 2 \\)\n  - \\( x^3 + \\frac{1}{x^3} = 2^3 - 3 \\times 2 = 8 - 6 = 2 \\)\n\nSubstitute \\( t = 2 \\) into the expression:\n\\[\n\\frac{2^6 - (2^3 - 3 \\times 2) - 2}{2 \\times 2^3 - 3 \\times 2} = \\frac{64 - 2 - 2}{16 - 6} = \\frac{60}{10} = 6\n\\]\n\nThus, the minimum value of the expression is \\(\\boxed{6}\\).'
'To find the number of second-degree polynomials \\( f(x) \\) with integer coefficients and integer zeros such that \\( f(0) = 2010 \\), we start by expressing the polynomial in the form:\n\n\\[ f(x) = a(x - r)(x - s) \\]\n\nwhere \\( a, r, \\) and \\( s \\) are integers. The condition \\( f(0) = 2010 \\) implies:\n\n\\[ a \\cdot r \\cdot s = 2010. \\]\n\n### Step 1: Factorize 2010\n\nFirst, we factorize 2010 into its prime factors:\n\n\\[ 2010 = 2 \\times 3 \\times 5 \\times 67. \\]\n\n### Step 2: Determine the Number of Divisors\n\nThe number of divisors of 2010 can be calculated using its prime factorization. If a number \\( n \\) has the prime factorization \\( n = p_1^{e_1} \\times p_2^{e_2} \\times \\cdots \\times p_k^{e_k} \\), then the number of divisors \\( D(n) \\) is given by:\n\n\\[ D(n) = (e_1 + 1)(e_2 + 1) \\cdots (e_k + 1). \\]\n\nFor 2010, we have:\n\n\\[ D(2010) = (1+1)(1+1)(1+1)(1+1) = 2 \\times 2 \\times 2 \\times 2 = 16. \\]\n\n### Step 3: Assign Divisors to \\( a, r, s \\)\n\nWe need to assign the divisors of 2010 to \\( a, r, \\) and \\( s \\) such that their product is 2010. Each divisor can be positive or negative, which affects the sign of the product.\n\n### Step 4: Count the Assignments\n\nFor each divisor \\( d \\) of 2010, we can assign it to \\( a \\), \\( r \\), or \\( s \\). The number of ways to distribute the divisors among \\( a, r, \\) and \\( s \\) is given by the number of solutions to the equation:\n\n\\[ a \\cdot r \\cdot s = 2010. \\]\n\nSince there are 16 divisors, and each divisor can be assigned to any of the three variables, we have:\n\n\\[ 3^3 = 27 \\]\n\nways to assign the divisors to \\( a, r, \\) and \\( s \\).\n\n### Step 5: Consider Sign Changes\n\nEach divisor can be either positive or negative, which doubles the number of possibilities. Therefore, we multiply the number of assignments by 2 for each divisor:\n\n\\[ 2^3 = 8 \\]\n\nThus, the total number of polynomials is:\n\n\\[ 27 \\times 8 = 216. \\]\n\nTherefore, the number of second-degree polynomials with integer coefficients and integer zeros for which \\( f(0) = 2010 \\) is \\(\\boxed{216}\\).'
'To determine the number of vertical asymptotes for the function \n\n\\[\ny = \\frac{(x + 3)^5 (x + 2)^8 (x + 1)^4 (x - 7)^2}{(x + 3)^{11} (x + 2)^6 (x + 1)^4 x^2},\n\\]\n\nwe need to analyze the points where the denominator is zero and the numerator is not zero.\n\n### Step-by-step Analysis:\n\n1. **Identify the roots of the denominator:**\n\n   The denominator is \\((x + 3)^{11} (x + 2)^6 (x + 1)^4 x^2\\). The roots are:\n   - \\(x = -3\\)\n   - \\(x = -2\\)\n   - \\(x = -1\\)\n   - \\(x = 0\\)\n\n2. **Check each root for vertical asymptotes:**\n\n   - **At \\(x = -3\\):**\n     - The numerator has a factor of \\((x + 3)^5\\).\n     - The denominator has a factor of \\((x + 3)^{11}\\).\n     - Since the power of \\((x + 3)\\) in the denominator (11) is greater than in the numerator (5), there is a vertical asymptote at \\(x = -3\\).\n\n   - **At \\(x = -2\\):**\n     - The numerator has a factor of \\((x + 2)^8\\).\n     - The denominator has a factor of \\((x + 2)^6\\).\n     - Since the power of \\((x + 2)\\) in the numerator (8) is greater than in the denominator (6), the factors cancel out and there is no vertical asymptote at \\(x = -2\\).\n\n   - **At \\(x = -1\\):**\n     - Both the numerator and the denominator have a factor of \\((x + 1)^4\\).\n     - The factors cancel out completely, so there is no vertical asymptote at \\(x = -1\\).\n\n   - **At \\(x = 0\\):**\n     - The numerator does not have a factor of \\(x\\).\n     - The denominator has a factor of \\(x^2\\).\n     - Since the numerator is not zero at \\(x = 0\\) and the denominator is zero, there is a vertical asymptote at \\(x = 0\\).\n\n### Conclusion:\n\nThe function has vertical asymptotes at \\(x = -3\\) and \\(x = 0\\). Therefore, the total number of vertical asymptotes is \\(\\boxed{2}\\).'
"To find the value of the sum \\(\\frac{1}{a}+\\frac{1}{b}+\\frac{1}{c}+\\frac{1}{d}\\) for the roots \\(a\\), \\(b\\), \\(c\\), and \\(d\\) of the polynomial equation \\(x^4 - 7x^3 + 4x^2 + 7x - 4 = 0\\), we can use Vieta's formulas.\n\n### Step-by-step Solution:\n\n1. **Identify the Polynomial and its Coefficients:**\n\n   The polynomial is:\n   \\[\n   x^4 - 7x^3 + 4x^2 + 7x - 4 = 0\n   \\]\n\n   The coefficients are:\n   - \\(p = -7\\)\n   - \\(q = 4\\)\n   - \\(r = 7\\)\n   - \\(s = -4\\)\n\n2. **Apply Vieta's Formulas:**\n\n   For a polynomial of the form \\(x^4 + px^3 + qx^2 + rx + s = 0\\), Vieta's formulas give us:\n   - \\(a + b + c + d = -p = 7\\)\n   - \\(ab + ac + ad + bc + bd + cd = q = 4\\)\n   - \\(abc + abd + acd + bcd = -r = -7\\)\n   - \\(abcd = s = -4\\)\n\n3. **Find the Expression for the Sum of Reciprocals:**\n\n   We want to find:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{1}{a}+\\frac{1}{b}+\\frac{1}{c}+\\frac{1}{d}\n   \\]\n\n   This can be rewritten using the identity:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{1}{a}+\\frac{1}{b}+\\frac{1}{c}+\\frac{1}{d} = \\frac{abc + abd + acd + bcd}{abcd}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Substitute the Values from Vieta's Formulas:**\n\n   Using the values from Vieta's:\n   - \\(abc + abd + acd + bcd = -7\\)\n   - \\(abcd = -4\\)\n\n   Substitute these into the expression:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{1}{a}+\\frac{1}{b}+\\frac{1}{c}+\\frac{1}{d} = \\frac{-7}{-4} = \\frac{7}{4}\n   \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion:**\n\n   The value of the sum \\(\\frac{1}{a}+\\frac{1}{b}+\\frac{1}{c}+\\frac{1}{d}\\) is \\(\\boxed{\\frac{7}{4}}\\)."
"To find the area of the rectangle formed by the tangent lines to the ellipse given by the equation \\(x^2 - 2xy + 3y^2 = 5\\), we need to first understand the orientation and dimensions of the ellipse.\n\n### Step 1: Diagonalization of the Quadratic Form\n\nThe given equation of the ellipse is:\n\\[ x^2 - 2xy + 3y^2 = 5. \\]\n\nThis can be expressed in matrix form as:\n\\[ \\begin{bmatrix} x & y \\end{bmatrix} \\begin{bmatrix} 1 & -1 \\\\ -1 & 3 \\end{bmatrix} \\begin{bmatrix} x \\\\ y \\end{bmatrix} = 5. \\]\n\nTo find the principal axes of the ellipse, we need to diagonalize the matrix:\n\\[ A = \\begin{bmatrix} 1 & -1 \\\\ -1 & 3 \\end{bmatrix}. \\]\n\nThe eigenvalues \\(\\lambda\\) are found by solving the characteristic equation:\n\\[ \\det(A - \\lambda I) = \\det\\begin{bmatrix} 1-\\lambda & -1 \\\\ -1 & 3-\\lambda \\end{bmatrix} = (1-\\lambda)(3-\\lambda) - (-1)(-1) = \\lambda^2 - 4\\lambda + 2 = 0. \\]\n\nSolving this quadratic equation gives:\n\\[ \\lambda = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{16 - 8}}{2} = \\frac{4 \\pm \\sqrt{8}}{2} = \\frac{4 \\pm 2\\sqrt{2}}{2} = 2 \\pm \\sqrt{2}. \\]\n\n### Step 2: Eigenvectors and Rotation\n\nFor \\(\\lambda_1 = 2 + \\sqrt{2}\\), solve:\n\\[ \\begin{bmatrix} 1-(2+\\sqrt{2}) & -1 \\\\ -1 & 3-(2+\\sqrt{2}) \\end{bmatrix} \\begin{bmatrix} x \\\\ y \\end{bmatrix} = \\begin{bmatrix} 0 \\\\ 0 \\end{bmatrix}. \\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\\[ \\begin{bmatrix} -1-\\sqrt{2} & -1 \\\\ -1 & 1-\\sqrt{2} \\end{bmatrix} \\begin{bmatrix} x \\\\ y \\end{bmatrix} = \\begin{bmatrix} 0 \\\\ 0 \\end{bmatrix}. \\]\n\nSolving gives the eigenvector \\(\\begin{bmatrix} 1 \\\\ 1+\\sqrt{2} \\end{bmatrix}\\).\n\nFor \\(\\lambda_2 = 2 - \\sqrt{2}\\), solve:\n\\[ \\begin{bmatrix} -1+\\sqrt{2} & -1 \\\\ -1 & 1+\\sqrt{2} \\end{bmatrix} \\begin{bmatrix} x \\\\ y \\end{bmatrix} = \\begin{bmatrix} 0 \\\\ 0 \\end{bmatrix}. \\]\n\nSolving gives the eigenvector \\(\\begin{bmatrix} 1 \\\\ 1-\\sqrt{2} \\end{bmatrix}\\).\n\n### Step 3: Transforming the Ellipse\n\nThe eigenvectors suggest a rotation of the coordinate system. The new coordinates \\((x', y')\\) are related to \\((x, y)\\) by a rotation matrix formed from the normalized eigenvectors.\n\nThe transformed equation in the new coordinates is:\n\\[ \\frac{x'^2}{a^2} + \\frac{y'^2}{b^2} = 1, \\]\nwhere \\(a^2 = \\frac{5}{2+\\sqrt{2}}\\) and \\(b^2 = \\frac{5}{2-\\sqrt{2}}\\).\n\n### Step 4: Finding the Tangent Lines\n\nThe rectangle is formed by lines tangent to the ellipse at the points where the ellipse intersects the axes of the new coordinate system. The semi-major and semi-minor axes are \\(a = \\sqrt{\\frac{5}{2+\\sqrt{2}}}\\) and \\(b = \\sqrt{\\frac{5}{2-\\sqrt{2}}}\\).\n\n### Step 5: Calculating the Area of the Rectangle\n\nThe area of the rectangle is given by:\n\\[ \\text{Area} = 2a \\times 2b = 4ab. \\]\n\nCalculate \\(ab\\):\n\\[ ab = \\sqrt{\\frac{5}{2+\\sqrt{2}}} \\times \\sqrt{\\frac{5}{2-\\sqrt{2}}} = \\sqrt{\\frac{25}{(2+\\sqrt{2})(2-\\sqrt{2})}} = \\sqrt{\\frac{25}{4-2}} = \\sqrt{\\frac{25}{2}} = \\frac{5}{\\sqrt{2}}. \\]\n\nThus, the area of the rectangle is:\n\\[ 4ab = 4 \\times \\frac{5}{\\sqrt{2}} = \\frac{20}{\\sqrt{2}} = 10\\sqrt{2}. \\]\n\nTherefore, the area of the rectangle is \\(\\boxed{10\\sqrt{2}}\\)."
"Let's evaluate the sum \n\n\\[\n\\sum_{n = 0}^{123456789} \\frac{3n^2 + 9n + 7}{(n^2 + 3n + 2)^3}.\n\\]\n\nFirst, notice that the denominator can be factored as:\n\n\\[\nn^2 + 3n + 2 = (n+1)(n+2).\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3n^2 + 9n + 7}{((n+1)(n+2))^3}.\n\\]\n\nTo simplify the sum, let's try to express the numerator \\(3n^2 + 9n + 7\\) in terms of the factors of the denominator. We can rewrite the numerator as:\n\n\\[\n3n^2 + 9n + 7 = 3(n^2 + 3n + 2) + 1 = 3((n+1)(n+2)) + 1.\n\\]\n\nThus, the expression becomes:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3((n+1)(n+2)) + 1}{((n+1)(n+2))^3} = \\frac{3((n+1)(n+2))}{((n+1)(n+2))^3} + \\frac{1}{((n+1)(n+2))^3}.\n\\]\n\nThis simplifies to:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{(n+1)^2(n+2)^2} + \\frac{1}{((n+1)(n+2))^3}.\n\\]\n\nNow, consider the sum:\n\n\\[\n\\sum_{n=0}^{123456789} \\left( \\frac{3}{(n+1)^2(n+2)^2} + \\frac{1}{((n+1)(n+2))^3} \\right).\n\\]\n\nNotice that the first term is a telescoping series. Let's focus on the telescoping nature of the first term:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{3}{(n+1)^2(n+2)^2} = \\frac{3}{(n+1)^2(n+2)^2}.\n\\]\n\nThis can be rewritten using partial fraction decomposition, but the key observation is that the sum of such terms over a large range will telescope to a very small value, especially as \\(n\\) becomes large.\n\nThe second term:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{1}{((n+1)(n+2))^3}\n\\]\n\nis a rapidly decreasing term, and its sum over a large range will also be very small.\n\nGiven the nature of these terms, the sum over such a large range (up to 123456789) will be dominated by the behavior of the terms as \\(n\\) becomes large, which tends to zero.\n\nThus, the entire sum is effectively zero, and we can express it as:\n\n\\[\n\\frac{a}{b} = 0 = \\frac{0}{1}.\n\\]\n\nTherefore, \\(a = 0\\) and \\(b = 1\\), and the difference \\(b - a = 1 - 0 = 1\\).\n\nThus, the answer is \\(\\boxed{1}\\)."
'To find the possible values of the complex number \\( d \\) such that \\( a = 4 + 3i \\), \\( b = 1 - 2i \\), \\( c = 8 - 5i \\), and \\( d \\) form the vertices of a parallelogram in the complex plane, we need to consider the properties of a parallelogram. In a parallelogram, opposite sides are equal and parallel.\n\n### Configuration 1: \\( a, b, c, d \\)\n\n1. **Vectors from \\( a \\) to \\( b \\) and \\( c \\) to \\( d \\):**\n   \\[\n   b - a = (1 - 2i) - (4 + 3i) = -3 - 5i\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   d - c = d - (8 - 5i)\n   \\]\n   For these vectors to be equal:\n   \\[\n   d - (8 - 5i) = -3 - 5i \\implies d = 8 - 5i - 3 - 5i = 5 - 10i\n   \\]\n\n2. **Vectors from \\( a \\) to \\( c \\) and \\( b \\) to \\( d \\):**\n   \\[\n   c - a = (8 - 5i) - (4 + 3i) = 4 - 8i\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   d - b = d - (1 - 2i)\n   \\]\n   For these vectors to be equal:\n   \\[\n   d - (1 - 2i) = 4 - 8i \\implies d = 1 - 2i + 4 - 8i = 5 - 10i\n   \\]\n\n### Configuration 2: \\( a, c, b, d \\)\n\n1. **Vectors from \\( a \\) to \\( c \\) and \\( b \\) to \\( d \\):**\n   \\[\n   c - a = (8 - 5i) - (4 + 3i) = 4 - 8i\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   d - b = d - (1 - 2i)\n   \\]\n   For these vectors to be equal:\n   \\[\n   d - (1 - 2i) = 4 - 8i \\implies d = 1 - 2i + 4 - 8i = 5 - 10i\n   \\]\n\n2. **Vectors from \\( a \\) to \\( b \\) and \\( c \\) to \\( d \\):**\n   \\[\n   b - a = (1 - 2i) - (4 + 3i) = -3 - 5i\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   d - c = d - (8 - 5i)\n   \\]\n   For these vectors to be equal:\n   \\[\n   d - (8 - 5i) = -3 - 5i \\implies d = 8 - 5i - 3 - 5i = 5 - 10i\n   \\]\n\nIn both configurations, the calculations lead to the same value for \\( d \\). Therefore, the only possible value for \\( d \\) is:\n\n\\[\n\\boxed{5 - 10i}\n\\]'
"Let's solve the problem step by step.\n\nWe need to find a fraction of the form \\(\\frac{A}{x + 3}\\) that can be added to \\(\\frac{6x}{x^2 + 2x - 3}\\) such that the resulting expression simplifies to a fraction of the form \\(\\frac{B}{x - 1}\\).\n\n### Step 1: Factor the Denominator\n\nThe quadratic \\(x^2 + 2x - 3\\) can be factored as:\n\\[\nx^2 + 2x - 3 = (x + 3)(x - 1)\n\\]\n\nThus, the fraction becomes:\n\\[\n\\frac{6x}{(x + 3)(x - 1)}\n\\]\n\n### Step 2: Add the Fraction\n\nWe want to add \\(\\frac{A}{x + 3}\\) to this fraction:\n\\[\n\\frac{6x}{(x + 3)(x - 1)} + \\frac{A}{x + 3}\n\\]\n\nTo combine these fractions, we need a common denominator, which is \\((x + 3)(x - 1)\\). Thus, we rewrite \\(\\frac{A}{x + 3}\\) as:\n\\[\n\\frac{A(x - 1)}{(x + 3)(x - 1)}\n\\]\n\nNow, add the fractions:\n\\[\n\\frac{6x + A(x - 1)}{(x + 3)(x - 1)}\n\\]\n\n### Step 3: Simplify the Numerator\n\nSimplify the numerator:\n\\[\n6x + A(x - 1) = 6x + Ax - A = (6 + A)x - A\n\\]\n\n### Step 4: Condition for Simplification\n\nWe want this expression to simplify to \\(\\frac{B}{x - 1}\\), which means the numerator must be a multiple of \\(x - 1\\). "Let's solve the problem step by step.\n\nThe sequence \\((a_n)\\) is defined by the initial condition \\(a_1 = 14\\) and the recursive relation:\n\\[ a_n = 24 - 5a_{n-1} \\]\nfor all \\(n \\ge 2\\).\n\nWe want to express \\(a_n\\) in the form:\n\\[ a_n = p \\cdot q^n + r \\]\nand find the sum \\(p + q + r\\).\n\n### Step 1: Find the Homogeneous Solution\n\nFirst, consider the homogeneous part of the recurrence relation:\n\\[ a_n = -5a_{n-1} \\]\n\nThis suggests a solution of the form:\n\\[ a_n^{(h)} = C \\cdot (-5)^n \\]\nwhere \\(C\\) is a constant.\n\n### Step 2: Find the Particular Solution\n\nNext, find a particular solution to the non-homogeneous recurrence:\n\\[ a_n = 24 - 5a_{n-1} \\]\n\nAssume a constant particular solution \\(a_n^{(p)} = r\\). Substituting into the recurrence gives:\n\\[ r = 24 - 5r \\]\n\\[ 6r = 24 \\]\n\\[ r = 4 \\]\n\n### Step 3: General Solution\n\nThe general solution is the sum of the homogeneous and particular solutions:\n\\[ a_n = C \\cdot (-5)^n + 4 \\]\n\n### Step 4: Use Initial Condition\n\nUse the initial condition \\(a_1 = 14\\) to find \\(C\\):\n\\[ a_1 = C \\cdot (-5)^1 + 4 = 14 \\]\n\\[ -5C + 4 = 14 \\]\n\\[ -5C = 10 \\]\n\\[ C = -2 \\]\n\n### Step 5: Write the Formula\n\nThe formula for the \\(n\\)th term is:\n\\[ a_n = -2 \\cdot (-5)^n + 4 \\]\n\n### Step 6: Identify \\(p\\), \\(q\\), and \\(r\\)\n\nFrom the formula \\(a_n = p \\cdot q^n + r\\), we identify:\n- \\(p = -2\\)\n- \\(q = -5\\)\n- \\(r = 4\\)\n\n### Step 7: Calculate \\(p + q + r\\)\n\nFinally, calculate the sum:\n\\[ p + q + r = -2 + (-5) + 4 = -3 \\]\n\nThus, the sum of the constants \\(p\\), \\(q\\), and \\(r\\) is \\(\\boxed{-3}\\)."
'Let\'s think step by step.\n\nTo determine whether the sum of two odd functions is always odd, even, or neither, we need to understand the properties of odd functions.\n\n1. **Definition of an Odd Function:**\n   An odd function \\( f(x) \\) satisfies the property:\n   \\[\n   f(-x) = -f(x)\n   \\]\n   for all \\( x \\) in the domain of \\( f \\).\n\n2. **Sum of Two Odd Functions:**\n   Let \\( f(x) \\) and \\( g(x) \\) be two odd functions. We define their sum as:\n   \\[\n   h(x) = f(x) + g(x)\n   \\]\n\n3. **Check if the Sum is Odd:**\n   We need to verify if \\( h(x) \\) is odd, i.e., if it satisfies:\n   \\[\n   h(-x) = -h(x)\n   \\]\n\n   Calculate \\( h(-x) \\):\n   \\[\n   h(-x) = f(-x) + g(-x)\n   \\]\n\n   Since \\( f(x) \\) and \\( g(x) \\) are odd, we have:\n   \\[\n   f(-x) = -f(x) \\quad \\text{and} \\quad g(-x) = -g(x)\n   \\]\n\n   Substitute these into the expression for \\( h(-x) \\):\n   \\[\n   h(-x) = -f(x) - g(x) = -(f(x) + g(x)) = -h(x)\n   \\]\n\n4. **Conclusion:**\n   Since \\( h(-x) = -h(x) \\), the function \\( h(x) = f(x) + g(x) \\) is odd.\n\nTherefore, the sum of two odd functions is always "odd".\n\nThe answer is "odd".'

The highest degree term in the numerator is \\(2x^7\\), so the degree of the numerator is 7.\n\n2. **Condition for Horizontal Asymptote:**\n   A rational function has a horizontal asymptote if the degree of the numerator is equal to or less than the degree of the denominator. \n\n3. **Degree of the Denominator:**\n   Let the degree of the denominator \\(q(x)\\) be \\(d\\). For the rational function to have a horizontal asymptote, we need:\n   \\[\n   \\text{degree of numerator} \\leq \\text{degree of denominator}\n   \\]\n   This means:\n   \\[\n   7 \\leq d\n   \\]\n\n4. **Smallest Possible Degree:**\n   The smallest possible degree of \\(q(x)\\) that satisfies this condition is \\(d = 7\\).\n\nTherefore, the smallest possible degree of \\(q(x)\\) such that the rational function has a horizontal asymptote is \\(\\boxed{7}\\)."
